10083{_}14{_}XXXV.--"As IF IT WERE A MECCA"   XXXVI.--THE SURCHARGED MOMENT     BOOK ONE  SMOKE    I  THE HESITATING STEP  To have reared a towering scheme Of happiness, and to behold it razed, Were nothing: all men hope, and see their hopes Frustrate, and grieve awhile, and hope anew; But--  _A Blot in the 'Scutcheon._   The moon rode high; but ominous clouds were rushing towards it--clouds heavy with snow.
10083{_}15{_}I watched these clouds as I drove recklessly, desperately, over the winter roads.
10083{_}16{_}I had just missed the desire of my life, the one precious treasure which I coveted with my whole undisciplined heart, and not being what you call a man of self-restraint, I was chafed by my defeat far beyond the bounds I have usually set for myself.
10083{_}17{_}The moon--with the wild skurry of clouds hastening to blot it out of sight--seemed to mirror the chaos threatening my better impulses; and, idly keeping it in view, I rode on, hardly conscious of my course till the rapid recurrence of several well-known landmarks warned me that I had taken the longest route home, and that in another moment I should be skirting the grounds of The Whispering Pines, our country clubhouse.
10083{_}18{_}_I_ had taken?
10083{_}19{_}Let me rather say, my horse; for he and I had traversed this road many times together, and he had no means of knowing that the season was over and the club-house closed.
10083{_}20{_}I did not think of it myself at the moment, and was recklessly questioning whether I should not drive in and end my disappointment in a wild carouse, when, the great stack of chimneys coming suddenly into view against the broad disk of the still unclouded moon, I perceived a thin trail of smoke soaring up from their midst and realised, with a shock, that there should be no such sign of life in a house I myself had closed, locked, and barred that very day.
10083{_}21{_}I was the president of the club and felt responsible.
10083{_}22{_}Pausing only long enough to make sure that I had yielded to no delusion, and that fire of some kind was burning on one of the club-house's deserted hearths, I turned in at the lower gateway.
10083{_}23{_}For reasons which I need not now state, there were no bells attached to my cutter and consequently my approach was noiseless.
10083{_}24{_}I was careful that it should be so, also careful to stop short of the front door and leave my horse and sleigh in the black depths of the pine-grove pressing up to the walls on either side.
10083{_}25{_}I was sure that all was not as it should be inside these walls, but, as God lives, I had no idea what was amiss or how deeply my own destiny was involved in the step I was about to take.
10083{_}26{_}Our club-house stands, as it may be necessary to remind you, on a knoll thickly wooded with the ancient trees I have mentioned.
10083{_}27{_}These trees--all pines and of a growth unusual and of an aspect well-nigh hoary--extend only to the rear end of the house, where a wide stretch of gently undulating ground opens at once upon the eye, suggesting to all lovers of golf the admirable use to which it is put from early spring to latest fall.
10083{_}28{_}Now, links, as well as parterres and driveways, are lying under an even blanket of winter snow, and even the building, with its picturesque gables and rows of be-diamonded windows, is well-nigh indistinguishable in the shadows cast by the heavy pines, which soar above it and twist their limbs over its roof and about its forsaken corners, with a moan and a whisper always desolate to the sensitive ear, but from this night on, simply appalling.
10083{_}29{_}No other building stood within a half-mile in any direction.
10083{_}30{_}It was veritably a country club, gay and full of life in the season, but isolated and lonesome beyond description after winter had set in and buried flower and leaf under a wide waste of untrodden snow.
10083{_}31{_}I felt this isolation as I stepped from the edge of the trees and prepared to cross the few feet of open space leading to the main door.
10083{_}32{_}The sudden darkness instantly enveloping me, as the clouds, whose advancing mass I had been watching, made their final rush upon the moon, added its physical shock to this inner sense of desolation, and, in some moods, I should have paused and thought twice before attempting the door, behind which lurked the unknown with its naturally accompanying suggestion of peril.
10083{_}33{_}But rage and disappointment, working hotly within me, had left no space for fear.
10083{_}34{_}Rather rejoicing in the doubtfulness of the adventure, I pushed my way over the snow until my feet struck the steps.
10083{_}35{_}Here, instinct caused me to stop and glance quickly up and down the building either way.
10083{_}36{_}Not a gleam of light met my eye from the smallest scintillating pane.
10083{_}37{_}Was the house as soundless as it was dark?
10083{_}38{_}I listened but heard nothing.
10083{_}39{_}I listened again and still heard nothing.
10083{_}40{_}Then I proceeded boldly up the steps and laid my hand on the door.
10083{_}41{_}It was unlatched and yielded to my touch.
10083{_}42{_}Light or no light, sound or no sound there was some one within.
10083{_}43{_}The fire which had sent its attenuated streak of smoke up into the moonlit air, was burning yet on one of the many hearths within, and before it I should presently see--  Whom?
10083{_}44{_}What?
10083{_}45{_}The question scarcely interested me.
10083{_}46{_}Nevertheless I proceeded to enter and close the door carefully behind me.
10083{_}47{_}As I did so, I cast an involuntary glance without.
10083{_}48{_}The sky was inky and a few wandering flakes of the now rapidly advancing storm came whirling in, biting my cheeks and stinging my forehead.
10083{_}49{_}Once inside, I stopped short, possibly to listen again, possibly to assure myself as to what I had best do next.
10083{_}50{_}The silence was profound.
10083{_}51{_}Not a sound disturbed the great, empty building.
10083{_}52{_}My own footfall, as I stirred, seemed to wake extraordinary echoes.
10083{_}53{_}I had moved but a few steps, yet to my heightened senses, the noise seemed loud enough to wake the dead.
10083{_}54{_}Instinctively I stopped and stood stock-still.
10083{_}55{_}There was no answering cessation of movement.
10083{_}56{_}Darkness, silence everywhere.
10083{_}57{_}Yet not quite absolute darkness.
10083{_}58{_}As my eyes grew accustomed to the place, I found it possible to discern the outlines of the windows and locate the stairs and the arches where the side halls opened.
10083{_}59{_}I was even able to pick out the exact spot where the great antlers spread themselves above the hatrack, and presently the rack itself came into view, with its row of empty pegs, yesterday so full, to-day quite empty.
10083{_}60{_}That rack interested me,--I hardly knew why,--and regardless of the noise I made, I crossed over to it and ran my hand along the wall underneath.
10083{_}61{_}The result was startling.
10083{_}62{_}A man's coat and hat hung from one of the pegs.
10083{_}63{_}I knew my business as president of this club.
10083{_}64{_}I also knew that no one should be in the house at this time--that no one could be in it on any honest errand.
10083{_}65{_}Some secret and sinister business must be at the bottom of this mysterious intrusion immediately after the place had been shut for the winter.
10083{_}66{_}Would this hat and coat identify the intruder?
10083{_}67{_}I would strike a light and see.
10083{_}68{_}But this involved difficulties.
10083{_}69{_}The gas had been turned off that very morning and I had no matches in my pocket.
10083{_}70{_}But I remembered where they could be found.
10083{_}71{_}I had seen them when I passed through the kitchen earlier in the day.
10083{_}72{_}They were very accessible from the end of the hall where I stood.
10083{_}73{_}I had but to feel my way through a passage or two and I should come to the kitchen door.
10083{_}74{_}I began to move that way, and presently came creeping back, with a match-box half full of matches in my hand.
10083{_}75{_}But I did not strike one then.
10083{_}76{_}I had just made a move to do so, when the unmistakable sound of a door opening somewhere in the house made me draw back into as quiet and dark a place as I could find.
10083{_}77{_}This lay in the rear and at the right of the staircase, and as the sound had appeared to come from above, it was the most natural retreat that offered.
10083{_}78{_}And a good one I found it.
10083{_}79{_}I had hardly taken up my stand when the darkness above gave way to a faint glimmer, and a step became audible coming from some one of the many small rooms in the second story, but so slowly and with such evident hesitation that my imagination had ample time to work and fill my mind with varying anticipations, each more disconcerting than the last.
10083{_}80{_}Now I seemed to be listening to the movements of an intoxicated man seeking an issue out of strange quarters, then to the wary approach of one who had his own reasons for dread and was as conscious of my presence as I was of his.
10083{_}81{_}But the light, steadily increasing with each lagging but surely advancing step, soon gave the lie to this latter supposition, since no sane man, afraid of an ambush, would be likely to offer such odds to the one lying in wait for him, as his own face illumined by a flaming candle, and I was yielding to the bewilderment of the moment when the uncertain step paused and a sob came faintly to my ears, wrung from lips so stiff with human anguish that my fears took on new shape and the event a significance which in my present mood of personal suffering and preoccupation was anything but welcome.
10083{_}82{_}Indeed, I was coward enough to contemplate flight and might in another moment have yielded to the unworthy impulse if the sound of a second sigh had not struck shudderingly on my ear, followed by the renewal of the step and the almost immediate appearance on the stairs of a young girl holding a candle in one hand and shielding her left cheek with the other.
10083{_}83{_}Life offers few such shocks to any man, whatever his story or whatever his temperament.
10083{_}84{_}I had been prepared by the sob I had heard to see a woman, but not this woman.
10083{_}85{_}Nothing could have prepared me for an encounter with this woman anywhere that night, after what had passed between us and the wreck she had made of my life.
10083{_}86{_}But here!
10083{_}87{_}in a place so remote and desolate I had hesitated to enter it myself!
10083{_}88{_}What was I to think?
10083{_}89{_}How was I to reconcile so inconceivable a fact with what I knew of her in the past, with what I hoped from her in the future.
10083{_}90{_}To steady my thoughts and bring my whirling brain again under control, I fixed my eyes on her well-known form and features as upon a stranger's whom I would understand and judge.
10083{_}91{_}I have called her a woman and certainly I had loved her as such, but as, in this moment of strange detachment, I watched her descend, swaying foot following swaying foot falteringly down the stairs, I was able to see that only the emotions which denaturalised her expression were a woman's; that her features, her pose, and the peculiar childlike contour of the one cheek open to view were those of one whose yesterday was in the playroom.
10083{_}92{_}But beautiful!
10083{_}93{_}You do not often see such beauty.
10083{_}94{_}Under all the disfigurement of an agitation so great as to daunt me and make me question if I were its sole cause, her face shone with an individual charm which marked her out as one of the few who are the making or marring of men, sometimes of nations.
10083{_}95{_}This is the heritage she was born to, this her lot, not to be shirked, not to be evaded even now at her early age of seventeen.
10083{_}96{_}So much any one could see even in a momentary scrutiny of her face and figure.
10083{_}97{_}But what was not so clear, not even to myself with the consciousness of what had passed between us during the last few hours, was why her heart should have so outrun her years, and the emotion I beheld betray such shuddering depths.
10083{_}98{_}Some grisly fear, some staring horror had met her in this strange retreat.
10083{_}99{_}Simple grief speaks with a different language from that which I read in her distorted features and tottering, slowly creeping form.
10083{_}100{_}What had happened above?
10083{_}101{_}She had escaped me to run upon what?
10083{_}102{_}My lips refused to ask, my limbs refused to move, and if I breathed at all, I did so with such fierceness of restraint that her eyes never turned my way, not even when she had reached the lowest step and paused for a moment there, oscillating in pain or uncertainty.
10083{_}103{_}Her face was turned more fully towards me now, and I had just begun to discern something in it besides its tragic beauty, when she made a quick move and blew out the candle she held.
10083{_}104{_}One moment that magical picture of superhuman loveliness, then darkness, I might say silence, for I do not think either of us so much as stirred for several instants.
10083{_}105{_}Then there came a crash, followed by the sound of flying feet.
10083{_}106{_}She had flung the candlestick out of her hand and was hurriedly crossing the hail.
10083{_}107{_}I thought she was coming my way, and instinctively drew back against the wall.
10083{_}108{_}But she stopped far short of me, and I heard her groping about, then give a sudden spring towards the front door.
10083{_}109{_}It opened and the wind soughed in.
10083{_}110{_}I felt the chill of snow upon my face, and realised the tempest.
10083{_}111{_}Then all was quiet and dark again.
10083{_}112{_}She had slid quickly out and the door had swung to behind her.
10083{_}113{_}Another instant and I heard the click of the key as it turned in the lock, heard it and made no outcry, such the spell, such the bewilderment of my faculties!
10083{_}114{_}But once the act was accomplished and egress made difficult, nay, for the moment, impossible, I felt all lesser emotions give way to an anxiety which demanded immediate action, for the girl had gone out without wraps or covering for her head, and my experience of the evening had told me how cold it was.
10083{_}115{_}I must follow and find her and rescue her if possible from the snow.
10083{_}116{_}The distance was long to town, the cold would seize and perhaps prostrate her, after which, the wind and snow would do the rest.
10083{_}117{_}Throwing myself against the door, I shook it violently.
10083{_}118{_}It was immovable.
10083{_}119{_}Then I flew to the windows.
10083{_}120{_}Their fastenings yielded readily enough, but not the windows themselves; one had a broken cord, another seemed glued to its frame, and I was still struggling with the latter when I heard a sound which lifted the hair on my head and turned my whole attention back to what lay behind and above me.
10083{_}121{_}There was still some one in the house.
10083{_}122{_}I had forgotten everything in this apparition of the woman I have described in a place so disassociated with any conception I could possibly have of her whereabouts on this especial evening.
10083{_}123{_}But this noise, short, sharp, but too distant to be altogether recognisable, roused doubts which once awakened changed the whole tenor of my thoughts and would not let me rest till I had probed the house from top to bottom.
10083{_}124{_}To find Carmel Cumberland alone in this desolation was a mystifying discovery to which I had found it hard enough to reconcile myself.
10083{_}125{_}But Carmel here in company with another at the very moment when I had expected the fruition of my own joy,--ah, that was to open hell's door in my breast; a possibility too intolerable to remain unsettled for an instant.
10083{_}126{_}Though she had passed out before my eyes in a drooping, almost agonised condition, not she, dear as she was, and great as were my fears in her regard, was to be sought out first, but the man!
10083{_}127{_}The man who was back of all this, possibly back of my disappointment; the man whose work I may have witnessed, but at whose identity I could not even guess.
10083{_}128{_}Leaving the window, I groped my way along the wall until I reached the rack where the man's coat and hat hung.
10083{_}129{_}Whether it was my intention to carry them away and hide them, in my anxiety to secure this intruder and hold him to a bitter account for the misery he was causing me, or whether I only meant to satisfy myself that they were the habiliments of a stranger and not those of some sneaking member of the club, is of little importance in the light of the fact which presently burst upon me.
10083{_}130{_}The hat and coat were gone.
10083{_}131{_}Nothing hung from the rack.
10083{_}132{_}The wall was free from end to end.
10083{_}133{_}She had taken these articles of male apparel with her; she had not gone forth into the driving snow, unprotected, but--  I did not know what to think.
10083{_}134{_}No acquaintanceship with her girlish impulses, nothing that had occurred between us before or during this night, had prepared me for a freak of this nature.
10083{_}135{_}I felt backward along the wall; I felt forward; I even handled the pegs and counted them as I passed to and fro, touching every one; but I could not alter the fact.
10083{_}136{_}The groping she had done had been in this direction.
10083{_}137{_}She was searching for this hat and coat (a man's hat,--a derby, as I had been careful to assure myself at the first handling) and, in them, she had gone home as she had probably come, and there was no man in the case, or if there were--  The doubt drove me to the staircase.
10083{_}138{_}Making no further effort to unravel the puzzle which only beclouded my faculties, I began my wary ascent.
10083{_}139{_}I had not the slightest fear, I was too full of cold rage for that.
10083{_}140{_}The arrangement of rooms on the second floor was well known to me.
10083{_}141{_}I understood every nook and corner and could find my way about the whole place without a light.
10083{_}142{_}I took but one precaution--that of slipping off my shoes at the foot of the stairs.
10083{_}143{_}I wished to surprise the intruder.
10083{_}144{_}I was willing to resort to any expedient to accomplish this.
10083{_}145{_}The matches I carried in my pocket would make this possible if once I heard him breathing.
10083{_}146{_}I held my own breath as I stole softly up, and waited for an instant at the top of the stairs to listen.
10083{_}147{_}There was an awesome silence everywhere, and I was hesitating whether to attack the front rooms first or to follow up a certain narrow hall leading to a rear staircase, when I remembered the thin line of smoke which, rising from one of the chimneys, had first attracted my attention to the house.
10083{_}148{_}In that was my clue.
10083{_}149{_}There was but one room on this floor where a fire could be lit.
10083{_}150{_}It lay a few feet beyond me down the narrow hall I have just mentioned.
10083{_}151{_}Why had I trusted everything to my ears when my nose would have been a better guide?
10083{_}152{_}As I took the few steps necessary, a slight smell of smoke became very perceptible, and no longer in doubt of my course, I pushed boldly on and entering the half-open door, struck a match and peered anxiously about.
10083{_}153{_}Emptiness here just as everywhere else.
10083{_}154{_}A few chairs, a dresser,--it was a ladies' dressing-room,--some smouldering ashes on the hearth, a lounge piled up with cushions.
10083{_}155{_}But no person.
10083{_}156{_}The sound I had heard had not issued from this room, yet something withheld me from seeking further.
10083{_}157{_}Chilled to the bone, with teeth chattering in spite of myself, I paused just inside the door, and when the match went out in my hand remained shivering there in the darkness, a prey to sensations more nearly approaching those of fear than any I had ever before experienced in my whole life.
10083{_}158{_}II  IT WAS SHE--SHE INDEED!
10083{_}159{_}Look on death itself!--up, up, and see The great doom's visage!
10083{_}160{_}_Macbeth_.
10083{_}161{_}Why, I did not know.
10083{_}162{_}There seemed to be no reason for this excess of feeling.
10083{_}163{_}I had no dread of attack; my apprehension was of another sort.
10083{_}164{_}Besides, any attack here must come from the rear--from the open doorway in which I stood--and my dread lay before me, in the room itself, which, as I have already said, appeared to be totally empty.
10083{_}165{_}What could occasion my doubts, and why did I not fly the place?
10083{_}166{_}There were passage-ways yet to search, why linger here like a gaby in the dark when perhaps the man I believed to be in hiding somewhere within these walls, was improving the opportunity to escape?
10083{_}167{_}If I asked myself this question, I did not answer it, but I doubt if I asked it then.
10083{_}168{_}I had forgotten the intruder; the interest which had carried me thus far had become lost in a fresher one of which the beginning and ending lay hidden within the four walls I now stared upon, unseeing.
10083{_}169{_}Not to see and yet to feel--did that make the horror?
10083{_}170{_}If so, another lighted match must help me out.
10083{_}171{_}I struck one while the thought was hot within me, and again took a look at the room.
10083{_}172{_}I noted but one thing new, but that made me reel back till I was half way into the hall.
10083{_}173{_}Then a certain dogged persistency I possess came to my rescue, and I re-entered the room at a leap and stood before the lounge and its pile of cushions.
10083{_}174{_}They were numerous,--all that the room contained, and more!
10083{_}175{_}Chairs had been stripped, window-seats denuded, and the whole collection disposed here in a set way which struck me as unnatural.
10083{_}176{_}Was this the janitor's idea?
10083{_}177{_}I hardly thought so, and was about to pluck one of these cushions off, when that most unreasonable horror seized me again and I found myself looking back over my shoulder at the fireplace from which rose a fading streak of smoke which some passing gust, perhaps, had blown out into the room.
10083{_}178{_}I felt sick.
10083{_}179{_}Was it the smell?
10083{_}180{_}It was not that of burning wood, hardly of burning paper, I--but here my second match went out.
10083{_}181{_}Thoroughly roused now (you will say, by what?)
10083{_}182{_}I felt my way out of the room and to the head of the staircase.
10083{_}183{_}I remembered the candle and candlestick I had heard thrown down on the lower floor by Carmel Cumberland.
10083{_}184{_}I would secure them and come back and settle these uncanny doubts.
10083{_}185{_}It might be the veriest fool business, but my mind was disturbed and must be set at ease.
10083{_}186{_}Nothing else seemed so important, yet I was not without anxiety for the lovely and delicate woman wandering the snow-covered roads in the teeth of a furious gale, any more than I was dead to the fact that I should never forgive myself if I allowed the man to escape whom I believed to be hiding somewhere in the rear of this house.
10083{_}187{_}I had a hunt for the candlestick and a still longer one for the candle, but finally I recovered both, and, lighting the latter, felt myself, for the first time, more or less master of the situation.
10083{_}188{_}Rapidly regaining the room in which my interest was now centred, I set the candlestick down on the dresser, and approached the lounge.
10083{_}189{_}Hardly knowing what I feared, or what I expected to find, I tore off one of the cushions and flung it behind me.
10083{_}190{_}More cushions were revealed--but that was not all.
10083{_}191{_}Escaping from the edge of one of them I saw a shiny tress of woman's hair.
10083{_}192{_}I gave a gasp and pulled off more cushions, then I fell on my knees, struck down by the greatest horror which a man can feel.
10083{_}193{_}Death lay before me--violent, uncalled-for death--and the victim was a woman.
10083{_}194{_}But it was not that.
10083{_}195{_}Though the head was not yet revealed, I thought I knew the woman and that she--Did seconds pass or many minutes before I lifted that last cushion?
10083{_}196{_}I shall never know.
10083{_}197{_}It was an eternity to me and I am not of a sentimental cast, but I have some sort of a conscience and during that interval it awoke.
10083{_}198{_}It has never quite slept since.
10083{_}199{_}The cushion had not concealed the hands, but I did not look at them--I did not dare.
10083{_}200{_}I must first see the face.
10083{_}201{_}But I did not twitch this pillow off; I drew it aside slowly, as though held by the restraining clutch of some one behind me.
10083{_}202{_}And I was so held, but not by what was visible--rather by the terrors which gather in the soul at the summons of some dreadful doom.
10083{_}203{_}I could not meet the certainty without some preparation.
10083{_}204{_}I released another strand of hair; then the side of a cheek, half buried out of sight in the loosened locks and bulging pillows; then, with prayers to God for mercy, an icy brow; two staring eyes--which having seen I let the cushion drop, for mercy was not to be mine.
10083{_}205{_}It was _she_, she, indeed!
10083{_}206{_}and judgment was glassed in the look I met--judgment and nothing more kindly, however I might appeal to Heaven for mercy or whatever the need of my fiercely startled and repentant soul.
10083{_}207{_}Dead!
10083{_}208{_}Adelaide!
10083{_}209{_}the woman I had planned to wrong that very night, and who had thus wronged me!
10083{_}210{_}For a moment I could take in nothing but this one astounding fact, then the how and the why woke in maddening curiosity within me, and seizing the cushion, I dragged it aside and stared down into the pitiful and accusing features thus revealed, as though to tear from them the story of the crime which had released me as I would not have been released, no, not to have had my heart's desire in all the fulness with which I had contemplated it a few short hours before.
10083{_}211{_}But beyond the ever accusing, protuberant stare, those features told nothing; and steeling myself to the situation, I made what observation I could of her condition and the surrounding circumstances.
10083{_}212{_}For this was my betrothed wife.
10083{_}213{_}Whatever my intentions, however far my love had strayed under the spell cast over me by her sister,--the young girl who had just passed out,--Adelaide and I had been engaged for many months; our wedding day was even set.
10083{_}214{_}But that was all over now--ended as her life was ended: suddenly, incomprehensibly, and by no stroke of God.
10083{_}215{_}Even the jewel on her finger was gone, the token of our betrothal.
10083{_}216{_}This was to be expected.
10083{_}217{_}She would be apt to take it off before committing herself to a fate that proclaimed me a traitor to this symbol.
10083{_}218{_}I should see that ring again.
10083{_}219{_}I should find it in a letter filled with bitter words.
10083{_}220{_}I would not think of it or of them now.
10083{_}221{_}I would try to learn how she had committed this act, whether by poison or--  It must have been by poison; no other means would suggest themselves to one of her refined sense; but if so, why those marks on her neck, growing darker and darker as I stared at them!
10083{_}222{_}My senses reeled as I scrutinised those marks.
10083{_}223{_}Small, delicate but deadly, they stared upon me from either side of her white neck till nature could endure no more and I tottered back against the further wall, beholding no longer room, nor lounge, nor recumbent body, but a young girl's exquisite face, set in lines which belied her seventeen years, and made futile any attempt on my part at self-deception when my reason inexorably demanded an explanation of this death.
10083{_}224{_}As suicide it was comprehensible, as murder, not, unless--  And it had been murder!
10083{_}225{_}I sank to the floor as I fully realised this.
10083{_}226{_}III  "OPEN!"
10083{_}227{_}PRINCE.--Bring forth the parties of suspicion.
10083{_}228{_}FRIAR.--I am the greatest, as the time and place Doth make against me, of this direful murder; And here I stand, both to impeach and purge.
10083{_}229{_}Myself condemned and myself excused.
10083{_}230{_}_Romeo and Juliet_.
10083{_}231{_}I have mentioned poison as my first thought.
10083{_}232{_}It was a natural one, the result undoubtedly of having noticed two small cordial glasses standing on a little table over against the fireplace.
10083{_}233{_}When I was conscious again of my own fears, I crossed to the table and peered into these glasses.
10083{_}234{_}They were both empty.
10083{_}235{_}However, they had not been so long.
10083{_}236{_}In each I found traces of anisette cordial, and though no bottle stood near I was very confident that it could readily be found somewhere in the room.
10083{_}237{_}What had preceded and followed the drinking of this cordial?
10083{_}238{_}As I raised my head from bending over these glasses--not club glasses, by the way--I caught sight of my face in the mantel mirror.
10083{_}239{_}It gave me maddening thoughts.
10083{_}240{_}In this same mirror there had been reflected but a little while before, two other faces, for a sight of whose expression at that fatal moment I would gladly risk my soul.
10083{_}241{_}How had _she_ looked--how that other?
10083{_}242{_}Would not the story of those awful, those irrevocable moments be plain to my eye, if the quickly responsive glass could but retain the impressions it receives and give back at need what had once informed its surface with moving life!
10083{_}243{_}I stared at the senseless glass, appealed to it with unreasoning frenzy, as to something which could give up its secret if it would, but only to meet my own features in every guise of fury and despair--features I no longer knew--features which insensibly increased my horror till I tore myself wildly from the spot, and cast about for further clues to enlightenment, before yielding to the conviction which was making a turmoil in mind, heart, and conscience.
10083{_}244{_}Alas!
10083{_}245{_}there was but little more to see.
10083{_}246{_}A pair of curling-irons lay on the hearth, but I had no sooner lifted them than I dropped them with a shudder of unspeakable loathing, only to start at the noise they made in striking the tiles.
10083{_}247{_}For it was the self-same noise I had heard when listening from below.
10083{_}248{_}These tongs, set up against the side of the fireplace had been jarred down by the forcible shutting of the large front door, and no man other than myself was in the house, or had been in the house; only the two women.
10083{_}249{_}But the time when this discovery would have brought comfort was passed.
10083{_}250{_}Better a hundred times that a man--I had almost said any man--should have been with them here, than that they should be closeted together in a spot so secluded, with rancour and cause for complaint in one heart, and a biting, deadly flame in the other, which once reaching up must from its very nature leave behind it a corrosive impress.
10083{_}251{_}I saw,-I felt,--but I did not desist from my investigations.
10083{_}252{_}A stick or two still smouldered on the hearthstone.
10083{_}253{_}In the ashes lay some scattered fragments of paper which crumbled at my touch.
10083{_}254{_}On the floor in front I espied only a stray hair-pin; everything else was in place throughout the room except the cushions and that horror on the lounge, waiting the second look I had so far refrained from giving it.
10083{_}255{_}That look I could no longer withhold.
10083{_}256{_}I must know the depth of the gulf over which I hung.
10083{_}257{_}I must not wrong with a thought one who had smiled upon me like an angel of light--a young girl, too, with the dew of innocence on her beauty to every eye but mine and only not to mine within--shall I say ten awful minutes?
10083{_}258{_}It seemed ages,--all of my life and more.
10083{_}259{_}Yet that lovely breast had heaved not so many times since I looked upon her as a deified mortal, and now two small spots on another woman's pulseless throat had drawn a veil of blood over that beauty, and given to a child the attributes of a Medusa.
10083{_}260{_}Yet hope was not quite stilled.
10083{_}261{_}I would look again and perhaps discover that my own eyes had been at fault, that there were no marks, or if marks, not just the ones my fancy had painted there.
10083{_}262{_}Turning, I let my glance fall first on the feet.
10083{_}263{_}I had not noted them before, and I was startled to see that the arctics in which they were clad were filled all around with snow.
10083{_}264{_}She had walked then, as the other was walking now; she, who detested every effort and was of such delicate make that exertion of unusual kind could not readily be associated with her.
10083{_}265{_}Had she come alone or in Carmel's company, and if in Carmel's company, on what ostensible errand if not that of death?
10083{_}266{_}Her dress, which was of dark wool, showed that she had changed her garments for this trip.
10083{_}267{_}I had seen her at dinner, and this was not the gown she had worn then--the gown in which she had confronted me during those few intolerable minutes when I could not meet her eyes.
10083{_}268{_}Fatal cowardice!
10083{_}269{_}A moment of realisation then and we might all have been saved this horror of sin and death and shameful retribution.
10083{_}270{_}And yet who knows?
10083{_}271{_}Not understanding what I saw, how could I measure the might-have-beens!
10083{_}272{_}I would proceed with my task--note if she wore the diamond brooch I had given her.
10083{_}273{_}No, she was without ornament; I had never seen her so plainly clad.
10083{_}274{_}Might I draw a hope from this?
10083{_}275{_}Even the pins which had fallen from her hair were such as she wore when least adorned.
10083{_}276{_}Nothing spoke of the dinner party or of her having been dragged here unaware; but all of previous intent and premeditation.
10083{_}277{_}Surely hope was getting uppermost.
10083{_}278{_}If I had dreamed the marks--  But no!
10083{_}279{_}There they were, unmistakable and damning, just where the breath struggles up.
10083{_}280{_}I put my own thumbs on these two dark spots to see if--when what was it?
10083{_}281{_}A lightning stroke or a call of fate which one must answer while sense remains?
10083{_}282{_}I felt my head pulled around by some unseen force from behind, and met staring into mine through the glass of the window a pair of burning eyes.
10083{_}283{_}Or was it fantasy?
10083{_}284{_}For in another moment they were gone, nor was I in the condition just then to dissociate the real from the unreal.
10083{_}285{_}But the possibility of a person having seen me in this position before the dead was enough to startle me to my feet, and though in another instant I became convinced that I had been the victim of hallucination, I nevertheless made haste to cross to the window and take a look through its dismal panes.
10083{_}286{_}A gale of blinding snow was sweeping past, making all things indistinguishable, but the absence of balcony outside was reassuring and I stepped hastily back, asking myself for the first time what I should do and where I should now go to ensure myself from being called as a witness to the awful occurrence which had just taken place in this house.
10083{_}287{_}Should I go home and by some sort of subterfuge now unthought of, try to deceive my servants as to the time of my return, or attempt to create an alibi elsewhere?
10083{_}288{_}Something I must do to save myself the anguish and Carmel the danger of my testimony in this matter.
10083{_}289{_}She must never know, the world must never know that I had seen her here.
10083{_}290{_}I had lost at a blow everything that gives zest or meaning to life, but I might still be spared the bottommost depth of misery--be saved the utterance of the word which would sink that erring but delicate soul into the hell yawning beneath her.
10083{_}291{_}It was my one thought now--though I knew that the woman who had fallen victim to her childish hate had loved me deeply and was well worth my avenging.
10083{_}292{_}I could not be the death of two women; the loss of one weighed heavily enough upon my conscience.
10083{_}293{_}I would fly the place--I would leave this ghastly find to tell its own story.
10083{_}294{_}The night was stormy, the hour late, the spot a remote one, and the road to it but little used.
10083{_}295{_}I could easily escape and when the morrow came--but it was the present I must think of now, this hour, this moment.
10083{_}296{_}How came I to stay so long!
10083{_}297{_}In feverish haste, I began to throw the pillows back over the quiet limbs, the accusing face.
10083{_}298{_}Shudderingly I hid those eyes (I understood their strange protuberance now) and recklessly bent on flight, was half way across the floor when my feet were stayed--I wonder that my reason was not unseated--by a sudden and tremendous attack on the great door below, mingled with loud cries to open which ran thundering through the house, calling up innumerable echoes from its dead and hidden corners.
10083{_}299{_}It was the police.
10083{_}300{_}The wild night, the biting storm had been of no avail.
10083{_}301{_}An alarm had reached headquarters, and all hope of escape on my part was at an end.
10083{_}302{_}Yet because at such crises instinct rises superior to reason, I blew out the candle and softly made my way into the hall.
10083{_}303{_}I had remembered a window opening over a shed at the head of the kitchen staircase.
10083{_}304{_}I could reach it from this rear hall by just a turn or two, and once on that shed, a short leap would land me on the ground; after which I could easily trust to the storm to conceal my flight across the open golf-links.
10083{_}305{_}It was worth trying at least; anything was better than being found in the house with my murdered betrothed.
10083{_}306{_}I had no reason to think that I was being sought, or that my presence in this building was even suspected.
10083{_}307{_}It might well be that the police were even ignorant of the tragedy awaiting them across the threshold of the door they seemed intent on battering down.
10083{_}308{_}The gleam of a candle burning in this closed-up house, or even the tale told by the rising smoke, may have drawn them from the road to investigate.
10083{_}309{_}Such coincidences had been.
10083{_}310{_}Such untoward happenings had misled people into useless self-betrayal.
10083{_}311{_}My case was too desperate for such weakness.
10083{_}312{_}Flight at this moment might save all; I would at least attempt it.
10083{_}313{_}The door was shaking on its hinges; these intruders seemed determined to enter.
10083{_}314{_}With a spring I reached the window by which I hoped to escape, and quickly raised it.
10083{_}315{_}A torrent of snow swept in, covering my face and breast in a moment.
10083{_}316{_}It did something more: it cleared my brain, and I remembered my poor horse standing in this blinding gale under cover of the snow-packed pines.
10083{_}317{_}Every one knew my horse.
10083{_}318{_}I could commit no greater folly than to flee by the rear fields while such a witness to my presence remained in full view in front.
10083{_}319{_}With the sensation of a trapped animal, I reclosed the window and cast about for a safe corner where I could lie concealed until I learned what had brought these men here and how much I really had to fear from their presence.
10083{_}320{_}I had but little time in which to choose.
10083{_}321{_}The door below had just given way and a party of at least three men were already stamping their feet free from snow in the hall.
10083{_}322{_}I did not like the tone of their voices, it was too low and steady to suit me.
10083{_}323{_}I had rather have heard drunken cries or a burst of wild hilarity than these stern and purposeful whispers.
10083{_}324{_}Men of resolution could have but one errand here.
10083{_}325{_}My doom was closing round me.
10083{_}326{_}I could only put off the fatal moment.
10083{_}327{_}But it was better to do this than to plunge headlong into the unknown fate awaiting me.
10083{_}328{_}I knew of a possible place of concealment.
10083{_}329{_}It was in the ballroom not far from where I stood.
10083{_}330{_}I remembered the spot well.
10083{_}331{_}It was at the top of a little staircase leading to the musicians' gallery.
10083{_}332{_}A balustrade guarded this gallery, supported by a boarding wide enough to hide a man lying behind it at his full length.
10083{_}333{_}If the search I was endeavouring to evade was not minute enough to lead them to look behind this boarding, it would offer me the double advantage of concealment and an unobstructed view of what went on in the hall, through the main doorway opening directly opposite.
10083{_}334{_}I could reach this ballroom and its terminal gallery without going around to this door.
10083{_}335{_}A smaller one communicated directly with the corridor in which I was then lurking, and towards this I now made my way with all the precaution suggested by my desperate situation.
10083{_}336{_}No man ever moved more lightly.
10083{_}337{_}The shoes which I had taken off in the lower hall were yet in my hand.
10083{_}338{_}I had caught them up after replacing the cushions on Adelaide's body.
10083{_}339{_}Even to my own straining ears I made no perceptible sound.
10083{_}340{_}I reached the balcony and had stretched myself out at full length behind the boarding, before the men below had left the lower floor.
10083{_}341{_}An interval of heart-torture and wearing suspense now followed.
10083{_}342{_}They were ransacking the rooms below by the aid of their own lanterns, as I could tell from their assured manner.
10083{_}343{_}That they had not made at once for the scene of crime brought me some small sense of comfort, but not much.
10083{_}344{_}They were too resolute in their movements and much too thorough and methodical in their search, for me to dream of their confining their investigations to the first floor.
10083{_}345{_}Unless I very much mistook their purpose, I should soon hear them ascending the stairs, after which, instinct, if not the faint smell of smoke still lingering in the air, would lead them to the room where my poor Adelaide lay.
10083{_}346{_}And thus it proved.
10083{_}347{_}More quickly than I expected, the total darkness in which I lay, brightened under an advancing lantern, and I heard the steps of two men coming down the hall.
10083{_}348{_}It was a steady if not rapid approach, and I was quite prepared for their presence when they finally reached the doorway opposite and stopped to look in at what must have appeared to them a vast and empty space.
10083{_}349{_}They were officials, true enough--one hasty glance through the balustrade assured me of that.
10083{_}350{_}I even knew one of them by name--he was a sergeant of police and a highly trustworthy man.
10083{_}351{_}But how they had been drawn to this place at a moment so critical, I could not surmise.
10083{_}352{_}Do men of this stamp scent crime as a hound scents out prey?
10083{_}353{_}They had the look of hounds.
10083{_}354{_}Even in the momentary glimpse I got of them, I noted the tense and expectant look with which they endeavoured to pierce the dim spaces between us.
10083{_}355{_}The chase was on.
10083{_}356{_}It was something more than curiosity or a chance exercise of their duty which had brought them here.
10083{_}357{_}Their object was definite, and if the sight of the low gallery in which I lay, should suggest to them all its possibilities as a hiding-place, I should know in just one moment more what it is for the helpless quarry to feel the clutch of the captor.
10083{_}358{_}But the moment passed without any attempt at approach on their part, and when I lifted my head again it was to catch a glimpse of their side faces as they turned to look elsewhere for what they were plainly in search of.
10083{_}359{_}An oath, muffled but stern, which was the first word above a whisper that I had heard issue from their lips, told me that they had reached _the_ room and had come upon the horror which lay there.
10083{_}360{_}What would they say to it!
10083{_}361{_}Would they know who she was--her name, her quality, her story--and respect her dead as they certainly must have respected her living?
10083{_}362{_}I listened but caught only a low murmur as they conferred together.
10083{_}363{_}I imagined their movements; saw them in my mind's eye leaning over that death-tenanted couch, pointing with accusing finger at those two dark marks, and consulting each other with side-long looks, as they passed from one detail of her appearance to another.
10083{_}364{_}I even imagined them crossing the floor and lifting the two cordial glasses just as I had done, and then slowly setting them down again, with perhaps a lift of the brows or a suggestive shake of the head; and maddened by my own intolerable position, drawn by a power I felt it impossible to resist, I crept to my feet and took my staggering way down the half-dozen steps of the gallery and thence along by the left-hand wall towards the further doorway, and through it to where these men stood weighing the chances in which my life and honour were involved, and those of one other of whom I dared not think and would not have these men think for all that was left me of hope and happiness.
10083{_}365{_}It was dark in the ballroom, and it was only a little less so in the corridor.
10083{_}366{_}All the light was in _that_ room; but I still slid along the wall like a thief, with eyes set and ears agape for any chance word which might reach me.
10083{_}367{_}Suddenly I heard one.
10083{_}368{_}It was this, uttered with a decision which had the strange effect of lifting my head and making a man of me again:  "That settles it.
10083{_}369{_}He will find it hard to escape after this."
10083{_}370{_}_He!_ I had been dreading to hear a _she_.
10083{_}371{_}Yet why?
10083{_}372{_}Who on God's earth, save myself, could know that Carmel had been within these woeful walls to-night.
10083{_}373{_}_He!_ I never stopped to question who was meant by this definite pronoun.
10083{_}374{_}I was not even conscious of caring very much.
10083{_}375{_}I was in a coil of threatening troubles, but I was in it alone, and, greatly relieved by the discovery, I drew myself up and stepped quickly forward into the room where the two officials stood.
10083{_}376{_}Their faces, as they wheeled sharply about and took in my shoeless and more or less dishevelled figure, told me with an eloquence which made my heart sink, the unfortunate impression which my presence made upon them.
10083{_}377{_}It was but a fleeting look, for these men were both by nature and training easy masters of themselves; but its language was unmistakable and I knew that if I were to hold my own with them, I must get all the support I could from the truth, save where it would involve her--from the truth and my own consciousness of innocence, if I had any such consciousness.
10083{_}378{_}I was not sure that I had, for my falseness had precipitated this tragedy,--how I might never know, but a knowledge of the how was not necessary to my self-condemnation.
10083{_}379{_}Nevertheless my hands were clean of this murder, and allowing the surety of this fact to take a foremost place in my mind, I faced these men and with real feeling, but as little display of it as possible, I observed:  "You have come to my aid in a critical moment.
10083{_}380{_}This is my betrothed wife--the woman I was to marry--and I find her lying here dead, in this closed and lonely house.
10083{_}381{_}What does it mean?
10083{_}382{_}I know no more than you do."
10083{_}383{_}IV  THE ODD CANDLESTICK  It is a damned and a bloody work; The graceless action of a heavy hand, If that it be the work of any hand.
10083{_}384{_}_King John_.
10083{_}385{_}The two men eyed me quietly, then Hexford pointed to my shoeless feet and sternly retorted:  "Permit us to doubt your last assertion.
10083{_}386{_}You seem to be in better position than ourselves to explain the circumstances which puzzle you."
10083{_}387{_}They were right.
10083{_}388{_}It was for me to talk, not for them.
10083{_}389{_}I conceded the point in these words:  "Perhaps--but you cannot always trust appearances.
10083{_}390{_}I can explain my own presence here and the condition in which you find me, but I cannot explain this tragedy, near and dear as Miss Cumberland was to me.
10083{_}391{_}I did not know she was in the building, alive or dead.
10083{_}392{_}I came upon her here covered with the cushions just as you found her.
10083{_}393{_}I have felt the shock.
10083{_}394{_}I do not look like myself--I do not feel like myself; it was enough--" Here real emotion seized me and I almost broke down.
10083{_}395{_}I was in a position much more dreadful than any they could imagine or should be allowed to.
10083{_}396{_}Their silence led me to examine their faces.
10083{_}397{_}Hexford's mouth had settled into a stiff, straight line and the other man's wore a cynical smile I did not like.
10083{_}398{_}At this presage of the difficulties awaiting me, I felt one strand of the rope sustaining me above this yawning gulf of shame and ignominy crack and give way.
10083{_}399{_}Oh, for a better record in the past!--a staff on which to lean in such an hour as this!
10083{_}400{_}But while nothing serious clouded my name, I had more to blush for than to pride myself upon in my career as prince of good fellows,--and these men knew it, both of them, and let it weigh in the scale already tipped far off its balance by coincidences which a better man than myself would have found it embarrassing to explain.
10083{_}401{_}I recognised all this, I say, in the momentary glance I cast at their stern and unresponsive figures; but the courage which had served me in lesser extremities did not fail me now, and, kneeling down before my dead betrothed, I kissed her cold white hand with sincere compunction, before attempting the garbled and probably totally incoherent story with which I endeavoured to explain the inexplainable situation.
10083{_}402{_}They listened--I will do them that much justice; but it was with such an air of incredulity that my words fell with less and less continuity and finally lost themselves in a confused stammer as I reached the point where I pulled the cushions from the couch and made my ghastly discovery.
10083{_}403{_}"You see--see for yourselves--what confronted me.
10083{_}404{_}My betrothed--a dainty, delicate woman--dead--alone--in this solitary, far-away spot--the victim of what?
10083{_}405{_}I asked myself then--I ask myself now.
10083{_}406{_}I cannot understand it--or those glasses yonder--or _those marks!
10083{_}407{_}"_ They were black by this time--unmistakable--not to be ignored by them or by me.
10083{_}408{_}"We understand those marks, and you ought to," came from the second man, the one I did not know.
10083{_}409{_}My head fell forward; my lips refused to speak the words.
10083{_}410{_}I saw as in a flash, a picture of the one woman bending over the other; terror, reproach, anguish in the eyes whose fixed stare would never more leave my consciousness, an access of rage or some such sadden passion animating the other whose every curve spoke tenderness, whose every look up to this awful day had been as an angel's look to me.
10083{_}411{_}The vision was a maddening one.
10083{_}412{_}I shook myself free from it by starting to my feet."
10083{_}413{_}It's--it's--" I gasped.
10083{_}414{_}"She has been strangled," quoth Hexford, doggedly.
10083{_}415{_}"A dog's death," mumbled the other.
10083{_}416{_}My hands came together involuntarily.
10083{_}417{_}At that instant, with the memory before me of the vision I have just described, I almost wished that it had been _my_ hate, _my_ anger which had brought those tell-tale marks out upon that livid skin.
10083{_}418{_}I should have suffered less.
10083{_}419{_}I should only have had to pay the penalty of my crime and not be forced to think of Carmel with terrible revulsion, as I was now thinking, minute by minute, fight with it as I would.
10083{_}420{_}"You had better sit down," Hexford suddenly suggested, pushing a chair my way.
10083{_}421{_}"Clarke, look up the telephone and ask for three more men.
10083{_}422{_}I am going into this matter thoroughly.
10083{_}423{_}Perhaps you will tell us where the telephone is," he asked, turning my way.
10083{_}424{_}It was some little time before I took in these words.
10083{_}425{_}When I did, I became conscious of his keen look, also of a change in my own expression.
10083{_}426{_}I had forgotten the telephone.
10083{_}427{_}It had not yet been taken out.
10083{_}428{_}If only I had remembered this before these men came--I might have saved--No, nothing could have saved her or me, except the snow, except the snow.
10083{_}429{_}That may already have saved her.
10083{_}430{_}All this time I was trying to tell where the telephone was.
10083{_}431{_}That I succeeded at last I judged from the fact that the second man left the room.
10083{_}432{_}As he did so, Hexford lit the candle.
10083{_}433{_}Idly watching, for nothing now could make me look at the lounge again, I noticed the candlestick.
10083{_}434{_}It was of brass and rare in style and workmanship--a candlestick to be remembered; one of a pair perhaps.
10083{_}435{_}I felt my hair stir as I took in the details of its shape and ornamentation.
10083{_}436{_}If its mate were in her house--No, no, no!
10083{_}437{_}I would not have it so.
10083{_}438{_}I could not control my emotion if I let my imagination stray too far.
10083{_}439{_}The candlestick must be the property of the club.
10083{_}440{_}I had only forgotten.
10083{_}441{_}It was bought when?
10083{_}442{_}While thinking, planning, I was conscious of Hexford's eyes fixed steadily upon me.
10083{_}443{_}"Did you go into the kitchen in your wanderings below?"
10083{_}444{_}he asked.
10083{_}445{_}"No," I began, but seeing that I had made a mistake, I bungled and added weakly: "Yes; after matches."
10083{_}446{_}"Only matches?"
10083{_}447{_}"That's all."

10083{_}449{_}"Yes."

10083{_}457{_}"I have said so."

10083{_}461{_}"Upstairs."

10083{_}463{_}"No, sir."

10083{_}465{_}"Quite sure."
10083{_}466{_}"That's a pity.

10083{_}468{_}I stared at him, dazed.

10083{_}479{_}Only what was the question.

10083{_}481{_}I had no key; the cellar had been ransacked without my help; should I acknowledge this?

10083{_}484{_}They are in my rooms at home."
10083{_}485{_}I finished with a gasp.
10083{_}486{_}I had suddenly remembered that these keys were not in my rooms.
10083{_}487{_}I had had them with me at Miss Cumberland's and being given to fooling with something when embarrassed, I had fooled with them and dropped them while talking with Adelaide and watching Carmel.
10083{_}488{_}I had meant to pick them up but I forgot and--  "You need say nothing more about it," remarked Hexford.

10083{_}490{_}And stepping across the room, he took up the glasses one after the other and smelled of them.
10083{_}491{_}"Some sweet stuff," he remarked.
10083{_}492{_}"Cordial, I should say anisette.
10083{_}493{_}There wasn't anything like that on the kitchen table.
10083{_}494{_}Let us see what there is in here," he added, stepping into the adjoining small room into which I had simply peered in my own investigation of the place.
10083{_}495{_}As he did so, a keen blast blew in; a window in the adjoining room was open.
10083{_}496{_}He cast me a hurried glance and with the door in his hand, made the following remark:  "Your lady love--the victim here--could not have come through the snow with no more clothing on her than we see now.
10083{_}497{_}She must have worn a hat and coat or furs or something of that nature.
10083{_}498{_}Let us look for them."
10083{_}499{_}I rose, stumbling.
10083{_}500{_}I saw that he did not mean to leave me alone for a moment.
10083{_}501{_}Indeed, I did not wish to be so left.
10083{_}502{_}Better any companionship than that of my own thoughts and of her white upturned face.

10083{_}505{_}"Good!"
10083{_}506{_}left my companion's lips.
10083{_}507{_}"That's all straight.
10083{_}508{_}You recognise these garments?"
10083{_}509{_}I nodded, speechless.
10083{_}510{_}A thousand memories rushed upon me at the sight of the long plush coat which I had so often buttoned about her, with a troubled heart.
10083{_}511{_}How her eyes would seek mine as we stood thus close together, searching, searching for the old love or the fancied love of which the ashes only remained.

10083{_}513{_}The window which stood open was a small one,-a mere slit in the wall; but it let in a stream of zero air and I saw Hexford shiver as he stepped towards it and looked out.

10083{_}515{_}V  A SCRAP OF PAPER  Look to the lady:-- And when we have our naked frailties hid, That suffer in exposure, let us meet, And question this most bloody piece of work, To know it further.
10083{_}516{_}Fears and scruples shake us; In the great hand of God I stand; and, thence, Against the undivulg'd pretence I fight Of treasonous malice.
10083{_}517{_}_Macbeth_.
10083{_}518{_}Shortly after this, a fresh relay of police arrived and I could hear the whole house being ransacked.
10083{_}519{_}I had found my shoes, and was sitting in my own private room before a fire which had been lighted for me on the hearth.
10083{_}520{_}I was in a state of stupor now, and if my body shook, as it did from time to time, it was not from cold, nor do I think from any special horror of mind or soul (I felt too dull for that), but in response to the shuddering pines which pressed up close to the house at this point and soughed and tapped at the walls and muttered among themselves with an insistence which I could not ignore, notwithstanding my many reasons for self-absorption.
10083{_}521{_}The storm, which had been exceedingly fierce while it lasted, had quieted down to a steady fall of snow.
10083{_}522{_}Had its mission been to serve as a blanket to this crime by wiping out from the old snow all tell-tale footsteps and such other records as simplify cases of this kind for the detectives, it could not have happened more _apropos_ to the event.
10083{_}523{_}From the complaints which had already reached my ears from the two policemen, I was quite aware that even as early as their first arrival, they had found a clean page where possibly a few minutes before the whole secret of this tragedy may have been written in unmistakable characters; and while this tilled me with relief in one way, it added to my care in another, for the storm which could accomplish so much in so short a time was a bitter one for a young girl to meet, and Carmel must have met it at its worst, in her lonesome struggle homeward.
10083{_}524{_}Where was she?
10083{_}525{_}Living or dead, where was she now and where was Adelaide--the two women who for the last six weeks had filled my life with so many unhallowed and conflicting emotions?
10083{_}526{_}The conjecture passed incessantly through my brain, but it passed idly also and was not answered even in thought.
10083{_}527{_}Indeed, I seemed incapable of sustaining any line of thought for more than an instant, and when after an indefinite length of time the door behind me opened, the look I turned upon the gentleman who entered must have been a strange and far from encouraging one.
10083{_}528{_}He brought a lantern with him.
10083{_}529{_}So far the room had had no other illumination than such as came from the fire, and when he had set this lantern down on the mantel and turned to face me, I perceived, with a sort of sluggish hope, that he was Dr. Perry, once a practising physician and my father's intimate friend, now a county official of no ordinary intelligence and, what was better, of no ordinary feeling.
10083{_}530{_}His attachment to my father had not descended to me and, for the moment, he treated me like a stranger.
10083{_}531{_}"I am the coroner of this district," said he.
10083{_}532{_}"I have left my bed to have a few words with you and learn if your detention here is warranted.
10083{_}533{_}You are the president of this club, and the lady whose violent death in this place I have been called upon to investigate, is Miss Cumberland, your affianced wife?"
10083{_}534{_}My assent, though hardly audible, was not to be misunderstood.

10083{_}536{_}"They have told me what you had to say in explanation of your presence here where a crime of some nature has taken place.

10083{_}538{_}I feel that I owe you this consideration.

10083{_}541{_}Miss Cumberland's virtue and social standing no one can question, while you are the son of a man who has deservedly been regarded as an honour to the town.
10083{_}542{_}You have been intending to marry Miss Cumberland?"
10083{_}543{_}"Yes."
10083{_}544{_}I looked the man directly in the eye.
10083{_}545{_}"Our wedding-day was set."

10083{_}558{_}Was the room light enough to reveal my guilty flush?

10083{_}562{_}This man was cognisant of it, and if he, why not others!
10083{_}563{_}Why not the whole town!
10083{_}564{_}A danger which up to this moment I had heard whispered only by the pines, was opening in a gulf beneath our feet.

10083{_}577{_}Then doubt came.

10083{_}672{_}I know what the manly course would have been, but I preferred to skulk.

10083{_}676{_}I have no means of knowing now.
10083{_}677{_}She has not been her natural self for these last few days, but she had other causes for worry, and I have been willing enough to think that these were the occasion of her restless ways and short, sharp speech and the blankness with which she met all my attempts to soothe and encourage her.

10083{_}680{_}"This evening," I falteringly continued, "I had set as the limit to my endurance of the intolerable situation.
10083{_}681{_}During a minute of solitude preceding the dinner at Miss Cumberland's house on the Hill, I wrote a few lines to her sister, urging her to trust me with her fate and meet me at the station in time for the ten-thirty train.
10083{_}682{_}I meant to carry her at once to P----, where I had a friend in the ministry who would at once unite us in marriage.

10083{_}689{_}She had not expected it and I fear that the action was observed, for when I took my leave of Miss Cumberland shortly after, I was struck by her expression.
10083{_}690{_}I had never seen such a look on her face before, nor can I conceive of one presenting a more extraordinary contrast to the few and commonplace words with which she bade me good evening.
10083{_}691{_}I could not forget that look.

10083{_}693{_}Man's egotism, Dr. Perry.
10083{_}694{_}I neither knew Adelaide nor did I know the girl whose love I had so over-estimated.
10083{_}695{_}She failed me, Dr. Perry.

10083{_}699{_}I had staked my whole future on one desperate throw and I had lost.

10083{_}701{_}Indeed, I had forgotten to whom I was talking.

10083{_}703{_}His action recalled me to the infinitely deeper misery of my present situation, and conscious of the conclusions which might be drawn from such impulsive utterances, I pulled myself together and proceeded to finish my story with greater directness.
10083{_}704{_}"I did not leave the station till the ten-thirty train had gone.
10083{_}705{_}I had hopes, still, of seeing her, or possibly I dreaded the long ride back to my apartments.
10083{_}706{_}It was from sheer preoccupation of mind that I drove this way instead of straight out by Marshall Avenue.
10083{_}707{_}I had no intention of stopping here; the club-house was formally closed yesterday, as you may know, and I did not even have the keys with me.

10083{_}709{_}"By the lower one."
10083{_}710{_}"Was it snowing at this time?"
10083{_}711{_}"Not yet.
10083{_}712{_}It was just before the clouds rushed upon the moon.
10083{_}713{_}I could see everything quite plainly."
10083{_}714{_}My companion nodded and I went breathlessly on.
10083{_}715{_}Any question of his staggered me.
10083{_}716{_}I was so ignorant of the facts at his command, of the facts at any one's command outside my own experience and observation, that the simplest admission I made might lead directly to some clew of whose very existence I was unaware.
10083{_}717{_}I was not even able to conjecture by what chance or at whose suggestion the police had raided the place and discovered the tragedy which had given point to that raid.
10083{_}718{_}No one had told me, and I had met with no encouragement to ask.
10083{_}719{_}I felt myself sliding amid pitfalls.
10083{_}720{_}My own act might precipitate the very doom I sought to avert.
10083{_}721{_}Yet I must preserve my self-possession and answer all questions as truthfully as possible lest I stumble into a web from which no skill of my own or of another could extricate me.
10083{_}722{_}"Fastening my horse to one of the pine trees in the thickest clump I saw--he is there now, I suppose--I crept up to the house, and tried the door.
10083{_}723{_}It was on the latch and I stole in.
10083{_}724{_}There was no light on the lower floor, and after listening for any signs of life, I began to feel my way about the house, searching for the intruder.
10083{_}725{_}As I did not wish to attract attention to myself, I took off my shoes.
10083{_}726{_}I went through the lower rooms, and then I came upstairs.
10083{_}727{_}It was some time before I reached the--the room where a fire had been lit; but when I did I knew--not," I hastily corrected, as I caught his quick concentrated glance, "what had happened or whom I should find there, but that this was the spot where the intruder had been, possibly was now, and I determined to grapple with him.
10083{_}728{_}What--what have I said?"
10083{_}729{_}I asked in anguish, as I caught a look on the coroner's face of irrepressible repulsion and disgust, slight and soon gone but unmistakable so long as it lasted.
10083{_}730{_}"Nothing," he replied, "go on."
10083{_}731{_}But his tone, considerate as it had been from the first, did not deceive me.
10083{_}732{_}I knew that I had been detected in some slip or prevarication.
10083{_}733{_}As I had omitted all mention of the most serious part of my adventure--had said nothing of my vision of Carmel or the terrible conclusions which her presence there had awakened--my conscience was in a state of perturbation which added greatly to my confusion.
10083{_}734{_}For a moment I did not know where I stood, and I am afraid I betrayed a sense of my position.
10083{_}735{_}He had to recall me to myself by an unimportant question or two before I could go on.
10083{_}736{_}When I did proceed, it was with less connection of ideas and a haste in speaking which was not due altogether to the harrowing nature of the tale itself.
10083{_}737{_}"I had matches in my pocket and I struck one," I began.
10083{_}738{_}"Afterwards I lit the candle.
10083{_}739{_}The emptiness of the room did not alarm me.
10083{_}740{_}I experienced the sense of tragedy.
10083{_}741{_}Seeing the pillows heaped high and too regularly for chance along a lounge ordinarily holding only two, I tore them off.
10083{_}742{_}I saw a foot, a hand, a tress of bright hair.
10083{_}743{_}Even then I did not think of _her_.
10083{_}744{_}Why should I?
10083{_}745{_}Not till I uncovered the face did I know the terrors of my discovery, and then, the confusion of it all unmanned me and I fell on my knees--"  "Go on!
10083{_}746{_}Go on!"
10083{_}747{_}The impetuosity, the suspense in the words astounded me.
10083{_}748{_}I stared at the coroner and lost the thread of my story--What had I to say more?
10083{_}749{_}How account for what must be ever unaccountable to him, to the world, to my own self, if in obedience to the demands of the situation I subdued my own memory and blotted out all I had seen but that which it was safe to confess to?
10083{_}750{_}"There is no more to say," I murmured.
10083{_}751{_}"The horror of that moment made a chaos in my mind.
10083{_}752{_}I looked at the dead body of her who lay there as I have looked at everything since; as I looked at the police when they came--as I look at you now.
10083{_}753{_}But I know nothing.
10083{_}754{_}It is all a phantasmagoria to me--with no more meaning than a nightmare.
10083{_}755{_}She is dead--I know that--but beyond that, all is doubt--confusion--what the world and all its passing show is to a blind man.
10083{_}756{_}I can neither understand nor explain."
10083{_}757{_}VI  COMMENTS AND REFLECTIONS  There is no agony and no solace left; Earth can console, Heaven can torment, no more  _Prometheus Unbound_   The coroner's intent look which had more or less sustained me through this ordeal, remained fixed upon my face as though he were still anxious to see me exonerate myself.

10083{_}759{_}That was the question.
10083{_}760{_}_How much did he know_?

10083{_}762{_}I had revealed all I dared to.
10083{_}763{_}As I came to this conclusion, his eyes fell and I knew that the favorable minute had passed.

10083{_}793{_}I was panting for relief.
