10083{_}799{_}Perry?"
10083{_}800{_}"There were three glasses in those rooms.
10083{_}801{_}Only two were drank from," he answered, steadily.
10083{_}802{_}"Tomorrow I may be in a position to answer your question.
10083{_}803{_}I am not to-night."
10083{_}804{_}Why did I take heart?
10083{_}805{_}Not a change, not the flicker of one had passed over his countenance at my utterance of the word _man_.
10083{_}806{_}Either his official habit had stood him in wonderful stead, or the police had failed so far to see any connection between this murder and the young girl whose footprints, for all I knew, still lingered on the stairs.
10083{_}807{_}Would the morrow arm them with completer knowledge?
10083{_}808{_}As I turned from his retreating figure and flung myself down before the hearth, this was the question I continually propounded to myself, in vain repetition.
10083{_}809{_}Would the morrow reveal the fact that Adelaide's young sister had been with her in the hour of death, or would the fates propitiously aid her in preserving this secret as they had already aided her in selecting for the one man who shared it, him who of all others was bound by honour and personal consideration for her not to divulge what he knew.
10083{_}810{_}Thus the hours between two and seven passed when I fell into a fitful sleep, from which I was rudely wakened by a loud rattle at my door, followed by the entrance of the officer who had walked up and down the corridor all night.
10083{_}811{_}"The waggon is here," said he.
10083{_}812{_}"Breakfast will be given you at the station."
10083{_}813{_}To which Hexford, looking over his shoulder, added: "I'm sorry to say that we have here the warrant for your arrest.
10083{_}814{_}Can I do anything for you?"
10083{_}815{_}"Warrant!"
10083{_}816{_}I burst out, "what do you want of a warrant?
10083{_}817{_}It is as a witness you seek to detain me, I presume?"
10083{_}818{_}"No," was his brusque reply.
10083{_}819{_}"The charge upon which you are arrested is one of murder.
10083{_}820{_}You will have to appear before a magistrate.
10083{_}821{_}I'm sorry to be the one to tell you this, but the evidence against you is very strong, and the police must do their duty."
10083{_}822{_}"But I am innocent, absolutely innocent," I protested, the perspiration starting from every pore as the full meaning of the charge burst upon me.
10083{_}823{_}"What I have told you was correct.
10083{_}824{_}I, myself, found her dead--"  Hexford gave me a look.
10083{_}825{_}"Don't talk," he kindly suggested.
10083{_}826{_}"Leave that to the lawyers."
10083{_}827{_}Then, as the other man turned aside for a moment, he whispered in my ear, "It's no go; one of our men saw you with your fingers on her throat.
10083{_}828{_}He had clambered into a pine tree and the shade of the window was up.
10083{_}829{_}You had better come quietly.
10083{_}830{_}Not a soul believes you innocent."
10083{_}831{_}This, then, was what had doomed me from the start; this, and that partly burned letter.
10083{_}832{_}I understood now why the kind-hearted coroner, who loved my father, had urged me to tell my tale, hoping that I would explain this act and give him some opportunity to indulge in a doubt.
10083{_}833{_}And I had failed to respond to the hint he had given me.
10083{_}834{_}The act itself must appear so sinister and the impulse which drove me to it so incomprehensible, without the heart-rending explanation I dare not subjoin, that I never questioned the wisdom of silence in its regard.
10083{_}835{_}Yet this silence had undone me.
10083{_}836{_}I had been seen fingering my dead betrothed's throat, and nothing I could now say or do would ever convince people that she was dead before my hands touched her, strangled by another's clutch.
10083{_}837{_}One person only in the whole world would know and feel how false this accusation was.
10083{_}838{_}And yesterday that one's trust in my guiltlessness would have thrown a ray of light upon the deepest infamy which could befall me.
10083{_}839{_}But to-day there had settled over that once innocent spirit, a cloud of too impenetrable a nature for any light to struggle to and fro between us.
10083{_}840{_}I could not contemplate that cloud.
10083{_}841{_}I could not dwell upon her misery, or upon the revulsion of feeling which follows such impetuous acts.
10083{_}842{_}And it had been an impetuous act--the result of one of her rages.
10083{_}843{_}I had been told of these rages.
10083{_}844{_}I had even seen her in one.
10083{_}845{_}When they passed she was her lovable self once more and very penitent and very downcast.
10083{_}846{_}If all I feared were true, she was suffering acutely now.
10083{_}847{_}But I gave no thought to this.
10083{_}848{_}I could dream of but one thing--how to save her from the penalty of crime, a penalty I might be forced to suffer myself and would prefer to suffer rather than see it fall upon one so young and so angelically beautiful.
10083{_}849{_}Turning to the officer next me, I put the question which had been burning in my mind for hours:  "Tell me, how you came to know there was trouble here?
10083{_}850{_}What brought you to this house?
10083{_}851{_}There can be nothing wrong in telling me that."
10083{_}852{_}"Well, if you don't know--" he began.
10083{_}853{_}"I do not," I broke in.
10083{_}854{_}"I guess you'd better wait till the chief has had a word with you."
10083{_}855{_}I suppressed all tokens of my disappointment, and by a not unnatural reaction, perhaps, began to take in, and busy myself with, the very considerations I had hitherto shunned.
10083{_}856{_}Where was Carmel, and how was she enduring these awful hours?
10083{_}857{_}Had repentance come, and with it a desire to own her guilt?
10083{_}858{_}Did she think of me and the effect this unlooked-for death would have upon my feelings?
10083{_}859{_}That I should suffer arrest for her crime could not have entered her mind.
10083{_}860{_}I had seen her, but she had not seen me, in the dark hall which I must now traverse as a prisoner and a suspect.
10083{_}861{_}No intimation of my dubious position or its inevitable consequences had reached her yet.
10083{_}862{_}When it did, what would she do?
10083{_}863{_}I did not know her well enough to tell.
10083{_}864{_}The attraction she had felt for me had not been strong enough to lead her to accommodate herself to my wishes and marry me off-hand, but it had been strong enough to nerve her arm in whatever altercation she may have had with her jealous-minded sister.
10083{_}865{_}It was the temper and not the strength of the love which would tell in a strait like this.
10083{_}866{_}Would it prove of a generous kind?
10083{_}867{_}Should I have to combat her desire to take upon herself the full blame of her deed, with all its shames and penalties?
10083{_}868{_}Or should I have the still deeper misery of finding her callous to my position and welcoming any chance which diverted suspicion from herself?
10083{_}869{_}Either supposition might be possible, according to my judgment in this evil hour.
10083{_}870{_}All communication between us, in spite of our ardent and ungovernable passion, had been so casual and so slight.
10083{_}871{_}Looks, a whispered word or so, one furtive clasp in which our hands seemed to grow together, were all I had to go upon as tests of her feeling towards me.
10083{_}872{_}Her character I had judged from her face, which was lovely.
10083{_}873{_}But faces deceive, and the loveliness of youth is not like the loveliness of age--an absolute mirror of the soul within.
10083{_}874{_}Was not Medusa captivating, for all her snaky locks?
10083{_}875{_}Hide those locks and one might have thought her a Daphne.
10083{_}876{_}What would relieve my doubts?
10083{_}877{_}As Hexford drew near me again on our way to the head of the staircase, I summoned up courage to ask:  "Have you heard anything from the Hill?
10083{_}878{_}Has the news of this tragedy been communicated to Miss Cumberland's family, and if so, how are they bearing this affliction?"
10083{_}879{_}His lip curled, and for a minute he hesitated; then something in my aspect or the straight-forward look I gave him, softened him and he answered frankly, if coldly:  "Word has gone there, of course, but only the servants are affected by it so far.
10083{_}880{_}Miss Cumberland, the younger, is very ill, and the boy--I don't know his name--has not shown up since last evening.
10083{_}881{_}He's very dissipated, they say, and may be in any one of the joints in the lower part of the town."
10083{_}882{_}I stopped in dismay, clutching wildly at the railing of the stairs we were descending.
10083{_}883{_}I had hardly heard the latter words, all my mind was on what he had said first.
10083{_}884{_}"Miss Carmel Cumberland ill?"
10083{_}885{_}I stammered, "too ill to be told?"
10083{_}886{_}I was sufficiently master of myself to put it this way.
10083{_}887{_}"Yes," he rejoined, kindly, as he urged me down the very stairs I had seen her descend in such a state of mind a few hours before.
10083{_}888{_}"A servant who had been out late, heard the fall of some heavy body as she was passing Miss Cumberland's rooms, and rushing in found Miss Carmel, as she called her, lying on the floor near the open fire.
10083{_}889{_}Her face had struck the bars of the grate in falling, and she was badly burned.
10083{_}890{_}But that was not all; she was delirious with fever, brought on, they think, by anxiety about her sister, whose name she was constantly repeating.
10083{_}891{_}They had a doctor for her and the whole house was up before ever the word came of what had happened here."
10083{_}892{_}I thanked him with a look.
10083{_}893{_}I had no opportunity for more.
10083{_}894{_}Half a dozen officers were standing about the front door, and in another moment I was bustled into the conveyance provided and was being driven away from the death-haunted spot.
10083{_}895{_}I had heard the last whisper of those pines for many, many days.
10083{_}896{_}But not in my dreams; it ever came back at night, sinister, awesome, haunted with dead hopes and breathing of an ever doubtful future.
10083{_}897{_}VII  CLIFTON ACCEPTS MY CASE  This hand of mine Is yet a maiden and an innocent hand, Not painted with the crimson spots of blood.
10083{_}898{_}Within this bosom never enter'd yet The dreadful motion of a murd'rous thought.
10083{_}899{_}_King John_.
10083{_}900{_}My first thought (when I could think at all) was this:  "She has some feeling, then!
10083{_}901{_}Her terror and remorse have maddened her.
10083{_}902{_}I can dwell upon her image with pity."
10083{_}903{_}The next, "Will they find her wet clothes and discover that she was out last night?"
10083{_}904{_}The latter possibility troubled me.
10083{_}905{_}My mind was the seat of strange contradictions.
10083{_}906{_}As the day advanced and I began to realise that I, Elwood Ranelagh, easy-going man of the world, but with traditions of respectable living on both sides of my house and a list of friends of which any man might be proud, was in a place of detention on the awful charge of murder, I found that my keenest torment arose from the fact that I was shut off from the instant knowledge of what was going on in the house where all my thoughts, my fears, and shall I say it, latent hopes were centred.
10083{_}907{_}To know Carmel ill and not to know how ill!
10083{_}908{_}To feel the threatening arm of the law hovering constantly over her head and neither to know the instant of its fall nor be given the least opportunity to divert it.
10083{_}909{_}To realise that some small inadvertance on her part, some trivial but incriminating object left about, some heedless murmur or burst of unconscious frenzy might precipitate her doom, and I remain powerless, bearing my share of suspicion and ignominy, it is true, but not the chief share if matters befell as I have suggested, which they were liable to do at any hour, nay, at any minute.
10083{_}910{_}My examination before the magistrate held one element of comfort.
10083{_}911{_}Nothing in its whole tenor went to show that, as yet, she was in the least suspected of any participation in my so-called crime.
10083{_}912{_}But the knowledge which came later, of how the police first learned of trouble at the club-house did not add to this sense of relief, whatever satisfaction it gave my curiosity.
10083{_}913{_}A cry of distress had come to them over the telephone; a wild cry, in a woman's choked and tremulous voice: "Help at The Whispering Pines!
10083{_}914{_}Help!"
10083{_}915{_}That was all, or all they revealed to me.
10083{_}916{_}In their endeavour to find out whether or not I was present when this call was made, I learned the nature of their own suspicions.
10083{_}917{_}They believed that Adelaide in some moment of prevision had managed to reach the telephone and send out this message.
10083{_}918{_}But what did I believe?
10083{_}919{_}What could I believe?
10083{_}920{_}All the incidents of the deadly struggle which must have preceded the fatal culminating act, were mysteries which my mind refused to penetrate.
10083{_}921{_}After hours of torturing uncertainty, and an evening which was the miserable precursor of a still more miserable night, I decided to drop conjecture and await the enlightenment which must come with the morrow.
10083{_}922{_}It was, therefore, in a condition of mingled dread and expectation that I opened the paper which was brought me the next morning.
10083{_}923{_}Of the shock which it gave me to see my own name blotting the page with suggestions of hideous crime, I will not speak, but pass at once to the few gleams of added knowledge I was able to gather from those abominable columns.
10083{_}924{_}Arthur, the good-for-nothing brother, had returned from his wild carouse and had taken affairs in charge with something like spirit and a decent show of repentance for his own shortcomings and the mad taste for liquor which had led him away from home that night.
10083{_}925{_}Carmel was still ill, and likely to be so for many days to come.
10083{_}926{_}Her case was diagnosed as one of brain fever and of a most dangerous type.
10083{_}927{_}Doctors and nurses were busy at her bedside and little hope was held out of her being able to tell soon, if ever, what she knew of her sister's departure from the house on that fatal evening.
10083{_}928{_}That her testimony on this point would be invaluable was self-evident, for proofs were plenty of her having haunted her sister's rooms all the evening in a condition of more or less delirium.
10083{_}929{_}She was alone in the house and this may have added to her anxieties, all of the servants having gone to the policemen's ball.
10083{_}930{_}It was on their return in the early morning hours that she had been discovered, lying ill and injured before her sister's fireplace.
10083{_}931{_}One fact was mentioned which set me thinking.
10083{_}932{_}The keys of the club-house had been found lying on a table in the side hall of the Cumberland mansion--the keys which I have already mentioned as missing from my pocket.
10083{_}933{_}An alarming discovery which might have acted as a clew to the suspicious I feared, if their presence there had not been explained by the waitress who had cleared the table after dinner.
10083{_}934{_}Coming upon these keys lying on the floor beside one of the chairs, she had carried them out into the hall and laid them where they would be more readily seen.
10083{_}935{_}She had not recognised the keys, but had taken it for granted that they belonged to Mr. Ranelagh who had dined at the house that night.
10083{_}936{_}They were my keys, and I have already related how I came to drop them on the floor.
10083{_}937{_}Had they but stayed there!
10083{_}938{_}Adelaide, or was it Carmel, might not have seen them and been led by some strange, if not tragic, purpose, incomprehensible to us now and possibly never to find full explanation, to enter the secret and forsaken spot where I later found them, the one dead, the other fleeing in frenzy, but not in such a thoughtless frenzy as to forget these keys or to fail to lock the club-house door behind her.
10083{_}939{_}That she, on her return home, should have had sufficient presence of mind to toss these keys down in the same place from which she or her sister had taken them, argued well for her clear-headedness up to that moment.
10083{_}940{_}The fever must have come on later--a fever which with my knowledge of what had occurred at The Whispering Pines, seemed the only natural outcome of the situation.
10083{_}941{_}The next paragraph detailed a fact startling enough to rouse my deepest interest.
10083{_}942{_}Zadok Brown, the Cumberlands' coachman, declared that Arthur's cutter and what he called the grey mare had been out that night.
10083{_}943{_}They were both in place when he returned to the stable towards early morning, but the signs were unmistakable that both had been out in the snow since he left the stable at about nine.
10083{_}944{_}He had locked the stable-door at that time, but the key always hung in the kitchen where any one could get it.
10083{_}945{_}This was on account of Arthur, who, if he wanted to go out late, sometimes harnessed a horse himself.
10083{_}946{_}Zadok judged that he had done so this night, though how the horse happened to be back and in her stall and no Mr. Arthur in the house, it would take wiser heads than his to explain.
10083{_}947{_}But he was sure the mare had been out.
10083{_}948{_}There was some comment made on this, because Arthur had denied using his cutter that night.
10083{_}949{_}He declared instead that he had gone out on foot and designated the coachman's tale as all bosh.
10083{_}950{_}"I was not the only one who had a drop too much down-town," was the dogged assertion with which he met all questions on this subject.
10083{_}951{_}"I wouldn't give a snap of my finger for Zadok's opinion on any subject, after five hours of dancing and the necessary drinks.
10083{_}952{_}There were no signs of the mare having been out when I got home."
10083{_}953{_}As this was about noon the next day, his opinion on this point could not be said to count for much.
10083{_}954{_}As for myself, I felt inclined to believe that the mare had been out, that one or both of the women had harnessed him and that it was by these means they had reached The Whispering Pines.
10083{_}955{_}The night was too cold, a storm too imminent, for them to have contemplated so long a walk on a road so remote as that leading to the club-house.
10083{_}956{_}Arthur was athletic but Adelaide was far from strong and never addicted to walking under the most favourable conditions.
10083{_}957{_}Of all the mysteries surrounding her dead presence in the club-house, the one which from the first had struck me as the most inexplicable was the manner of her reaching there.
10083{_}958{_}Now I could understand both that fact and how Carmel had succeeded in returning in safety to her home.
10083{_}959{_}She had ridden both ways--a theory which likewise explained how she came to wear a man's derby and possibly a man's overcoat.
10083{_}960{_}With her skirts covered by a bear-skin she would present a very fair figure of a man to any one who chanced to pass her.
10083{_}961{_}This was desirable in her case.
10083{_}962{_}A man and woman driving at a late hour through the city streets would attract little, if any, attention, while two women might.
10083{_}963{_}Having no wish to attract attention, they had resorted to subterfuge--or Carmel had; it was not like Adelaide to do so.
10083{_}964{_}She was always perfectly open, both in manner and speech.
10083{_}965{_}These were my deductions drawn from my own knowledge.
10083{_}966{_}Would others who had not my knowledge be in any wise influenced to draw the same?
10083{_}967{_}Would the fact that the mare had been out during those mysterious hours when everybody had appeared to be absent from the house, saving the one young girl whom they afterwards found stark, staring mad with delirium, serve to awaken suspicion of her close and personal connection with this crime?
10083{_}968{_}There was nothing in this reporter's article to show that such an idea had dawned upon his mind, but the police are not readily hoodwinked and I dreaded the result of their inquiries, if they chose to follow this undoubted clew.
10083{_}969{_}Yet, if they let this point slip, where should I be?
10083{_}970{_}Human nature is human all the way through, and I could not help having moments when I asked myself if this young girl were worth the sacrifice I contemplated making for her?
10083{_}971{_}She was lovely to look at, amiable and of womanly promise save at those rare and poignant moments when passion would seize her in a gust which drove everything before it.
10083{_}972{_}But were any of these considerations sufficient to justify me in letting my whole manhood slip for the sake of one who, whatever the provocation, had used the strength of her hands against the sister who had been as a mother to her for so many years.
10083{_}973{_}That she had had provocation I did not doubt.
10083{_}974{_}Adelaide, for all her virtues, was not an easy person to deal with.
10083{_}975{_}Upright and perfectly sincere herself, she had no sympathy with or commiseration for any lack of principle or any display of selfishness in others.
10083{_}976{_}A little cold, a little reserved, a little lacking in spontaneity, though always correct and always generous in her gifts and often in her acts, her whole nature would rise at any evidence of meanness or ingratitude, and though she said little, you would feel her disapprobation through and through.
10083{_}977{_}She would even change physically.
10083{_}978{_}Naturally pallid and of small inconspicuous features, her eyes on these occasions would so flame and her whole figure so dilate that she looked like another woman.
10083{_}979{_}I have seen her brother, six feet in height and weighty for his years, cringe under her few quiet words at these times till she absolutely seemed the taller of the two.
10083{_}980{_}It was only in these moments she was handsome, and had I loved her, I should probably have admired this passionate purity, this intolerance of all that was small or selfish or unworthy a good woman's esteem.
10083{_}981{_}But not loving her, I had merely cherished a wholesome fear of her displeasure, and could quite comprehend what a full display of anger on her part might call up in her sensitive, already deeply suffering sister.
10083{_}982{_}The scathing arraignment, the unbearable taunt--Well, well, it was all dream-work, but I had time to dream and opportunity for little else, and pictures, which till now I had sedulously kept in the background of my imagination, would come to the front as I harped on this topic and weighed in my disturbed mind the following question: Should I continue the course which I had instinctively taken out of a natural sense of chivalry, or face my calumniators with the truth and leave my cause and hers to the justice of men, rather than to the slow but righteous workings of Providence?
10083{_}983{_}I struggled with the dilemma for hours, the more so, that I did not stand alone in the world.
10083{_}984{_}I had relatives and I had friends, some of whom had come to see me and gone away deeply grieved at my reticence.
10083{_}985{_}I was swayed, too, by another consideration.
10083{_}986{_}I had deeply loved my mother.
10083{_}987{_}She was dead, but I had her honour to think of.
10083{_}988{_}Should it be said she had a murderer for her son?
10083{_}989{_}In the height of my inner conflict, I had almost cried aloud the fierce denial which would arise at this thought.
10083{_}990{_}But ere the word could leave my lips, such a vision rose before me of a bewildering young face with wonderful eyes and a smile too innocent for guile and too loving for hypocrisy, that I forgot my late antagonistic feelings, forgot the claims of my dear, dead mother, and even those of my own future.
10083{_}991{_}Such passion and such devotion merited consideration from the man who had called them forth.
10083{_}992{_}I would not slight the claims of my dead mother but I would give this young girl a chance for her life.
10083{_}993{_}Let others ferret out the fact that she had visited the club-house with her sister; I would not proclaim it.
10083{_}994{_}It was enough for me to proclaim my innocence, and that I would do to the last.
10083{_}995{_}I was in this frame of mind when Charles Clifton called and was allowed to see me.
10083{_}996{_}I had sent for him in one of my discouraged moods.
10083{_}997{_}He was my friend, but he was also my legal adviser, and it was as such I had summoned him, and it was as such he had now come.
10083{_}998{_}Cordial as our relations had been--though he was hardly one of my ilk--I noted no instinctive outstretching of his hand, and so did not reach out mine.
10083{_}999{_}Appearances had been too strong against me for any such spontaneous outburst from even my best friends.
10083{_}1000{_}I realised that to expect otherwise from him or from any other man would be to play the fool; and this was no time for folly.
10083{_}1001{_}The day for that was passed.
10083{_}1002{_}I was the first to speak.
10083{_}1003{_}"You see me where you have never thought to see a friend of yours.
10083{_}1004{_}But we won't go into that.
10083{_}1005{_}The police have good reasons for what they have done and I presume feel justified in my commitment.
10083{_}1006{_}Notwithstanding, I am an innocent man so far as the attack made upon Miss Cumberland goes.
10083{_}1007{_}I had no hand in her murder, if murder it is found out to be.
10083{_}1008{_}My story which you have read in the papers and which I felt forced to give out, possibly to my own shame and that of another whom I would fain have saved, is an absolutely true one.
10083{_}1009{_}I did not arrive at The Whispering Pines until after Miss Cumberland was dead.
10083{_}1010{_}To this I am ready to swear and it is upon this fact you must rely, in any defence you may hereafter be called upon to make in my regard."
10083{_}1011{_}He listened as a lawyer would be apt to listen to such statements from the man who had summoned him to his aid.
10083{_}1012{_}But I saw that I had made no impression on his convictions.
10083{_}1013{_}He regarded me as a guilty man, and what was more to the point no doubt, as one for whom no plea could be made or any rational defence undertaken.
10083{_}1014{_}"You don't believe me," I went on, still without any great bitterness.
10083{_}1015{_}"I am not surprised at it, after what the man Clarke has said of seeing me with my hands on her throat.
10083{_}1016{_}Any man, friend or not, would take me for a villain after that.
10083{_}1017{_}But, Charles, to you I will confess what cowardice kept me from owning to Dr. Perry at the proper, possibly at the only proper moment, that I did this out of a wild desire to see if those marks were really the marks of strangling fingers.
10083{_}1018{_}I could not believe that she had been so killed and, led away by my doubts, I leaned over her and--You shall believe me, you must," I insisted, as I perceived his hard gaze remain unsoftened.
10083{_}1019{_}"I don't ask it of the rest of the world.
10083{_}1020{_}I hardly expect any one to give me credit for good impulses or even for speaking the plain truth after the discovery which has been made of my treacherous attitude towards these two virtuous and devoted women.
10083{_}1021{_}But you--if you are to act as my counsel--must take this denial from me as gospel truth.
10083{_}1022{_}I may disappoint you in other ways.
10083{_}1023{_}I may try you and often make you regret that you undertook my case, but on this fact you may safely pin your faith.
10083{_}1024{_}She was dead before I touched her.
10083{_}1025{_}Had the police spy whose testimony is likely to hang me, climbed the tree a moment sooner than he did, he would have seen that.
10083{_}1026{_}Are you ready to take my case?"
10083{_}1027{_}Clifton is a fair fellow and I knew if he once accepted the fact I thus urged upon him, he would work for me with all the skill and ability my desperate situation demanded.
10083{_}1028{_}I, therefore, watched him with great anxiety for the least change in the constrained attitude and fixed, unpromising gaze with which he had listened to me, and was conscious of a great leap of heart as the set expression of his features relaxed, and he responded almost warmly:  "I will take your case, Ranelagh.
10083{_}1029{_}God help me to make it good against all odds."
10083{_}1030{_}I was conscious of few hopes, but some of the oppression under which I laboured lifted at those words.
10083{_}1031{_}I had assured one man of my innocence!
10083{_}1032{_}It was like a great rock in the weary desert.
10083{_}1033{_}My sigh of relief bespoke my feelings and I longed to take his hand, but the moment had not yet come.
10083{_}1034{_}Something was wanting to a perfect confidence between us, and I was in too sensitive a frame of mind to risk the slightest rebuff.
10083{_}1035{_}He was ready to speak before I was.
10083{_}1036{_}"Then, you had not been long on the scene of crime when the police arrived?"
10083{_}1037{_}"I had been in the room but a few minutes.
10083{_}1038{_}I do not know how long I was searching the house."
10083{_}1039{_}"The police say that fully twenty minutes elapsed between the time they received Miss Cumberland's appeal for help and their arrival at the club-house.
10083{_}1040{_}If you were there that long--"  "I cannot say.
10083{_}1041{_}Moments are hours at such a crisis--I--"  My emotions were too much for me, and I confusedly stopped.
10083{_}1042{_}He was surveying me with the old distrust.
10083{_}1043{_}In a moment I saw why.
10083{_}1044{_}"You are not open with me," he protested.
10083{_}1045{_}"Why should moments be hours to you previous to the instant when you stripped those pillows from the couch?
10083{_}1046{_}You are not a fanciful man, nor have you any cowardly instincts.
10083{_}1047{_}Why were you in such a turmoil going through a house where you could have expected to find nothing worse than some miserable sneak thief?"
10083{_}1048{_}This was a poser.
10083{_}1049{_}I had laid myself open to suspicion by one thoughtless admission, and what was worse, it was but the beginning in all probability of many other possible mistakes.
10083{_}1050{_}I had never taken the trouble to measure my words and the whole truth being impossible, I necessarily must make a slip now and then.
10083{_}1051{_}He had better be warned of this.
10083{_}1052{_}I did not wish him to undertake my cause blindfolded.
10083{_}1053{_}He must understand its difficulties while believing in my innocence.
10083{_}1054{_}Then, if he chose to draw back, well and good.
10083{_}1055{_}I should have to face the situation alone.
10083{_}1056{_}"Charles," said I, as soon as I could perfectly control my speech, "you are quite just in your remark.
10083{_}1057{_}I am not and can not be perfectly open with you.
10083{_}1058{_}I shall tell you no lies, but beyond that I cannot promise.
10083{_}1059{_}I am caught in a net not altogether of my own weaving.
10083{_}1060{_}So far I will be frank with you.
10083{_}1061{_}A common question may trip me up, others find me free and ready with my defence.
10083{_}1062{_}You have chanced upon one of the former.
10083{_}1063{_}I was in a turmoil of mind from the moment of my entrance into that fatal house, but I can give no reason for it unless I am, as you hinted, a coward."
10083{_}1064{_}He settled that supposition with a gesture I had rather not have seen.
10083{_}1065{_}It would be better for him to consider me a poltroon than to suspect my real reasons for the agitation which I had acknowledged.
10083{_}1066{_}"You say you cannot be open with me.
10083{_}1067{_}That means you have certain memories connected with that night which you cannot divulge."
10083{_}1068{_}"Right, Charles; but not memories of guilt--of active guilt, I mean.
10083{_}1069{_}This I have previously insisted on, and this is what you must believe.
10083{_}1070{_}I am not even an accessory before the fact.
10083{_}1071{_}I am perfectly innocent so far as Adelaide's death is concerned.
10083{_}1072{_}You may proceed on that basis without fear.
10083{_}1073{_}That is, if you continue to take an interest in my case.
10083{_}1074{_}If not, I shall be the last to blame you.
10083{_}1075{_}Little honour is likely to accrue to you from defending me."
10083{_}1076{_}"I have accepted the case and I shall continue to interest myself in it," he assured me, with a dogged rather than genial persistence.
10083{_}1077{_}"But I should like to know what I am to work upon, if it cannot be shown that her call for help came before you entered the building."
10083{_}1078{_}"That would be the best defence possible, of course," I replied; "but neither from your standpoint nor mine is it a feasible one.
10083{_}1079{_}I have no proof of my assertion, I never looked at my watch from the time I left the station till I found it run down this very morning.
10083{_}1080{_}The club-house clock has been out of order for some time and was not running.
10083{_}1081{_}All I know and can swear to about the length of time I was in that building prior to the arrival of the police, is that it could not have been very long, since she was not only dead and buried under those accumulated cushions, but in a room some little distance from the telephone."
10083{_}1082{_}"That will do for me," said he, "but scarcely for those who are prejudiced against you.
10083{_}1083{_}Everything points so indisputably to your guilt.
10083{_}1084{_}The note which you say you wrote to Carmel to meet you at the station looks very much more like one to Miss Cumberland to meet you at the club-house."
10083{_}1085{_}It was thus I first learned which part of this letter had been burned off.
10083{_}1086{_}[1]  [Footnote :1 It was the top portion, leaving the rest to read:  _"Come, come my darling, my life.
10083{_}1087{_}She will forgive when all is done.
10083{_}1088{_}Hesitation will only undo us.
10083{_}1089{_}To-night at 10:30.
10083{_}1090{_}I shall never marry any one but you.
10083{_}1091{_}"_  It was also evident that I had failed to add those expressions of affection linked to Carmel's name which had been in my mind and awakened my keenest apprehension.]
10083{_}1092{_}"Otherwise," he pursued, "what could have taken her there?
10083{_}1093{_}Everybody who knew her will ask that.
10083{_}1094{_}Such a night!
10083{_}1095{_}so soon after seeing you!
10083{_}1096{_}It is a mystery any way, but one entirely inconceivable without some such excuse for her.
10083{_}1097{_}These lines said 'Come!'
10083{_}1098{_}and she went, for reasons which may be clear to you who were acquainted with her weak as well as strong points.
10083{_}1099{_}Went how?
10083{_}1100{_}No one knows.
10083{_}1101{_}By chance or by intention on her part or yours, every servant was out of the house by nine o'clock, and her brother, too.
10083{_}1102{_}Only the sister remained, the sister whom you profess to have urged to leave the town with you that very evening; and she can tell us nothing,--may die without ever being able to do so.
10083{_}1103{_}Some shock to her feelings--you may know its character and you may not--drove her from a state of apparent health into the wildest delirium in a few hours.
10083{_}1104{_}It was not your letter--if your story is true about that letter--or she would have shown its effect immediately upon receiving it; that is, in the early evening.
10083{_}1105{_}And she did not.
10083{_}1106{_}Helen, one of the maids, declares that she saw her some time after you left the house, and that she wore anything but a troubled look; that, in fact, her countenance was beaming and so beautiful that, accustomed as the girl was to her young mistress's good looks, she was more than struck by her appearance and spoke of it afterwards at the ball.
10083{_}1107{_}A telling circumstance against you, Ranelagh, not only contradicting your own story but showing that her after condition sprang from some sudden and extreme apprehension in connection with her sister.
10083{_}1108{_}Did you speak?"
10083{_}1109{_}No, I had not spoken.
10083{_}1110{_}I had nothing to say.
10083{_}1111{_}I was too deeply shaken by what he had just told me, to experience anything but the utmost confusion of ideas.
10083{_}1112{_}Carmel beaming and beautiful at an hour I had supposed her suffering and full of struggle!
10083{_}1113{_}I could not reconcile it with the letter she had written me, or with that understanding with her sister which ended so hideously in The Whispering Pines.
10083{_}1114{_}The lawyer, seeing my helpless state, proceeded with his presentation of my case as it looked to unprejudiced eyes.
10083{_}1115{_}"Miss Cumberland comes to the club-house; so do you.
10083{_}1116{_}You have not the keys and so go searching about the building till you find an unlocked window by which you both enter.
10083{_}1117{_}There are those who say you purposely left this window unfastened when you went about the house the day before; that you dropped the keys in her house where they would be sure to be found, and drove down to the station and stood about there for a good half hour, in order to divert suspicion from yourself afterwards and create an alibi in case it should be wanted.
10083{_}1118{_}I do not believe any of this myself, not since accepting your assurance of innocence, but there are those who do believe it firmly and discern in the whole affair a cool and premeditated murder.
10083{_}1119{_}Your passion for Carmel, while not generally known, has not passed unsuspected by your or her intimates; and this in itself is enough to give colour to these suspicions, even if you had not gone so far as to admit its power over you and the extremes to which you were willing to go to secure the wife you wished.
10083{_}1120{_}So much for the situation as it appears to outsiders.
10083{_}1121{_}Of the circumstantial evidence which links you personally to this crime, we have already spoken.
10083{_}1122{_}It is very strong and apparently unassailable.
10083{_}1123{_}But truth is truth, and if you only felt free to bare your whole soul to me as you now decline to do, I should not despair of finding some weak link in the chain which seems so satisfactory to the police and, I am forced to add, to the general public."
10083{_}1124{_}"Charles--"  I was very near unbosoming myself to him at that moment.
10083{_}1125{_}But I caught myself back in time.
10083{_}1126{_}While Carmel lay ill and unconscious, I would not clear my name at her expense by so much as a suggestion.
10083{_}1127{_}"Charles," I repeated, but in a different tone and with a different purpose, "how do they account for the cordial that was drunk--the two emptied glasses and the flask which were found in the adjacent closet?"
10083{_}1128{_}"It's one of the affair's conceded incongruities.
10083{_}1129{_}Miss Cumberland is a well-known temperance woman.
10083{_}1130{_}Had the flask and glasses not come from her house, you would get no one to believe that she had had anything to do with them.
10083{_}1131{_}Have you any hint to give on this point?
10083{_}1132{_}It would be a welcome addition to our case."
10083{_}1133{_}Alas!
10083{_}1134{_}I was as much puzzled by those emptied cordial glasses as he was, and told him so; also by the presence of the third unused one.
10083{_}1135{_}As I dwelt in thought on the latter circumstance, I remembered the observation which Coroner Perry had made concerning it.
10083{_}1136{_}"Coroner Perry speaks of a third and unused glass which was found with the flask," I ventured, tentatively.
10083{_}1137{_}"He seemed to consider it an important item, hiding some truth that would materially help this case.
10083{_}1138{_}What do you think, or rather, what is the general opinion on this point?"
10083{_}1139{_}"I have not heard.
10083{_}1140{_}I have seen the fact mentioned, but without comment.
10083{_}1141{_}It is a curious circumstance.
10083{_}1142{_}I will make a note of it.
10083{_}1143{_}You have no suggestions to offer on the subject?"
10083{_}1144{_}"None."
10083{_}1145{_}"The clew is a small one," he smiled.
10083{_}1146{_}"So is the one offered by the array of bottles found on the kitchen table; yet the latter may lead directly to the truth.
10083{_}1147{_}Adelaide never dug those out of the cellar where they were locked up, and I'm sure I did not.
10083{_}1148{_}Yet I suppose I'm given credit for doing so."
10083{_}1149{_}"Naturally.
10083{_}1150{_}The key to the wine-vault was the only key which was lacking from the bunch left at Miss Cumberland's.
10083{_}1151{_}That it was used to open the wine-vault door is evident from the fact that it was found in the lock."
10083{_}1152{_}This was discouraging.
10083{_}1153{_}Everything was against me.
10083{_}1154{_}If the whole affair had been planned with an intent to inculpate me and me only, it could not have been done with more attention to detail, nor could I have found myself more completely enmeshed.
10083{_}1155{_}Yet I knew, both from circumstances and my own instinct that no such planning had occurred.
10083{_}1156{_}I was a victim, not of malice but of blind chance, or shall I say of Providence?
10083{_}1157{_}As to this one key having been slipped from the rest and used to open the wine-vault for wine which nobody wanted and nobody drank--this must be classed with the other incongruities which might yet lead to my enlargement.
10083{_}1158{_}"You may add this coincidence to the other," I conceded, after I had gone thus far in my own mind.
10083{_}1159{_}"I swear that I had nothing to do with that key."
10083{_}1160{_}Neither could I believe that it had been used or even carried there by Adelaide or Carmel, though I knew that the full ring of keys had been in their hands and that they had entered the building by means of one of them.
10083{_}1161{_}So assured was I of their innocence in this regard that the idea which afterwards assumed such proportions in all our minds had, at this moment, its first dawning in mine, as well as its first outward expression.
10083{_}1162{_}"Some other man than myself was thirsty that night," I firmly declared.
10083{_}1163{_}"We are getting on, Charles."
10083{_}1164{_}Evidently he did not consider the pace a very fast one, but being a cheerful fellow by nature, he simply expressed his dissatisfaction by an imperceptible shrug.
10083{_}1165{_}"Do you know exactly what the club-house's wine-vault contained?"
10083{_}1166{_}he asked.
10083{_}1167{_}"An inventory was given me by the steward the morning we closed.
10083{_}1168{_}It must be in my rooms."
10083{_}1169{_}"Your rooms have been examined.
10083{_}1170{_}You expected that, didn't you?
10083{_}1171{_}Probably this inventory has been found.
10083{_}1172{_}I don't suppose it will help any."
10083{_}1173{_}"How should it?"
10083{_}1174{_}"Very true; how should it!
10083{_}1175{_}No thoroughfare there, of course."
10083{_}1176{_}"No thoroughfare anywhere to-day," I exclaimed.
10083{_}1177{_}"To-morrow some loop-hole of escape may suggest itself to me.
10083{_}1178{_}I should like to sleep on the matter.
10083{_}1179{_}I--I should like to sleep on it."
10083{_}1180{_}He saw that I had something in mind of which I had thus far given him no intimation, and he waited anxiously for me to reconsider my last words before he earnestly remarked:  "A day lost at a time like this is often a day never retrieved.
10083{_}1181{_}Think well before you bid me leave you, unenlightened as to the direction in which you wish me to work."
10083{_}1182{_}But I was not ready, not by any means ready, and he detected this when I next spoke.
10083{_}1183{_}"I will see you to-morrow; any time to-morrow; meantime I will give you a commission which you are at liberty to perform yourself or to entrust to some capable detective.
10083{_}1184{_}The letter, of which a portion remains, _was_ written to Carmel, and she sent me a reply which was handed me on the station platform by a man who was a perfect stranger to me.
10083{_}1185{_}I have hardly any memory of how the man looked, but it should be an easy task to find him and if you cannot do that, the smallest scrap of the note he gave me, and which unfortunately I tore up and scattered to the winds, would prove my veracity in this one particular and so make it easier for them to believe the rest."
10083{_}1186{_}His eye lightened.
10083{_}1187{_}I presume the prospect of making any practical attempt in my behalf was welcome.
10083{_}1188{_}"One thing more," I now added.
10083{_}1189{_}"My ring was missing from Miss Cumberland's hand when I took away those pillows.
10083{_}1190{_}I have reason to think--or it is natural for me to think--that she planned to return it to me by some messenger or in some letter.
10083{_}1191{_}Do you know if such messenger or such letter has been received at my apartments?
10083{_}1192{_}Have you heard anything about this ring?
10083{_}1193{_}It was a notable one and not to be confounded with any other.
10083{_}1194{_}Any one who knew us or who had ever remarked it on her hand would be able to identify it."
10083{_}1195{_}"I have heard the ring mentioned," he replied, "I have even heard that the police are interested in finding it; but I have not heard that they have been successful.
10083{_}1196{_}You encourage me much by assuring me that it was missing from her hand when you first saw her.
10083{_}1197{_}That ring may prove our most valuable clew."
10083{_}1198{_}"Yes, but you must also remember that she may have taken it off before she started for the club-house."
10083{_}1199{_}"That is very true."
10083{_}1200{_}"You do not know whether they have looked for it at her home?"
10083{_}1201{_}"I do not."
10083{_}1202{_}"Will you find out, and will you see that I get all my letters?"
10083{_}1203{_}"I certainly will, but you must not expect to receive the latter unopened."
10083{_}1204{_}"I suppose not."
10083{_}1205{_}I said this with more cheerfulness than he evidently expected.
10083{_}1206{_}My heart had been lightened of one load.
10083{_}1207{_}The ring had not been discovered on Carmel as I had secretly feared.
10083{_}1208{_}"I will take good care of your interests from now on," he remarked, in a tone much more natural than any he had before used.
10083{_}1209{_}"Be hopeful and show a brave front to the district attorney when he comes to interview you.
10083{_}1210{_}I hear that he is expected home to-morrow.
10083{_}1211{_}If you are innocent, you can face him and his whole office with calm assurance."
10083{_}1212{_}Which showed how little he understood my real position.
10083{_}1213{_}There was comfort in this very thought, however, and I quietly remarked that I did not despair.
10083{_}1214{_}"And I _will_ not," he emphasised, rising with an assumption of ease which left him as he remained hesitating before me.
10083{_}1215{_}It was my moment of advantage, and I improved it by proffering a request which had been more or less in my mind during the whole of this prolonged colloquy.
10083{_}1216{_}First thanking him for his disinterestedness, I remarked that he had shown me so much consideration as a lawyer, that I now felt emboldened to ask something from him as my friend.
10083{_}1217{_}"You are free," said I; "I am not.
10083{_}1218{_}Miss Cumberland will be buried before I leave these four walls.
10083{_}1219{_}I hate to think of her going to her grave without one token from the man to whom she has been only too good and who, whatever outrage he may have planned to her feelings, is not without reverence for her character and a heartfelt repentance for whatever he may have done to grieve her.
10083{_}1220{_}Charles, a few flowers,--white--no wreath, just a few which can be placed on her breast or in her hand.
10083{_}1221{_}You need not say whom they are from.
10083{_}1222{_}It would seem a mockery to any one but her.
10083{_}1223{_}Lilies, Charles.
10083{_}1224{_}I shall feel happier to know that they are there.
10083{_}1225{_}Will you do this for me?"
10083{_}1226{_}"I will."
10083{_}1227{_}"That is all."
10083{_}1228{_}Instinctively he held out his hand.
10083{_}1229{_}I dropped mine in it; there was a slight pressure, some few more murmured words and he was gone.
10083{_}1230{_}I slept that night.
10083{_}1231{_}VIII  A CHANCE!
10083{_}1232{_}I TAKE IT  I entreat you then From one that so imperfectly conjects, You'd take no notice; nor build yourself a trouble Out of his scattering and unsure observance: It were not for your quiet, nor your good, Nor for my manhood, honesty or wisdom, To let you know my thoughts.
10083{_}1233{_}_Othello_   I slept, though a question of no small importance was agitating my mind, demanding instant consideration and a definite answer before I again saw this friend and adviser.
10083{_}1234{_}I woke to ask if the suggestion which had come to me in our brief conversation about the bottles taken from the wine-vault, was the promising one it had then appeared, or only a fool's trick bound to end in disaster.
10083{_}1235{_}I weighed the matter in every conceivable way, and ended by trusting to the instinct which impelled me to have resource to the one and only means by which the scent might be diverted from its original course, confusion be sown in the minds of the police, and Carmel, as well as myself, be saved from the pit gaping to receive us.
10083{_}1236{_}This was my plan.
10083{_}1237{_}I would acknowledge to having seen a horse and cutter leave the club-house by the upper gateway, simultaneously with my entrance through the lower one.
10083{_}1238{_}I would even describe the appearance of the person driving this cutter.
10083{_}1239{_}No one by the greatest stretch of imagination would be apt to associate this description with Carmel; but it might set the authorities thinking, and if by any good chance a cutter containing a person wearing a derby hat and a coat with an extra high collar should have been seen on this portion of the road, or if, as I earnestly hoped, the snow had left any signs of another horse having been tethered in the clump of trees opposite the one where I had concealed my own, enough of the truth might be furnished to divide public opinion and start fresh inquiry.
10083{_}1240{_}That a woman's form had sought concealment under these masculine habiliments would not, could not, strike anybody's mind.
10083{_}1241{_}Nothing in the crime had suggested a woman's presence, much less a woman's active agency.
10083{_}1242{_}On the contrary, all the appearances, save such as I believed known to myself alone, spoke so openly of a man's strength, a man's methods, a man's appetite, and a man's brutal daring that the suspicion which had naturally fallen on myself as the one and only person implicated, would in shifting pass straight to another man, and, if he could not be found, return to me, or be lost in a maze of speculation.
10083{_}1243{_}This seemed so evident after a long and close study of the situation that I was ready with my confession when Mr. Clifton next came.
10083{_}1244{_}I had even forestalled it in a short interview forced upon me by the assistant district attorney and Chief Hudson.
10083{_}1245{_}That it had made an altogether greater impression upon the latter than I had expected, gave me additional courage when I came to discuss this new line of defence with the young lawyer.
10083{_}1246{_}I was even able to tell him that, to all appearance, my long silence on a point so favourable to my own interests had not militated against me to the extent one would expect from men so alive to the subterfuges and plausible inventions of suspected criminals.
10083{_}1247{_}"Chief Hudson believes me, late as my statement is.
10083{_}1248{_}I saw it in his eye."
10083{_}1249{_}Thus I went on.
10083{_}1250{_}"And the assistant district attorney, too.
10083{_}1251{_}At least, the latter is willing to give me the benefit of the doubt, which was more than I expected.
10083{_}1252{_}What do you suppose has happened?
10083{_}1253{_}Some new discovery on their part?
10083{_}1254{_}If so, I ought to know what it is.
10083{_}1255{_}Believe me, Charles, I ought to know what it is."

10083{_}1468{_}"Meanwhile, will you cast your eye over these fragments of a note which Mr. Ranelagh says he received from Miss Carmel Cumberland while waiting on the station platform for her coming."
10083{_}1469{_}Taking an envelope from his pocket, Mr. Clifton drew forth two small scraps of soiled and crumpled paper, one of which was the half of another envelope presenting very nearly the following appearance:  As he pointed this out, he remarked:  "Elwood is not so common a baptismal name, that there can be any doubt as to the person addressed."
10083{_}1470{_}The other scraps, also written in pencil and by the same hand, contained but two or three disconnected words; but one of those words was _Adelaide_.
10083{_}1471{_}"I spent an hour and a half in the yards adjoining the station before I found those two bits," explained the young lawyer with a simple earnestness not displeasing to the two seasoned men he addressed.
10083{_}1472{_}"One was in hiding under a stacked-up pile of outgoing freight, and the other I picked out of a cart of stuff which had been swept up in the early morning.
10083{_}1473{_}I offer them in corroboration of Mr. Ranelagh's statement that the '_Come!_' used in the partially consumed letter found in the clubhouse chimney was addressed to Miss Carmel Cumberland and not to Adelaide, and that the place of meeting suggested by this word was the station platform, and not the spot since made terrible by death."
10083{_}1474{_}"You are acquainted with Miss Carmel Cumberland's handwriting?"
10083{_}1475{_}"If I am not, the town is full of people who are.
10083{_}1476{_}I believe these words to have been written by Carmel Cumberland."
10083{_}1477{_}Mr. Fox placed the pieces back in their envelope and laid the whole carefully away.

10083{_}1479{_}"You can cancel the obligation," was the quick retort, "by discovering the identity of the man who in derby hat and a coat with a very high collar, left the grounds of The Whispering Pines just as Mr. Ranelagh drove into them.
10083{_}1480{_}I have no facilities for the job, and no desire to undertake it."

10083{_}1484{_}"The confronting of that man with Ranelagh will cause the latter to unseal his lips.
10083{_}1485{_}Before you have finished with my client, you will esteem him much more highly than you do now."
10083{_}1486{_}The district attorney smiled at what seemed the callow enthusiasm of a youthful lawyer; but the coroner who knew his district well, looked very thoughtfully down at the table before which he sat, and failed to raise his head until the young man had vanished from the room and his place had been taken by another of very different appearance and deportment.
10083{_}1487{_}Then he roused himself and introduced the newcomer to the prosecuting attorney as Caleb Sweetwater, of the New York police department.
10083{_}1488{_}Caleb Sweetwater was no beauty.
10083{_}1489{_}He was plain-featured to the point of ugliness; so plain-featured that not even his quick, whimsical smile could make his face agreeable to one who did not know his many valuable qualities.
10083{_}1490{_}His receding chin and far too projecting nose were not likely to create a favourable impression on one ignorant of his cheerful, modest, winsome disposition; and the district attorney, after eyeing him for a moment with ill-concealed disfavour, abruptly suggested:  "You have brought some credentials with you, I hope."
10083{_}1491{_}"Here is a letter from one of the department.
10083{_}1492{_}Mr. Gryce wrote it," he added, with just a touch of pride.
10083{_}1493{_}"The letter is all right," hastily remarked Dr. Perry on looking it over.
10083{_}1494{_}"Mr. Sweetwater is commended to us as a man of sagacity and becoming reserve."
10083{_}1495{_}"Very good.
10083{_}1496{_}To business, then.
10083{_}1497{_}The sooner we get to work on this new theory, the better.
10083{_}1498{_}Mr. Sweetwater, we have some doubts if the man we have in hand is the man we really want.
10083{_}1499{_}But first, how much do you know about this case?"
10083{_}1500{_}"All that's in the papers."
10083{_}1501{_}"Nothing more?"
10083{_}1502{_}"Very little.
10083{_}1503{_}I've not been in town above an hour."
10083{_}1504{_}"Are you known here?"
10083{_}1505{_}"I don't think so; it's my first visit this way."
10083{_}1506{_}"Then you are as ignorant of the people as they are of you.
10083{_}1507{_}Well, that has its disadvantages."
10083{_}1508{_}"And its advantages, if you will permit me to say so, sir.
10083{_}1509{_}I have no prejudices, no preconceived notions to struggle against.
10083{_}1510{_}I can take persons as I find them; and if there is any deep family secret to unearth, it's mighty fortunate for a man to have nothing stand in the way of his own instincts.
10083{_}1511{_}No likings, I mean--no leanings this way or that, for humane or other purely unprofessional reasons."
10083{_}1512{_}The eye of District Attorney Fox stole towards that of his brother official, but did not meet it.
10083{_}1513{_}The coroner had turned his attention to the table again, and, while betraying no embarrassment, was not quite his usual self.
10083{_}1514{_}The district attorney's hand stole to his chin, which he softly rubbed with his lean forefinger as he again addressed Sweetwater.
10083{_}1515{_}"This tragedy--the most lamentable which has ever occurred in this town--is really, and without exaggeration, a tragedy in high life.
10083{_}1516{_}The lady who was strangled by a brute's clutch, was a woman of the highest culture and most estimable character.
10083{_}1517{_}Her sister, who is supposed to have been the unconscious cause of the crime, is a young girl of blameless record.
10083{_}1518{_}Of the man who was seen bending over the victim with his hands on her throat, we cannot speak so well.
10083{_}1519{_}He has the faults and has lived the life of a social favourite.
10083{_}1520{_}Gifted in many ways, and popular with both men and women, he has swung on his course with an easy disregard of the claims of others, which, while leaving its traces no doubt in many a humble and uncomplaining heart, did not attract notice to his inherent lack of principle, until the horrors of this tragedy lifted him into public view stripped of all his charms.
10083{_}1521{_}He's an egotist, of the first water; there is no getting over that.
10083{_}1522{_}But did he strangle the woman?
10083{_}1523{_}He says not; that he was only following some extraordinary impulse of the moment in laying his thumbs on the marks he saw on Miss Cumberland's neck.
10083{_}1524{_}A fantastic story--told too late, besides, for perfect credence, and not worthy of the least attention if--"  The reasons which followed are too well known to us for repetition.
10083{_}1525{_}Sweetwater listened with snapping eyes to all that was said; and when he had been given the various clews indicating the presence of a third--and as yet unknown--party on the scene of crime, he rose excitedly to his feet and, declaring that it was a most promising case, begged permission to make his own investigations at The Whispering Pines, after which he would be quite ready to begin his search for the man in the derby hat and high coat-collar, whose love for wine was so great that he chose and carried off the two choicest bottles that the club-house contained.
10083{_}1526{_}"A hardy act for any man, gentleman or otherwise, who had just strangled the life out of a fine woman like that.
10083{_}1527{_}If he exists and the whole story is not a pure fabrication of the entrapped Ranelagh, he shouldn't be hard to find.
10083{_}1528{_}What do you say, gentlemen?
10083{_}1529{_}He shouldn't be hard to find."
10083{_}1530{_}"_We_ have not found him," emphasised the district attorney, with the shortest possible glance at the coroner's face.
10083{_}1531{_}"Then the field is all before me," smiled Sweetwater.
10083{_}1532{_}"Wish me luck, gentlemen.
10083{_}1533{_}It's a blind job, but that's just in my line.
10083{_}1534{_}A map of the town, a few general instructions, and I'm off."
10083{_}1535{_}Mr. Fox turned towards the coroner, and opened his lips; but closed them again without speaking.
10083{_}1536{_}Did Sweetwater notice this act of self-restraint?
10083{_}1537{_}If he did, he failed to show it.
10083{_}1538{_}X  "I CAN HELP YOU"  A subtle knave; a finder out of occasions; That has an eye can stamp and counterfeit Advantages though true advantage never presents Itself; A devilish knave!
10083{_}1539{_}_Othello_.
10083{_}1540{_}A half hour spent with Hexford in and about the club-house, and Sweetwater was ready for the road.
10083{_}1541{_}As he made his way through the northern gate, he cast a quick look back at the long, low building he had just left, with its tall chimneys and rows of sightless windows, half hidden, half revealed by the encroaching pines.
10083{_}1542{_}The mystery of the place fascinated him.
10083{_}1543{_}To his awakened imagination, there was a breathless suggestion in it--a suggestion which it was his foremost wish, just now, to understand.
10083{_}1544{_}And those pines--gaunt, restless, communicative!
10083{_}1545{_}ready with their secret, if one could only interpret their language.
10083{_}1546{_}How their heads came together as their garrulous tongues repeated the tale, which would never grow old to them until age nipped their hoary heads and laid them low in the dust, with their horror half expressed, their gruesome tale unfinished.
10083{_}1547{_}"Witnesses of it all," commented the young detective as he watched the swaying boughs rising and dipping before a certain window.
10083{_}1548{_}"They were peering into that room long before Clarke stole the glimpse which has undone the unfortunate Ranelagh.
10083{_}1549{_}If I had their knowledge, I'd do something more than whisper."
10083{_}1550{_}Thus musing, thus muttering, he plodded up the road, his insignificant figure an unpromising break in the monotonous white of the wintry landscape.
10083{_}1551{_}But could the prisoner who had indirectly speeded this young detective on his present course, have read his thoughts and rightly estimated the force of his purpose, would he have viewed with so much confidence the entrance of this unprepossessing stranger upon the no-thoroughfare into which his own carefully studied admissions had blindly sent him?
10083{_}1552{_}As has been said before, this road was an outlying one and but little travelled save in the height of summer.
10083{_}1553{_}Under ordinary circumstances Sweetwater would have met not more than a half-dozen carts or sledges between the club-house gates and the city streets.
10083{_}1554{_}But to-day, the road was full of teams carrying all sorts of incongruous people, eager for a sight of the spot made forever notorious by a mysterious crime.
10083{_}1555{_}He noted them all; the faces of the men, the gestures of the women; but he did not show any special interest till he came to that portion of the road where the long line of half-buried fences began to give way to a few scattered houses.
10083{_}1556{_}Then his spirit woke, and be became quick, alert, and persuasive.
10083{_}1557{_}He entered houses; he talked with the people.
10083{_}1558{_}Though evidently not a dissipated man, he stopped at several saloons, taking his time with his glass and encouraging the chatter of all who chose to meet his advances.
10083{_}1559{_}He was a natural talker and welcomed every topic, but his eye only sparkled at one.
10083{_}1560{_}This he never introduced himself; he did not need to.
10083{_}1561{_}Some one was always ready with the great theme; and once it was started, he did not let the conversation languish till every one present had given his or her quota of hearsay or opinion to the general fund.
10083{_}1562{_}It seemed a great waste of time, for nobody had anything to say worth the breath expended on it.
10083{_}1563{_}But Sweetwater showed no impatience, and proceeded to engage the attention of the next man, woman, or child he encountered with undiminished zest and hopefulness.
10083{_}1564{_}He had left the country road behind, and had entered upon the jumble of sheds, shops, and streets which marked the beginnings of the town in this direction, when his quick and experienced eye fell on a woman standing with uncovered head in an open doorway, peering up the street in anxious expectation of some one not yet in sight.
10083{_}1565{_}He liked the air and well-kept appearance of the woman; he appreciated the neatness of the house at her back and gauged at its proper value the interest she displayed in the expected arrival of one whom he hoped would delay that arrival long enough for him to get in the word which by this time dropped almost unconsciously from his lips.
10083{_}1566{_}But a second survey of the woman's face convinced him that his ordinary loquaciousness would not serve him here.
10083{_}1567{_}There was a refinement in her aspect quite out of keeping with the locality in which she lived, and he was hesitating how to proceed, when fortune favoured him by driving against his knees a small lad on an ill-directed sled, bringing him almost to the ground and upsetting the child who began to scream vociferously.
10083{_}1568{_}It was the woman's child, for she made instantly for the gate which, for some reason, she found difficulty in opening.
10083{_}1569{_}Sweetwater, seeing this, blessed his lucky stars.
10083{_}1570{_}He was at his best with children, and catching the little fellow up, he soothed and fondled him and finally brought him with such a merry air of triumph straight to his mother's arms, that confidence between them was immediately established and conversation started.
10083{_}1571{_}He had in his pocket an ingenious little invention which he had exhibited all along the road as an indispensable article in every well-kept house.
10083{_}1572{_}He wanted to show it to her, but it was too cold a day for her to stop outside.
10083{_}1573{_}Wouldn't she allow him to step in and explain how her work could be materially lessened and her labour turned to play by a contrivance so simple that a child could run it?
10083{_}1574{_}It was all so ridiculous in face of this woman's quiet intelligence, that he laughed at his own words, and this laughter, echoed by the child and in another instant by the mother, made everything so pleasant for the moment that she insensibly drew back while he pulled open the gate, only remarking, as she led the way in:  "I was looking for my husband.
10083{_}1575{_}He may come any minute and I'm afraid he won't care much about contrivances to save me work--that is, if they cost very much."
10083{_}1576{_}Sweetwater, whose hand was in his pocket, drew it hastily out.
10083{_}1577{_}"You were watching for your husband?
10083{_}1578{_}Do you often stand in the open doorway, looking for him?"
10083{_}1579{_}Her surprised eyes met his with a stare that would have embarrassed the most venturesome book agent, but this man was of another ilk.
10083{_}1580{_}"If you do," he went on imperturbably, but with a good-humoured smile which deepened her favourable impression of him, "how much I would give if you had been standing there last Tuesday night when a certain cutter and horse went by on its way up the hill."
10083{_}1581{_}She was a self-contained woman, this wife of a master mechanic in one of the great shops hard by; but her jaw fell at this, and she forgot to chide or resist her child when he began to pull her towards the open kitchen door.
10083{_}1582{_}Sweetwater, sensitive to the least change in the human face, prayed that the husband might be detained, if only for five minutes longer, while he, Sweetwater, worked this promising mine.
10083{_}1583{_}"You _were_ looking out," he ventured.
10083{_}1584{_}"And you _did_ see that horse and cutter.
10083{_}1585{_}What luck!
10083{_}1586{_}It may save a man's life."

10083{_}1588{_}she repeated, staggering back a few steps and dragging the child with her.
10083{_}1589{_}"Save a man's life!
10083{_}1590{_}What do you mean by that?"
10083{_}1591{_}"Not much if it was any cutter and any horse, and at any hour.
10083{_}1592{_}But if it was the horse and cutter which left The Whispering Pines at ten or half past ten that night, then it may mean life and death to the man now in jail under the dreadful charge of murder."
10083{_}1593{_}Catching up her child, she slid into the kitchen and sat down with it, in the first chair she came to.

10083{_}1595{_}The steaming kettles and the table set for dinner gave warning of the expected presence for which she had been watching, but she seemed to have forgotten her husband; forgotten everything but her own emotions.

10083{_}1671{_}XI  IN THE COACH HOUSE  All things that we ordained festival Turn from their office to black funeral; Our instruments to melancholy bells; Our wedding cheer to a sad burial feast; And all things change them to the contrary.

10083{_}1673{_}Fifteen minutes later, he stood in a finely wooded street before an open gateway guarded by a policeman.
10083{_}1674{_}Showing his badge, he passed in, and entered a long and slightly curved driveway.
10083{_}1675{_}As he did so, he took a glance at the house.
10083{_}1676{_}It was not as pretentious as he expected, but infinitely more inviting.
10083{_}1677{_}Low and rambling, covered with vines, and nestling amid shrubbery which even in winter gave it a habitable air, it looked as much the abode of comfort as of luxury, and gave--in outward appearance at least--no hint of the dark shadow which had so lately fallen across it.
10083{_}1678{_}The ceremonies had been set for three o'clock, and it was now half past two.
10083{_}1679{_}As Sweetwater reached the head of the driveway, he saw the first of a long file of carriages approaching up the street.
10083{_}1680{_}"Lucky that my business takes me to the stable," thought he.

10083{_}1683{_}Ah--Zadok!
10083{_}1684{_}Zadok Brown.

10083{_}1686{_}He had reached this point in his soliloquy (a bad habit of his, for it sometimes took audible expression) when he ran against another policeman set to guard the side door.
10083{_}1687{_}A moment's parley, and he left this man behind; but not before he had noted this door and the wide and hospitable verandah which separated it from the driveway.
10083{_}1688{_}"I am willing to go all odds that I shall find that verandah the most interesting part of the house," he remarked, in quiet conviction, to himself, as he noted its nearness to the stable and the ease with which one could step from it into a vehicle passing down the driveway.
10083{_}1689{_}It had another point of interest, or, rather the wing had to which it was attached.
10083{_}1690{_}As his eye travelled back across this wing, in his lively walk towards the stable, he caught a passing glimpse of a nurse's face and figure in one of its upper windows.
10083{_}1691{_}This located the sick chamber, and unconsciously he hushed his step and moved with the greatest caution, though he knew that this sickness was not one of the nerves, and that the loudest sound would fail to reach ears lapsed in a blessed, if alarming, unconsciousness.
10083{_}1692{_}Once around the corner, he resumed a more natural pace, and perceiving that the stable-door was closed but that a window well up the garden side was open, he cast a look towards the kitchen windows at his back, and, encountering no watchful eye, stepped up to the former one and peered in.
10083{_}1693{_}A man sat with his back to him, polishing a bit of harness.
10083{_}1694{_}This was probably Zadok, the coachman.
10083{_}1695{_}As his interest was less with him than with the stalls beyond, he let his eye travel on in their direction, when he suddenly experienced a momentary confusion by observing the head and shoulders of Hexford leaning towards him from an opposite window--in much the same fashion, and certainly with exactly the same intent, as himself.
10083{_}1696{_}As their glances crossed, both flushed and drew back, only to return again, each to his several peep-hole.
10083{_}1697{_}Neither meant to lose the advantage of the moment.
10083{_}1698{_}Both had heard of the grey horse and wished to identify it; Hexford for his own satisfaction, Sweetwater as the first link of the chain leading him into the mysterious course mapped out for him by fate.
10083{_}1699{_}That each was more or less under the surveillance of the other did not trouble either.
10083{_}1700{_}There were three stalls, and in each stall a horse stamped and fidgeted.
10083{_}1701{_}Only one held their attention.
10083{_}1702{_}This was a mare on the extreme left, a large grey animal with a curious black patch on its near shoulder.
10083{_}1703{_}The faces of both men changed as they recognised this distinguishing mark, and instinctively their eyes met across the width of the open space separating them.
10083{_}1704{_}Hexford's finger rose to his mouth, but Sweetwater needed no such hint.
10083{_}1705{_}He stood, silent as his own shadow, while the coachman rubbed away with less and less purpose, until his hands stood quite still and his whole figure drooped in irresistible despondency.
10083{_}1706{_}As he raised his face, moved perhaps by that sense of a watchful presence to which all of us are more or less susceptible, they were both surprised to see tears on it.
10083{_}1707{_}The next instant he had started to his feet and the bit of harness had rattled from his hands to the floor.
10083{_}1708{_}"Who are you?"
10083{_}1709{_}he asked, with a touch of anger, quite natural under the circumstances.
10083{_}1710{_}"Can't you come in by the door, and not creep sneaking up to take a man at disadvantage?"
10083{_}1711{_}As he spoke, he dashed away the tears with which his cheeks were still wet.
10083{_}1712{_}"I thought a heap of my young mistress," he added, in evident apology for this display of what such men call weakness.
10083{_}1713{_}"I didn't know that it was in me to cry for anything, but I find that I can cry for her."
10083{_}1714{_}Hexford left his window, and Sweetwater slid from his; next minute they met at the stable door.
10083{_}1715{_}"Had luck?"
10083{_}1716{_}whispered the local officer.

10083{_}1719{_}"To this stable."
10083{_}1720{_}"Have you heard that the horse was out that night?"
10083{_}1721{_}"Yes, she was out."
10083{_}1722{_}"Who driving?"
10083{_}1723{_}"Ah, that's the question!"
10083{_}1724{_}"This man can't tell you."
10083{_}1725{_}A jerk of Hexford's thumb in Zadok's direction emphasised this statement.

10083{_}1727{_}"He wasn't here that night; he was at a dance.
10083{_}1728{_}He only knows that the mare was out."
10083{_}1729{_}"But I'm going to talk to him."

10083{_}1731{_}I'll not interrupt.
10083{_}1732{_}I've just fifteen minutes to spare."
10083{_}1733{_}"You can do as you please.
10083{_}1734{_}I've nothing to hide--from you, at any rate."
10083{_}1735{_}Which wasn't quite true; but Sweetwater wasn't a stickler for truth, except in the statements he gave his superiors.
10083{_}1736{_}Hexford threw open the stable-door, and they both walked in.
10083{_}1737{_}The coachman was not visible, but they could hear him moving about above, grumbling to himself in none too encouraging a way.
10083{_}1738{_}Evidently he was in no mood for visitors.
10083{_}1739{_}"I'll be down in a minute," he called out, as their steps sounded on the hardwood floor.
10083{_}1740{_}Hexford sauntered over to the stalls.
10083{_}1741{_}Sweetwater stopped near the doorway and glanced very carefully about him.
10083{_}1742{_}Nothing seemed to escape his eye.
10083{_}1743{_}He even took the trouble to peer into a waste-bin, and was just on the point of lifting down a bit of broken bottle from an open cupboard when Brown appeared on the staircase, dressed in his Sunday coat and carrying a bunch of fresh, hot-house roses.
10083{_}1744{_}He stopped midway as Sweetwater turned towards him from the cupboard, but immediately resumed his descent and was ready with his reply when Hexford accosted him from the other end of the stable:  "An odd beast, this.
10083{_}1745{_}They don't drive her for her beauty, that's evident."

10083{_}1747{_}"Reason enough for overlooking her spots.

10083{_}1749{_}he grunted, with a drop of his lantern jaws, and a slight gesture towards the unknown interloper.

10083{_}1751{_}"We're both rather interested in this horse."
10083{_}1752{_}"Wouldn't another time do?"

10083{_}1758{_}She knows a lot, this mare.
10083{_}1759{_}I can see it in her eye.
10083{_}1760{_}I understand horses; we'll have a little chat, she and I, when you are gone."

10083{_}1765{_}"She does look knowing, don't she?
10083{_}1766{_}Would like to tell us something, perhaps.

10083{_}1780{_}"The old gal is telling me all about it," muttered this sly, adaptable fellow.
10083{_}1781{_}He had sidled up to the mare and their heads were certainly very close together.
10083{_}1782{_}"Not touch her?

10083{_}1784{_}Sweetwater had his arm round the filly's neck and was looking straight into her fiery and intelligent eye.

10083{_}1786{_}he asked, with a magnetic smile at the astonished coachman, which not only softened him but seemed to give the watchful Hexford quite a new idea of this gawky interloper.
10083{_}1787{_}"You'll oblige _me_ if you can put her knowledge into words," the man Zadok declared, with one fascinated eye on the horse and the other on the house where he evidently felt that his presence was wanted.
10083{_}1788{_}"She was out that night, and I know it, as any coachman would know, who doesn't come home stone drunk.
10083{_}1789{_}But where she was and who took her, get her to tell if you can, for I don't know no more 'n the dead."
10083{_}1790{_}"The dead!"
10083{_}1791{_}flashed out Sweetwater, wheeling suddenly about and pointing straight through the open stable-door towards the house where the young mistress the old servant mourned, lay in her funeral casket.
10083{_}1792{_}"Do you mean her--the lady who is about to be buried?
10083{_}1793{_}Could _she_ tell if her lips were not sealed by a murderer's hand?"
10083{_}1794{_}"She!"
10083{_}1795{_}The word came low and awesomely.
10083{_}1796{_}Rude and uncultured as the man was, he seemed to be strangely affected by this unexpected suggestion.
10083{_}1797{_}"I haven't the wit to answer that," said he.
10083{_}1798{_}"How can we tell what she knew.
10083{_}1799{_}The man who killed her is in jail.
10083{_}1800{_}_He_ might talk to some purpose.
10083{_}1801{_}Why don't you question him?"
10083{_}1802{_}"For a very good reason," replied Sweetwater, with an easy good-nature that was very reassuring.
10083{_}1803{_}"He was arrested on the spot; so that it wasn't he who drove this mare home, unharnessed her, put her back in her stall, locked the stable-door and hung up the key in its place in the kitchen.
10083{_}1804{_}Somebody else did _that_."
10083{_}1805{_}"That's true enough, and what does it show?
10083{_}1806{_}That the mare was out on some other errand than the one which ended in blood and murder," was the coachman's unexpected retort.
10083{_}1807{_}"Is that so?"

10083{_}1810{_}"She's keeping something back.
