10083{_}1812{_}he pointedly inquired, leaving the stalls and walking briskly up to Zadok.
10083{_}1813{_}The coachman frowned and hastily retreated a step; but in another moment he leaped in a rage upon Sweetwater, when the sight of the flowers he held recalled him to himself and he let his hand fall again with the quiet remark:  "You're overstepping your dooty.
10083{_}1814{_}I don't know who you are or what you want with me, but you're overstepping your dooty."
10083{_}1815{_}"He's right," muttered Hexford.
10083{_}1816{_}"Better let the fellow go.
10083{_}1817{_}See!
10083{_}1818{_}one of the maids is beckoning to him."
10083{_}1819{_}"He shall go, and welcome, if he will tell me where he gets his taste for this especial brand of whiskey."
10083{_}1820{_}Sweetwater had crossed to the cupboard and taken down the lower half of the broken bottle which had attracted his notice on his first entrance, and was now holding it out, with a quizzical look at the departing coachman.
10083{_}1821{_}Hexford was at his shoulder with a spring, and together they inspected the label still sticking to it--which was that of the very rare and expensive spirit found missing from the club-house vault.
10083{_}1822{_}"This is a find," muttered Hexford into his fellow detective's ear.
10083{_}1823{_}Then, with a quick move towards Zadok, he shouted out:  "You'd better answer that question.
10083{_}1824{_}Where did this bit of broken bottle come from?
10083{_}1825{_}They don't give you whiskey like this to drink."
10083{_}1826{_}"That they don't," muttered the coachman, not so much abashed as they had expected.
10083{_}1827{_}"And I wouldn't care for it if they did.
10083{_}1828{_}I found that bit of bottle in the ash-barrel outside, and fished it out to put varnish in.
10083{_}1829{_}I liked the shape."
10083{_}1830{_}"Broken this way?"
10083{_}1831{_}"Yes; it's just as good."
10083{_}1832{_}"Is it?
10083{_}1833{_}Well, never mind, run along.
10083{_}1834{_}We'll close the stable-door for you."
10083{_}1835{_}"I'd rather do it myself and carry in the key."
10083{_}1836{_}"Here then; we're going to the funeral, too.
10083{_}1837{_}You'd like to?"
10083{_}1838{_}This latter in a whisper to Sweetwater.
10083{_}1839{_}The answer was a fervent one.
10083{_}1840{_}Nothing in all the world would please this protean-natured man quite so well.
10083{_}1841{_}XII  "LILA--LILA!"
10083{_}1842{_}O, treble woe Fall ten times treble on that cursed head, Whose wicked deed thy most ingenious sense Depriv'd thee of!--Hold off the earth awhile, Till I have caught her once more in my arms.
10083{_}1843{_}_Hamlet_.
10083{_}1844{_}"Let us enter by the side door," suggested Sweetwater, as the two moved towards the house.
10083{_}1845{_}"And be sure you place me where I can see without being seen.
10083{_}1846{_}I have no wish to attract attention to myself, or to be identified with the police until the necessity is forced upon me."
10083{_}1847{_}"Then we won't go in together," decided Hexford.
10083{_}1848{_}"Find your own place; you won't have any difficulty.
10083{_}1849{_}A crowd isn't expected.
10083{_}1850{_}Miss Cumberland's condition forbids it."
10083{_}1851{_}Sweetwater nodded and slid in at the side door.
10083{_}1852{_}He found himself at once in a narrow hall, from the end of which opened a large room.
10083{_}1853{_}A few people were to be seen in this latter place, and his first instinct was to join them; but finding that a few minutes yet remained before the hour set for the services, he decided to improve them by a rapid glance about this hall, which, for certain reasons hardly as yet formulated in his own mind, had a peculiar interest for him.
10083{_}1854{_}The most important object within view, according to his present judgment, was the staircase which connected it with the floor above; but if you had asked his reason for this conclusion, he would not have told you, as Ranelagh might have done, that it was because it was the most direct and convenient approach to Carmel Cumberland's room.
10083{_}1855{_}His thoughts were far from this young girl, intimately connected as she was with this crime; which shows through what a blind maze he was insensibly working.
10083{_}1856{_}With his finger on the thread which had been put in his hand, he was feeling his way along inch by inch.
10083{_}1857{_}It had brought him to this staircase, and it led him next to a rack upon which hung several coats and a gentleman's hat.
10083{_}1858{_}He inspected the former and noted that one was finished with a high collar; but he passed the latter by--it was not a derby.
10083{_}1859{_}The table stood next the rack, and on its top lay nothing more interesting than a clothes-brush and one or two other insignificant objects; but, with his memory for details, he had recalled the keys which one of the maids had picked up somewhere about this house, and laid on a hall table.
10083{_}1860{_}If this were the hall and this the table, then was every inch of the latter's simple cloth-covered top of the greatest importance in his eyes.
10083{_}1861{_}He had no further time for even these cursory investigations; Hexford's step could be heard on the verandah, and Sweetwater was anxious to locate himself before the officer came in.
10083{_}1862{_}Entering the room before him, he crossed to the small group clustered in its further doorway.
10083{_}1863{_}There were several empty chairs in sight; but he passed around them all to a dark and inconspicuous corner, from which, without effort, he could take in every room on that floor--from the large parlour in which the casket stood, to the remotest region of the servants' hall.
10083{_}1864{_}The clergyman had not yet descended, and Sweetwater had time to observe the row of little girls sitting in front of the bearers, each with a small cluster of white flowers in her hand.
10083{_}1865{_}Miss Cumberland's Sunday-school class, he conjectured, and conjectured rightly.
10083{_}1866{_}He also perceived that some of these children loved her.
10083{_}1867{_}Near them sat a few relatives and friends.
10083{_}1868{_}Among these was a very, very old man, whom he afterwards heard was a great-uncle and a centenarian.
10083{_}1869{_}Between him and one of the little girls, there apparently existed a strong sympathy; for his hand reached out and drew her to him when the tears began to steal down her cheeks, and the looks which passed between the two had all the appeal and all the protection of a great love.
10083{_}1870{_}Sweetwater, who had many a soft spot in his breast, felt his heart warm at this one innocent display of natural feeling in an assemblage otherwise frozen by the horror of the occasion.
10083{_}1871{_}His eyes dwelt lingeringly on the child, and still more lingeringly on the old, old man, before passing to that heaped-up mound of flowers, under which lay a murdered body and a bruised heart.
10083{_}1872{_}He could not see the face, but the spectacle was sufficiently awe-compelling without that.
10083{_}1873{_}Would it have seemed yet more so, had he known at whose request the huge bunch of lilies had been placed over that silent heart?
10083{_}1874{_}The sister sick, the brother invisible, there was little more to hold his attention in this quarter; so he let it roam across the heads of the people about him, to the distant hall communicating with the kitchen.
10083{_}1875{_}Several persons were approaching from this direction, among them Zadok.
10083{_}1876{_}The servants of the house, no doubt, for they came in all together and sat down, side by side, in the chairs Sweetwater had so carefully passed by.
10083{_}1877{_}There were five persons in all: two men and three women.
10083{_}1878{_}Only two interested him--Zadok, with whom he had already made a superficial acquaintance and had had one bout; and a smart, bright-eyed girl with a resolute mouth softened by an insistent dimple, who struck him as possessing excellent sense and some natural cleverness.
10083{_}1879{_}A girl to know and a girl to talk to, was his instantaneous judgment.
10083{_}1880{_}Then he forgot everything but the solemnity of the occasion, for the clergyman had entered and taken his place, and a great hush had fallen upon the rooms and upon every heart there present.
10083{_}1881{_}"_I am the resurrection and the life_."
10083{_}1882{_}Never had these consoling words sounded more solemn than when they rang above the remains of Adelaide Cumberland, in this home where she had reigned as mistress ever since her seventeenth year.
10083{_}1883{_}The nature of the tragedy which had robbed the town of one of its most useful young women; the awful fate impending over its supposed author,--a man who had come and gone in these rooms with a spell of fascination to which many of those present had themselves succumbed--the brooding sense of illness, if not of impending death, in the room above; gave to these services a peculiar poignancy which in some breasts of greater susceptibility than the rest, took the form of a vague expectancy bordering on terror.
10083{_}1884{_}Sweetwater felt the poignancy, but did not suffer from the terror.
10083{_}1885{_}His attention had been attracted in a new direction, and he found himself watching, with anxious curiosity, the attitude and absorbed expression of a good-looking young man whom he was far from suspecting to be the secret representative of the present suspect, whom nobody could forget, yet whom nobody wished to remember at this hallowed hour.
10083{_}1886{_}Had this attitude and this absorption been directed towards the casket over which the clergyman's words rose and fell with ever increasing impressiveness, he might have noted the man but would scarcely have been held by him.
10083{_}1887{_}But this interest, sincere and strong as it undoubtedly was, centred not so much in the services, careful as he was to maintain a decorous attitude towards the same, but in the faint murmurs which now and then came down from above where unconsciousness reigned and the stricken brother watched over the delirious sister, with a concentration and abandonment to fear which made him oblivious of all other duties, and almost as unconscious of the rites then being held below over one who had been as a mother to him, as the sick girl herself with her ceaseless and importunate "Lila!
10083{_}1888{_}Lila!"
10083{_}1889{_}The detective, watching this preoccupied stranger, shared in some measure his secret emotions, and thus was prepared for the unexpected occurrence of a few minutes later.
10083{_}1890{_}No one else had the least forewarning of any break in the services.
10083{_}1891{_}There had been nothing in the subdued but impressive rendering of the prayers to foreshadow a dramatic episode; yet it came, and in this manner:  The final words had been said, and the friends present invited to look their last on the calm face which, to many there, had never worn so sweet a smile in life.
10083{_}1892{_}Some had hesitated; but most had obeyed the summons, among them Sweetwater.
10083{_}1893{_}But he had not much time in which to fix those features in his mind; for the little girls, who had been waiting patiently for this moment, now came forward; and he stepped aside to watch them as they filed by, dropping as they did so, a tribute of fragrant flowers upon the quiet breast.
10083{_}1894{_}They were followed by the servants, among whom Zadok had divided his roses.
10083{_}1895{_}As the last cluster fell from the coachman's trembling hand, the undertaker advanced with the lid, and, pausing a moment to be sure that all were satisfied, began to screw it on.
10083{_}1896{_}Suddenly there was a cry, and the crowd about the door leading into the main hall started back, as wild steps were heard on the stairs and a young man rushed into the room where the casket stood, and advanced upon the officiating clergyman and the astonished undertaker with a fierceness which was not without its suggestion of authority.
10083{_}1897{_}"Take it off!"
10083{_}1898{_}he cried, pointing at the lid which had just been fastened down.
10083{_}1899{_}"I have not seen her--I must see her.
10083{_}1900{_}Take it off!"
10083{_}1901{_}It was the brother, awake at last to the significance of the hour!
10083{_}1902{_}The clergyman, aghast at the sacrilegious look and tone of the intruder, stepped back, raising one arm in remonstrance, and instinctively shielding the casket with the other.
10083{_}1903{_}But the undertaker saw in the frenzied eye fixed upon his own, that which warned him to comply with the request thus harshly and peremptorily uttered.
10083{_}1904{_}Unscrewing the lid, he made way for the intruder, who, drawing near, pushed aside the roses which had fallen on the upturned face, and, laying his hand on the brow, muttered a few low words to himself.
10083{_}1905{_}Then he withdrew his hand, and without glancing to right or left, staggered back to the door amid a hush as unbroken as that which reigned behind him in that open casket.
10083{_}1906{_}Another moment and his white, haggard face and disordered figure would be blotted from sight by the door-jamb.
10083{_}1907{_}The minister recovered his poise and the bearers their breath; the men stirred in their seats and the women began to cast frightened looks at each other, and then at the children, some of whom had begun to whimper, when in an instant all were struck again into stone.
10083{_}1908{_}The young man had turned and was facing them all, with his hands held out in a clench which in itself was horrible.
10083{_}1909{_}"If they let the man go," he called out in loud and threatening tones, "I will strangle him with these two hands."
10083{_}1910{_}The word, and not the shriek which burst irrepressibly from more than one woman before him, brought him to himself.
10083{_}1911{_}With a ghastly look on his bloated features, he scanned for one moment the row of deeply shocked faces before him, then tottered back out of sight, and fled towards the staircase.
10083{_}1912{_}All thought that an end had come to the harrowing scene, and minister and people faced each other once more; when, loud and sharp from above, there rang down the shrill cry of delirium, this time in articulate words which even the children could understand:  "Break it open, I say!
10083{_}1913{_}break it open, and see if her heart is there!"
10083{_}1914{_}It was too awful.
10083{_}1915{_}Men and women and children leaped to their feet and dashed away into the streets, uttering smothered cries and wild ejaculations.
10083{_}1916{_}In vain the clergyman raised his voice and bade them respect the dead; the rooms were well-nigh empty before he had finished his appeal.
10083{_}1917{_}Only the very old uncle and the least of the children remained of all who had come there in memory of their departed kinswoman and friend.
10083{_}1918{_}The little one had fled to the old man's arms before he could rise, and was now held close to his aged and shaking knees, while he strove to comfort her and explain.
10083{_}1919{_}Soon these, too, were gone, and the casket was refastened and carried out by the shrinking bearers, leaving in those darkened rooms a trail of desolation which was only broken from time to time by the now faint and barely heard reiteration of the name of her who had just been borne away!
10083{_}1920{_}"Lila!
10083{_}1921{_}Lila!"
10083{_}1922{_}XIII  "WHAT WE WANT IS HERE"  I'll tell you, by the way, The greatest comfort in the world.
10083{_}1923{_}You said There was a clew to all.
10083{_}1924{_}Remember, Sweet, He said there was a clew!
10083{_}1925{_}I hold it.
10083{_}1926{_}Come!
10083{_}1927{_}_A Blot in the 'Scutcheon._   Sweetwater, however affected by this scene, had not lost control of himself or forgotten the claims of duty.
10083{_}1928{_}He noted at a glance that, while the candid looking stranger, whose lead he had been following, was as much surprised as the rest at the nature of the interruption--which he had possibly anticipated and for which he was in some measure prepared--he was, of all present, the most deeply and peculiarly impressed by it.
10083{_}1929{_}No element of fear had entered into his emotion; nor had it been heightened by any superstitious sense.
10083{_}1930{_}Something deeper and more important by far had darkened his thoughtful eye and caused that ebb and flow of colour in a cheek unused, if Sweetwater read the man aright, to such quick and forcible changes.
10083{_}1931{_}Sweetwater took occasion, likewise, while the excitement was at its height, to mark what effect had been made on the servants by the action and conduct of young Cumberland.
10083{_}1932{_}"They know him better than we do," was his inner comment; "what do they think of his words, and what do they think of him?"
10083{_}1933{_}It was not so easy to determine as the anxious detective might wish.
10083{_}1934{_}Only one of them showed a simple emotion, and that one was, without any possibility of doubt, the cook.
10083{_}1935{_}She was a Roman Catholic, and was simply horrified by the sacrilege of which she had been witness.
10083{_}1936{_}There was no mistaking her feelings.
10083{_}1937{_}But those of the other two women were more complex.
10083{_}1938{_}So were those of the men.
10083{_}1939{_}Zadok specially watched each movement of his young master with open mistrust; and very nearly started upright, in his repugnance and dismay, when that intruding hand fell on the peaceful brow of her over whose fate, to his own surprise, he had been able to shed tears.
10083{_}1940{_}Some personal prejudice lay back of this or some secret knowledge of the man from whose touch even the dead appeared to shrink.
10083{_}1941{_}And the women!
10083{_}1942{_}Might not the same explanation account for that curious droop of the eye with which the two younger clutched at each other's hands, to keep from screaming, and interchanged whispered words which Sweetwater would have given considerable out of his carefully cherished hoard to have heard.
10083{_}1943{_}It was impossible to tell, at present; but he was confident that it would not be long before he understood these latter, at least.
10083{_}1944{_}He had great confidence in his success with women, homely as he was.
10083{_}1945{_}He was not so sure of himself with men; and he felt that some difficulties and not a few pitfalls lay between him and, for instance, the uncommunicative Zadok.
10083{_}1946{_}"But I've the whole long evening before me," he added in quiet consolation to himself.
10083{_}1947{_}"It will be a pity if I can't work some of them in that time."
10083{_}1948{_}The last thing he had remarked, before Carmel's unearthly cry had sent the horrified guests in disorder from the house, was the presence of Dr. Perry in a small room which Sweetwater had supposed empty, until the astonishing events I have endeavoured to describe brought its occupant to the door.

10083{_}1950{_}Plans had been made for carrying the servants to the cemetery, and, despite the universal disturbance consequent upon these events, these plans were adhered to.
10083{_}1951{_}Sweetwater watched them all ride away in the last two carriages.

10083{_}1954{_}"Dr. Perry, Mr. Clifton, the lawyer, Mr. Cumberland, his sick sister, and the nurse."

10083{_}1988{_}The coroner turned quickly.

10083{_}1990{_}This was quite a different looking personage.

10083{_}2143{_}This reached the ear oblivious to all else.

10083{_}2154{_}Perfect beauty is so rare, its effect so magical!
10083{_}2155{_}Not even the bandage which swathed one cheek could hide the exquisite symmetry of the features, or take from the whole face its sweet and natural distinction.
10083{_}2156{_}Frenzy, which had distorted the muscles and lit the eyes with a baleful glare, was lacking at this moment.
10083{_}2157{_}Repose had quieted the soul and left the body free to express its natural harmonies.
10083{_}2158{_}Sweetwater gazed at the winsome, brown head over the nurse's shoulder, and felt that for him a new and important factor had entered into this case, with his recognition of this woman's great beauty.

10083{_}2160{_}"Excuse the intrusion," he said.
10083{_}2161{_}"We thought you might need these things.

10083{_}2174{_}Strength of mind and rigid attendance to duty dominated the kindness, however.
10083{_}2175{_}If crossed in what she considered best for her patient, possibly for herself, she could be severe, if not biting, in her speech and manner.

10083{_}2185{_}It was my fault; I opened the door just for an instant, and in that instant my patient broke through her torpor and spoke."

10083{_}2190{_}He was young and had not yet sunk the man entirely in the detective.

10083{_}2197{_}It was a unique specimen.
10083{_}2198{_}What it lacked in height--it could not have measured more than a foot from the bottom to the top--it made up in length, which must have exceeded five feet.
10083{_}2199{_}The doors, of which it had two, were both tightly locked; but as they were made of transparent glass, the objects behind them were quite visible.
10083{_}2200{_}It was the nature of these objects which made the mystery.
10083{_}2201{_}The longer Sweetwater examined them, the less he understood the reason for their collection, much less for their preservation in a room which in all other respects, expressed the quintessence of taste.
10083{_}2202{_}At one end he saw a stuffed canary, not perched on a twig, but lying prone on its side.
10083{_}2203{_}Near it was a doll, with scorched face and limbs half-consumed.
10083{_}2204{_}Next this, the broken pieces of a china bowl and what looked like the torn remnants of some very fine lace.
10083{_}2205{_}Further along, his eye lighted on a young girl's bonnet, exquisite in colour and nicety of material, but crushed out of all shape and only betraying its identity by its dangling strings.
10083{_}2206{_}The next article, in this long array of totally unhomogeneous objects, was a metronome, with its pendulum wrenched half off and one of its sides lacking.
10083{_}2207{_}He could not determine the character of what came next, and only gave a casual examination to the rest.

10083{_}2217{_}Sweetwater held his breath, and the nurse leaped towards her and gently encircled her with protecting arms.

10083{_}2219{_}Everything is all right: I am looking after things.

10083{_}2222{_}Break the glass and look in.

10083{_}2438{_}He was walking south and on the best lighted and most beautiful street in town, but his eyes were forever seeking a break in the long line of fence which marked off the grounds of a seemingly interminable stretch of neighbouring mansions, and when a corner was at last reached, he dashed around it and took a straight course for Huested Street, down which he passed with quickened steps and an air of growing assurance.
10083{_}2439{_}He was soon at the bottom of the hill where the street, taking a turn, plunged him at once into a thickly populated district.
10083{_}2440{_}As this was still the residence quarter, he passed on until he gained the heart of the town and the region of the saloons.

10083{_}2446{_}He carried another list, that of certain small groceries and quiet unobtrusive hotels where a man could find a private room in which to drink alone; it being Sweetwater's conviction that in such a place, and in such a place only, would be found the tokens of those solitary hours spent by Arthur Cumberland between the time of his sister's murder and his reappearance the next day.
10083{_}2447{_}"Had they been spent in his old haunts or in any of the well-known drinking saloons of the city, some one would have peached on him before this," he went on, in silent argument with himself.
10083{_}2448{_}"He's too well known, too much of a swell for all his lowering aspect and hang-dog look, to stroll along unnoticed through any of the principal streets, so soon after the news of his sister's murder had set the whole town agog.
10083{_}2449{_}Yet he was not seen till he struck Garden Street, a good quarter of a mile from his usual resorts."
10083{_}2450{_}Here, Sweetwater glanced up at the corner gas-lamp beneath which he stood, and seeing that he was in Garden Street, tried to locate himself in the exact spot where this young man had first been seen on the notable morning in question.
10083{_}2451{_}Then he looked carefully about him.

10083{_}2490{_}He reached a corner before coming to 62 and was still more interested to perceive that the street which branched off thus immediately from the markets was a wide and busy one, offering both a safe and easy approach to dealer and customer.

10083{_}2498{_}An alley ran down one side of the house to the stables, now locked but later to be thrown open for the use of the farmers who begin to gather here as early as four o'clock.

10083{_}2500{_}It was an unusual hour for guests, and the woman whom he saw bending over a sort of desk in one corner of the room he strode into, looked up hastily, almost suspiciously.

10083{_}2504{_}I'm in trouble I am; but I don't want to do any mischief; I only want to forget.
10083{_}2505{_}I've money, and--" as he saw her mouth open, "and I've the stuff.
10083{_}2506{_}Whiskey, just whiskey.
10083{_}2507{_}Give me a room.
10083{_}2508{_}I'll be quiet."
10083{_}2509{_}"I'll give you nothing."
10083{_}2510{_}She was hot, angry, and full of distrust.
10083{_}2511{_}"This house is not for such as you.
10083{_}2512{_}It's a farmer's lodging; honest men, who'd stare and go mad to see a feller like you about.
10083{_}2513{_}Go along, I tell you, or I'll call Jim.
10083{_}2514{_}He'll know what to do with you."
10083{_}2515{_}"Then, he'll know mor'n I do myself," mumbled the detective, with a crushed and discouraged air.
10083{_}2516{_}"Money and not a place to spend it in!
10083{_}2517{_}Why can't I go in there?"
10083{_}2518{_}he peevishly inquired with a tremulous gesture towards a half-open door through which a glimpse could be got of a neat little snuggery.
10083{_}2519{_}"Nobody'll see me.
10083{_}2520{_}Give me a glass and leave me till I rap for you in the morning.
10083{_}2521{_}That's worth a fiver.
10083{_}2522{_}Don't you think so, missus?--And we'll begin by passing over the fiver."
10083{_}2523{_}"No."
10083{_}2524{_}She was mighty peremptory and what was more, she was in a great hurry to get rid of him.
10083{_}2525{_}This haste and the anxious ear she turned towards the hall enlightened him as to the situation.
10083{_}2526{_}There was some one within hearing or liable to come within hearing, who possibly was not so stiff under temptation.
10083{_}2527{_}Could it be her husband?
10083{_}2528{_}If so, it might be worth his own while to await the good man's coming, if only he could manage to hold his own for the next few minutes.
10083{_}2529{_}Changing his tactics, he turned his back on the snuggery and surveyed the offended woman, with just a touch of maudlin sentiment.
10083{_}2530{_}"I say," he cried, just loud enough to attract the attention of any one within ear-shot.
10083{_}2531{_}"You're a mighty fine woman and the boss of this here establishment; that's evident.
10083{_}2532{_}I'd like to see the man who could say no to you.
10083{_}2533{_}He's never sat in that 'ere cashier's seat where you be; of that I'm dead sure.
10083{_}2534{_}He wouldn't care for fivers if you didn't, nor for tens either."
10083{_}2535{_}She was really a fine woman for her station, and a buxom, powerful one, too.
10083{_}2536{_}But her glance wavered under these words and she showed a desire, with difficulty suppressed, to use the strength of her white but brawny arms, in shoving him out of the house.
10083{_}2537{_}To aid her self-control, he, on his part, began to edge towards the door, always eyeing her and always speaking loudly in admirably acted tipsy unconsciousness of the fact.
10083{_}2538{_}"I'm a man who likes my own way as well as anybody," were the words with which he sought to save the situation, and further his own purposes.
10083{_}2539{_}"But I never quarrel with a woman.
10083{_}2540{_}Her whims are sacred to me.
10083{_}2541{_}I may not believe in them; they may cost me money and comfort; but I yield, I do, when they are as strong in their wishes as you be.
10083{_}2542{_}I'm going, missus --I'm going--Oh!"
10083{_}2543{_}The exclamation burst from him.
10083{_}2544{_}He could not help it.
10083{_}2545{_}The door behind him had opened, and a man stepped in, causing him so much astonishment that he forgot himself.
10083{_}2546{_}The woman was big, bigger than most women who rule the roost and do the work in haunts where work calls for muscle and a good head behind it.
10083{_}2547{_}She was also rosy and of a make to draw the eye, if not the heart.
10083{_}2548{_}But the man who now entered was small almost to the point of being a manikin, and more than that, he was weazen of face and ill-balanced on his two tiny, ridiculous legs.
10083{_}2549{_}Yet she trembled at his presence, and turned a shade paler as she uttered the feeble protest:  "Jim!"
10083{_}2550{_}"Is she making a fool of herself?"
10083{_}2551{_}asked the little man in a voice as shrill as it was weak.
10083{_}2552{_}"Do your business with me.
10083{_}2553{_}Women are no good."
10083{_}2554{_}And he stalked into the room as only little men can.
10083{_}2555{_}Sweetwater took out his ten; pointed to the snuggery, and tapped his breast-pocket.
10083{_}2556{_}"Whiskey here," he confided.
10083{_}2557{_}"Bring me a glass.
10083{_}2558{_}I don't mind your farmers.
10083{_}2559{_}They won't bother me.
10083{_}2560{_}What I want is a locked door and a still mouth in your head."
10083{_}2561{_}The last he whispered in the husband's ear as the wife crossed reluctantly back to her books.
10083{_}2562{_}The man turned the bill he had received, over and over in his hand; then scrutinised Sweetwater, with his first show of hesitation.
10083{_}2563{_}"You don't want to kill yourself?"
10083{_}2564{_}he asked.
10083{_}2565{_}Sweetwater laughed with a show of good humour that appeared to relieve the woman, if it did not the man.
10083{_}2566{_}"Oh, that's it," he cried.
10083{_}2567{_}"That's what the missus was afraid of, was it?
10083{_}2568{_}Well, I vow!
10083{_}2569{_}And ten thousand dollars to my credit in the bank!
10083{_}2570{_}No, I don't want to kill myself.
10083{_}2571{_}I just want to booze to my heart's content, with nobody by to count the glasses.
10083{_}2572{_}You've known such fellers before, and that cosey, little room over there has known them, too.
10083{_}2573{_}Just add me to the list; it won't harm you."
10083{_}2574{_}The man's hand closed on the bill.
10083{_}2575{_}Sweetwater noted the action out of the corner of his eye, but his direct glance was on the woman.
10083{_}2576{_}Her back was to him, but she had started as he mentioned the snuggery and made as if to turn; but thought better of it, and bent lower over her books.
10083{_}2577{_}"I've struck the spot," he murmured, exultantly to himself.
10083{_}2578{_}"This is the place I want and here I'll spend the night; but not to booze my wits away, oh, no."
10083{_}2579{_}Nevertheless it was a night virtually wasted.
10083{_}2580{_}He learned nothing more than what was revealed by that one slight movement on the part of the woman.
10083{_}2581{_}Though the man came in and sat with him for an hour, and they drank together out of the flask Sweetwater had brought with him, he was as impervious to all Sweetwater's wiles and as blind to every bait he threw out, as any man the young detective had ever had to do with.
10083{_}2582{_}When the door closed on him, and Sweetwater was left to sit out the tedious night alone, it was with small satisfaction to himself, and some regret for his sacrificed bill.
10083{_}2583{_}The driving in of the farmers and the awakening of life in the market, and all the stir it occasioned inside the house and out, prevented sleep even if he had been inclined that way.
10083{_}2584{_}He had to swallow his pill, and he did it with the best grace possible.
10083{_}2585{_}Sooner than was expected of him, sooner than was wise, perhaps, he was on his feet and peering out of the one small window this most dismal day room contained.
10083{_}2586{_}He had not mistaken the outlook.
10083{_}2587{_}It gave on to the alley, and all that was visible from behind the curtains where he stood, was the high brick wall of the neighbouring house.
10083{_}2588{_}This wall had not even a window in it; which in itself was a disappointment to one of his resources.
10083{_}2589{_}He turned back into the room, disgusted; then crept to the window again, and, softly raising the sash, cast one of his lightning glances up and down the alley.
10083{_}2590{_}Then he softly let the sash fall again and retreated to the centre of the room, where he stood for a moment with a growing smile of intelligence and hope on his face.
10083{_}2591{_}He had detected close against the side of the wall, a box or hand-cart full of empty bottles.
10083{_}2592{_}It gave him an idea.
10083{_}2593{_}With an impetuosity he would have criticised in another man, he flung himself out of the room in which he had been for so many hours confined, and coming face to face with the landlady standing in unexpected watch before the door, found it a strain on his nerves to instantly assume the sullen, vaguely abused air with which he had decided to leave the house.
10083{_}2594{_}Nevertheless, he made the attempt, and if he did not succeed to his own satisfaction, he evidently did to hers, for she made no effort to stop him as he stumbled out, and in her final look, which he managed with some address to intercept, he perceived nothing but relief.
10083{_}2595{_}What had been in her mind?
10083{_}2596{_}Fear for him or fear for themselves?
10083{_}2597{_}He could not decide until he had rummaged that cart of bottles.
10083{_}2598{_}But how was he to do this without attracting attention to himself in a way he still felt, to be undesirable.
10083{_}2599{_}In his indecision, he paused on the sidewalk and let his glances wander vaguely over the busy scene before him.
10083{_}2600{_}Before be knew it, his eye had left the market and travelled across the snow-covered fields to a building standing by itself in the far distance.
10083{_}2601{_}Its appearance was not unfamiliar.
10083{_}2602{_}Seizing hold of the first man who passed him, he pointed it out, crying:  "What building is that?"
10083{_}2603{_}"That?
10083{_}2604{_}That's The Whispering Pines, the country club-house, where--"  He didn't wait for the end of the sentence, but plunged into the thickest group of people he could find, with a determination greater than ever to turn those bottles over before he ate.
10083{_}2605{_}His manner of going about this was characteristic.
10083{_}2606{_}Lounging about the stalls until he found just the sort of old codger he wanted, he scraped up an acquaintance with him on the spot, and succeeded in making himself so agreeable that when the old fellow sauntered back to the stables to take a look at his horse, Sweetwater accompanied him.
10083{_}2607{_}Hanging round the stable-door, he kept up his chatter, while sizing up the bottles heaped in the cart at his side.
10083{_}2608{_}He even allowed himself to touch one or two in an absent way, and was meditating an accidental upset of the whole collection when a woman he had not seen before, thrust her head out of a rear window, shouting sharply:  "Leave those bottles alone.
10083{_}2609{_}They're waiting for the old clothes man.
10083{_}2610{_}He pays us money for them."
10083{_}2611{_}Sweetwater gaped and strolled away.
10083{_}2612{_}He had used his eyes to purpose, and was quite assured that the bottle he wanted was not there.
10083{_}2613{_}But the woman's words had given him his cue, and when later in the day a certain old Jew peddler went his rounds through this portion of the city, a disreputable-looking fellow accompanied him, whom even the sharp landlady in Cuthbert Road would have failed to recognise as the same man who had occupied the snuggery the night before.
10083{_}2614{_}He was many hours on the route and had many new experiences with human nature.
10083{_}2615{_}But he gained little else, and was considering with what words he should acknowledge his defeat at police headquarters, when he found himself again at the markets and a minute later in the alley where the cart stood, with the contents of which he had busied himself earlier in the day.
10083{_}2616{_}He had followed the peddler here because he had followed him to every other back door and alley.
10083{_}2617{_}But he was tired and had small interest in the cart which looked quite undisturbed and in exactly the same condition as when he turned his back upon it in the morning.
10083{_}2618{_}But when he drew nearer and began to lend a hand in removing the bottles to the waggon, he discovered that a bottle had been added to the pile, and that this bottle bore the label which marked it as being one of the two which had been taken from the club-house on the night of the murder.
10083{_}2619{_}XVII  "MUST I TELL THESE THINGS?"
10083{_}2620{_}Had I but died an hour before this chance, I had liv'd a blessed time; for from this instant, There's nothing serious in mortality: All is but toys; renown, and grace is dead; The wine of life is drawn, and the lees Is left this vault to brag of.
10083{_}2621{_}_Macbeth_.
10083{_}2622{_}The lamp in the coroner's room shone dully on the perturbed faces of three anxious men.
10083{_}2623{_}They had been talking earnestly and long, but were now impatiently awaiting the appearance of a fourth party, as was shown by the glances which each threw from time to time towards the door leading into the main corridor.
10083{_}2624{_}The district attorney courted the light, and sat where he would be the first seen by any one entering.
10083{_}2625{_}He had nothing to hide, being entirely engrossed in his duty.
10083{_}2626{_}Further back and rather behind the lamp than in front of it stood or sat, as his restlessness prompted, Coroner Perry, the old friend of Amasa Cumberland, with whose son he had now to do.
10083{_}2627{_}Behind him, and still further in the shadow, could be seen the quiet figure of Sweetwater.
10083{_}2628{_}All counted the minutes and all showed relief--the coroner by a loud sigh--when the door finally opened and an officer appeared, followed by the lounging form of Adelaide's brother.
10083{_}2629{_}Arthur Cumberland had come unwillingly, and his dissatisfaction did not improve his naturally heavy countenance.
10083{_}2630{_}However, he brightened a little at sight of the two men sitting at the table, and, advancing, broke into speech before either of the two officials had planned their questions.
10083{_}2631{_}"I call this hard," he burst forth.
10083{_}2632{_}"My place is at home and at the bedside of my suffering sister, and you drag me down here at nine o'clock at night to answer questions about things of which I am completely ignorant.
10083{_}2633{_}I've said all I have to say about the trouble which has come into my family; but if another repetition of the same things will help to convict that scoundrel who has broken up my home and made me the wretchedest dog alive, then I'm ready to talk.
10083{_}2634{_}So, fire ahead, Dr. Perry, and let's be done with it."
10083{_}2635{_}"Sit down," replied the district attorney, gravely, with a gesture of dismissal to the officer.
10083{_}2636{_}"Mr. Cumberland, we have spared you up to this time, for two very good reasons.
10083{_}2637{_}You were in great trouble, and you appeared to be in the possession of no testimony which would materially help us.
10083{_}2638{_}But matters have changed since you held conversation with Dr. Perry on the day following your sister's decease.
10083{_}2639{_}You have laid that sister away; the will which makes you an independent man for life has been read in your hearing; you are in as much ease of mind as you can be while your remaining sister's life hangs trembling in the balance; and, more important still, discoveries not made before the funeral, have been made since, rendering it very desirable for you to enter into particulars at this present moment, which were not thought necessary then."
10083{_}2640{_}"Particulars?
10083{_}2641{_}What particulars?
10083{_}2642{_}Don't you know enough, as it is, to hang the fellow?
10083{_}2643{_}Wasn't he seen with his fingers on Adelaide's throat?
10083{_}2644{_}What can I tell you that is any more damaging than that?
10083{_}2645{_}Particulars!"
10083{_}2646{_}The word seemed to irritate him beyond endurance.
10083{_}2647{_}Never had he looked more unprepossessing or a less likely subject for sympathy, than when he stumbled into the chair set for him by the district attorney.
10083{_}2648{_}"Arthur!"
10083{_}2649{_}The word had a subtle ring.
10083{_}2650{_}The coroner, who uttered it, waited to watch its effect.
10083{_}2651{_}Seemingly it had none, after the first sullen glance thrown him by the young man; and the coroner sighed again, but this time softly, and as a prelude to the following speech:  "We can understand," said he, "why you should feel so strongly against one who has divided the hearts of your sisters, and played with one, if not with both.
10083{_}2652{_}Few men could feel differently.
10083{_}2653{_}You have reason for your enmity and we excuse it; but you must not carry it to the point of open denunciation before the full evidence is in and the fact of murder settled beyond all dispute.
10083{_}2654{_}Whatever you may think, whatever we may think, it has not been so settled.
10083{_}2655{_}There are missing links still to be supplied, and this is why we have summoned you here and ask you to be patient and give the district attorney a little clearer account of what went on in your own house, before you broke up that evening and you went to your debauch, and your sister Adelaide to her death at The Whispering Pines."
10083{_}2656{_}"I don't know what you mean."
10083{_}2657{_}He brought his fist down on the table with each word.
10083{_}2658{_}"Nothing went on.
10083{_}2659{_}That is,--"  "Something went on at dinner-time.
10083{_}2660{_}It was not a usual meal," put in the district attorney.
10083{_}2661{_}"You and your sisters--"  "Stop!"
10083{_}2662{_}He was at that point of passion which dulls the most self-controlled to all sense of propriety.
10083{_}2663{_}"Don't talk to me about that dinner.
10083{_}2664{_}I want to forget that dinner.
10083{_}2665{_}I want to forget everything but the two things I live for--to see that fellow hanged, and to--" The words choked him, and he let his head fall, but presently threw it up again.
10083{_}2666{_}"That dastard, whom may God confound, passed a letter across Adelaide into Carmel's hand," he panted out.
10083{_}2667{_}"I saw him, but I didn't take it in; I wasn't thinking.
10083{_}2668{_}I was--"  "Who broke the glasses?"
10083{_}2669{_}urged his relentless inquisitor.
10083{_}2670{_}"One at your plate, one at Carmel's, and one at the head of the board where sat your sister Adelaide?"
10083{_}2671{_}"God!
10083{_}2672{_}Must I tell these things?"
10083{_}2673{_}He had started to his feet and his hand, violent in all it did, struck his forehead impulsively, as he uttered this exclamation.
10083{_}2674{_}"Have it, then!
10083{_}2675{_}Heaven knows I think of it enough not to be afraid to speak it out in words.
10083{_}2676{_}Adelaide"--the name came with passion, but once uttered, produced its own calming effect, so that he went on with more restraint--"Adelaide never had much patience with me.
10083{_}2677{_}She was a girl who only saw one way.
10083{_}2678{_}'The right!
10083{_}2679{_}the right!'
10083{_}2680{_}was what she dinned into my ears from the time I was a small boy and didn't know but that all youngsters were brought up by sisters.
10083{_}2681{_}I grew to hate what she called 'the right,' I wanted pleasure, a free time, and a good drink whenever the fancy took me.
10083{_}2682{_}You know what I am, Dr. Perry, and everybody in town knows; but the impulse which has always ruled me was not a downright evil one; or if it was, I called it natural independence, and let it go at that.
10083{_}2683{_}But Adelaide suffered.
10083{_}2684{_}I didn't understand it and I didn't care a fig for it, but she _did_ suffer.
10083{_}2685{_}God forgive me!"
10083{_}2686{_}He stopped and mopped his forehead.
10083{_}2687{_}Sweetwater moved a trifle on his seat, but the others--men who had passed the meridian of life, who had known temptations, possibly had succumbed to them, from time to time--sat like two statues, one in full light and the other in as dark a shadow as he could find.
10083{_}2688{_}"That afternoon," young Cumberland presently resumed, "she was keyed up more than usual.
10083{_}2689{_}She loved Ranelagh,--damn him!--and he had played or was playing her false.
10083{_}2690{_}She watched him with eyes that madden me, now, when I think of them.
10083{_}2691{_}She saw him look at Carmel, and she saw Carmel look at him.
10083{_}2692{_}Then her eyes fell on me.
10083{_}2693{_}I was angry; angry at them all, and I wanted a drink.
10083{_}2694{_}It was not her habit to have wine on the table; but sometimes, when Ranelagh was there, she did.
10083{_}2695{_}She was a slave to Ranelagh, and he could make her do whatever he wished, just as he can make you and everybody else."
10083{_}2696{_}Here he shot insolent glances at his two interlocutors, one of whom changed colour--which, happily, he did not see.
10083{_}2697{_}"'Ring the bell,' I ordered, 'and have in the champagne.
10083{_}2698{_}I want to drink to your marriage and the happy days in prospect for us all,' It was brutal and I knew it; but I was reckless and wild for the wine.
10083{_}2699{_}So, I guess, was Ranelagh, for he smiled at her, and she rang for the champagne.
10083{_}2700{_}When the glasses had been set beside each plate, she turned towards Carmel.
10083{_}2701{_}'We will all drink,' she said, 'to my coming marriage,' This made Carmel turn pale; for Adelaide had never been known to drink a drop of liquor in her life.
10083{_}2702{_}I felt a little queer, myself; and not one of us spoke till the glasses were filled and the maid had left the dining-room and shut the door.
10083{_}2703{_}"Then Adelaide rose.
10083{_}2704{_}'We will drink standing,' said she, and never had I seen her look as she did then.
10083{_}2705{_}I thought of my evil life when I should have been watching Ranelagh; and when she lifted the glass to her lips and looked at me, almost as earnestly as she did at Ranelagh,--but it was a different kind of earnestness,--I felt like--like--well, like the wretch I was and always had been; possibly, always will be.
10083{_}2706{_}She drank;--we wouldn't call it drinking, for she just touched the wine with her lips; but to her it was debauch.
10083{_}2707{_}Then she stood waiting, with the strangest gleam in her eyes, while Ranelagh drained his glass and I drained mine.
10083{_}2708{_}Ranelagh thought she wanted some sentiment, and started to say something appropriate; but his eye fell on Carmel, who had tried to drink and couldn't, and he bungled over his words and at last came to a pause under the steady stare of Adelaide's eyes.
10083{_}2709{_}"'Never mind, Elwood,' she said; 'I know what you would like to say.
10083{_}2710{_}But that's not what I am thinking of now.
10083{_}2711{_}I am thinking of my brother, the boy who will soon be left to find his way through life without even the unwelcome restraint of my presence.
10083{_}2712{_}I want him to remember this day.
10083{_}2713{_}I want him to remember me as I stand here before him with this glass in my hand.
10083{_}2714{_}You see wine in it, Arthur; but I see poison--poison--nothing else, for one like you who cannot refuse a friend, cannot refuse your own longing.
10083{_}2715{_}Never from this day on shall another bottle be opened under my roof.
10083{_}2716{_}Carmel, you have grieved as well as I over what has passed for pleasure in this house.
10083{_}2717{_}Do as I do, and may Arthur see and remember.'
10083{_}2718{_}"Her fingers opened; the glass fell from her hand, and lay in broken fragments beside her plate.
10083{_}2719{_}Carmel followed suit, and, before I knew it, my own fingers had opened, and my own glass lay in pieces on the table-cloth beneath me.
10083{_}2720{_}Only Ranelagh's hand remained steady.
10083{_}2721{_}He did not choose to please her, or he was planning his perfidy and had not caught her words or understood her action.
10083{_}2722{_}She held her breath, watching that hand; and I can hear the gasp yet with which she saw him set his glass down quietly on the board.
10083{_}2723{_}That's the story of those three broken glasses.
10083{_}2724{_}If she had not died that night, I should be laughing at them now; but she did die and I don't laugh!
10083{_}2725{_}I curse--curse her recreant lover, and sometimes myself!
10083{_}2726{_}Do you want anything more of me?
10083{_}2727{_}I'm eager to be gone, if you don't."
10083{_}2728{_}The district attorney sought out and lifted a paper from the others lying on the desk before him.
10083{_}2729{_}It was the first movement he had made since Cumberland began his tale.
10083{_}2730{_}"I'm sorry," said he, with a rapid examination of the paper in his hand, "but I shall have to detain you a few minutes longer.
10083{_}2731{_}What happened after the dinner?
10083{_}2732{_}Where did you go from the table?"
10083{_}2733{_}"I went to my room to smoke.
10083{_}2734{_}I was upset and thirsty as a fish."
10083{_}2735{_}"Have you liquor in your room?"
10083{_}2736{_}"Sometimes."
10083{_}2737{_}"Did you have any that night?"
10083{_}2738{_}"Not a drop.
10083{_}2739{_}I didn't dare.
10083{_}2740{_}I wanted that champagne bottle, but Adelaide had been too quick for me.
10083{_}2741{_}It was thrown out--wasted--I do believe, wasted."
10083{_}2742{_}"So you did not drink?
10083{_}2743{_}You only smoked in your room?"
10083{_}2744{_}"Smoked one cigar.
10083{_}2745{_}That was all.
10083{_}2746{_}Then I went down town."
10083{_}2747{_}His tone had grown sulky, the emotion which had buoyed him up till now, seemed suddenly to have left him.
10083{_}2748{_}With it went the fire from his eye, the quiver from his lip, and it is necessary to add, everything else calculated to awaken sympathy.
10083{_}2749{_}He was simply sullen now.
10083{_}2750{_}"May I ask by which door you left the house?"
10083{_}2751{_}"The side door--the one I always take."
10083{_}2752{_}"What overcoat did you wear?"
10083{_}2753{_}"I don't remember.
10083{_}2754{_}The first one I came to, I suppose."
10083{_}2755{_}"But you can surely tell what hat?"

10083{_}3043{_}"At ten o'clock."
10083{_}3044{_}XVIII  ON IT WAS WRITTEN--  Can this avail thee?
10083{_}3045{_}Look to it!
10083{_}3046{_}_Prometheus Bound_.
10083{_}3047{_}The district attorney was right; Sweetwater was not happy.
10083{_}3048{_}His night's rest had not benefited him.
10083{_}3049{_}He had seemed natural enough when he first appeared at the coroner's office in the early morning, and equally natural all through the lengthy conference which followed; but a half hour later, any one who knew him well,--any of his fellow detectives in New York; especially Mr. Gryce, who had almost fathered him since he came among them, a raw and inexperienced recruit--would have seen at first glance that his spirits were no longer at par, and that the cheer he displayed in manner and look was entirely assumed, and likely to disappear as soon as he found himself alone.
10083{_}3050{_}And it did so disappear.
10083{_}3051{_}When, at two o'clock, he entered the club-house grounds, it was without buoyancy or any of the natural animation with which he usually went about his work.
10083{_}3052{_}Each step seemed weighted with thought, or, at least, heavy with inner dissatisfaction.
10083{_}3053{_}But his eye was as keen as ever, and he began to use that eye from the moment he passed the gates.
10083{_}3054{_}What was in his mind?
10083{_}3055{_}Was he hunting for new clews, or was he merely seeking to establish the old?
10083{_}3056{_}The officers on guard knew him, by this time, and let him pass hither, thither, and where he would, unmolested.
10083{_}3057{_}He walked up and down the driveways, peering continuously at the well-trodden snow.
10083{_}3058{_}He studied the spaces between.
10083{_}3059{_}He sauntered to the rear, and looked out over the golf-links.
10083{_}3060{_}Then he began to study the ground in this direction, as he had already studied it in front.
10083{_}3061{_}The few mutterings which left his lips continued to speak of discontent.
10083{_}3062{_}"If I had only had Clarke's chance, or even Hexford's," was among his complaints.
10083{_}3063{_}"But what can I hope now?
10083{_}3064{_}The snow has been trampled till it is one solid cake of ice, to the very edge of the golf-links.
10083{_}3065{_}Beyond that, the distance is too great for minute inspection.
10083{_}3066{_}Yet it will have to be gone over, inch by inch, before I shall feel satisfied.
10083{_}3067{_}I must know how much of his story is to be believed, and how much of it we can safely set aside."
10083{_}3068{_}He ended by wandering down on the golf-links.
10083{_}3069{_}Taking out his watch, he satisfied himself that he had time for an experiment, and immediately started for Cuthbert Road.
10083{_}3070{_}An hour later, he came wandering back, on a different line.
10083{_}3071{_}He looked soured, disappointed.
10083{_}3072{_}When near the building again, he cast his eye over its rear, and gazed long and earnestly at the window which had been pointed out to him as the one from which a possible light had shone forth that night.
10083{_}3073{_}There were no trees on this side of the house--only vines.
10083{_}3074{_}But the vines were bare of leaves and offered no obstruction to his view.
10083{_}3075{_}"If there had been a light in that window, any one leaving this house by the rear would have seen it, unless he had been drunk or a fool," muttered Sweetwater, in contemptuous comment to himself.
10083{_}3076{_}"Arthur Cumberland's story is one lie.
10083{_}3077{_}I'll take the district attorney's suggestion and return to New York to-night.
10083{_}3078{_}My work's done here."
10083{_}3079{_}Yet he hung about the links for a long time, and finally ended by entering the house, and taking up his stand beneath the long, narrow window of the closet overlooking the golf-links.
10083{_}3080{_}With chin resting on his arms, he stared out over the sill and sought from the space before him, and from the intricacies of his own mind, the hint he lacked to make this present solution of the case satisfactory to all his instincts.
10083{_}3081{_}"Something is lacking."
10083{_}3082{_}Thus he blurted out after a look behind him into the adjoining room of death.
10083{_}3083{_}"I can't say what; nor can I explain my own unrest, or my disinclination to leave this spot.
10083{_}3084{_}The district attorney is satisfied, and so, I'm afraid is the coroner; but I'm not, and I feel as guilty--"  Here he threw open the window for air, and, thrusting his head out, glanced over the links, then aside at the pines, showing beyond the line of the house on the southern end, and then out of mere idleness, down at the ground beneath him.
10083{_}3085{_}"As guilty," he went on, "as Ranelagh appears to be, and some one really is.
10083{_}3086{_}I--"  Starting, he leaned farther out.
10083{_}3087{_}What was that he saw in the vines--not on the snow of the ground, but half way up in the tangle of small branches clinging close to the stone of the lower story, just beneath this window?
10083{_}3088{_}He would see.
10083{_}3089{_}Something that glistened, something that could only have got there by falling from this window.
10083{_}3090{_}Could he reach it?
10083{_}3091{_}No; he would have to climb up from below to do that.
10083{_}3092{_}Well, that was easy enough.
10083{_}3093{_}With the thought, he rushed from the room.
10083{_}3094{_}In another minute he was beneath that window; had climbed, pulled, pushed his way up; had found the little pocket of netted vines observable from above; had thrust in his fingers and worked a small object out; had looked at it, uttered an exclamation curious in its mixture of suppressed emotions, and let himself down again into the midst of the two or three men who had scented the adventure and hastened to be witnesses of its outcome.
10083{_}3095{_}"A phial!"
10083{_}3096{_}he exclaimed, "An empty phial, but--" Holding the little bottle up between his thumb and forefinger, he turned it slowly about until the label faced them.
10083{_}3097{_}On it was written one word, but it was a word which invariably carries alarm with it.
10083{_}3098{_}That word was: _Poison_.
10083{_}3099{_}Sweetwater did not return to New York that night.
10083{_}3100{_}XIX  "IT 'S NOT WHAT YOU WILL FIND"  I am not mad;--I would to heaven I were!
10083{_}3101{_}For then, 't is like I should forget myself: O, if I could, what grief should I forget!-- Preach some philosophy to make me mad, For being not mad, but sensible of grief, My reasonable part produces reason How I may be delivered of these woes.
10083{_}3102{_}_King John_.
10083{_}3103{_}"I regret to disturb you, Arthur; but my business is of great importance, and should be made known to you at once.
10083{_}3104{_}This I say as a friend.
10083{_}3105{_}I might have waited for the report to have reached you from hearsay, or through the evening papers; but I preferred to be the one to tell you.
10083{_}3106{_}You can understand why."
10083{_}3107{_}Sullen and unmollified, the young man thus addressed eyed, apprehensively, his father's old friend, placed so unfortunately in his regard, and morosely exclaimed:  "Out with it!
10083{_}3108{_}I'm a poor hand at guessing.
10083{_}3109{_}What has happened now?"
10083{_}3110{_}"A discovery.
10083{_}3111{_}A somewhat serious one I fear; at least, it will force the police to new action.
10083{_}3112{_}Your sister may not have died entirely from strangulation; other causes may have been at work!"
10083{_}3113{_}"Now, what do you mean by that?"
10083{_}3114{_}Arthur Cumberland was under his own roof and in presence of one who should have inspired his respect; but he made no effort to hide the fury which these words called up.
10083{_}3115{_}"I should like to know what deviltry is in your minds now.
10083{_}3116{_}Am I never to have peace?"
10083{_}3117{_}"Peace and tragedy do not often run together," came in the mild tones of his would-be friend.
10083{_}3118{_}"A great crime has taken place.
10083{_}3119{_}All the members of this family are involved--to say nothing of the man who lies, now, under the odium of suspicion, in our common county jail.
10083{_}3120{_}Peace can only come with the complete clearing up of this crime, and the punishment of the guilty.
10083{_}3121{_}But the clearing up must antedate the punishment.
10083{_}3122{_}Mr. Ranelagh's assertion that he found Miss Cumberland dead when he approached her, may not be, as so many now believe, the reckless denial of a criminal, disturbed in his act.
10083{_}3123{_}It may have had a basis in fact."
10083{_}3124{_}"I don't believe it.
10083{_}3125{_}Nothing will make me believe it," stormed the other, jumping up, and wildly pacing the drawing-room floor.
10083{_}3126{_}"It is all a scheme for saving the most popular man in society.
10083{_}3127{_}Society!
10083{_}3128{_}That for society!"
10083{_}3129{_}he shouted out, snapping his fingers.
10083{_}3130{_}"He is president of the club; the pet of women; the admired of all the dolts and gawks who are taken with his style, his easy laughter, and his knack at getting at men's hearts.
10083{_}3131{_}He won't laugh so easily when he's up before a jury for murder; and he'll never again fool women or bulldoze men, even if they are weak enough to acquit him of this crime.
10083{_}3132{_}Enough of the smirch will stick to prevent that.
10083{_}3133{_}If it doesn't, I'll--"  Again his hands went out in the horribly suggestive way they had done at his sister's funeral.
10083{_}3134{_}The coroner sat appalled,--confused, almost distracted between his doubts, his convictions, his sympathy for the man and his recoil from the passions he would be only too ready to pardon if he could feel quite sure of their real root and motive.
10083{_}3135{_}Cumberland may have felt the other's silence, or he may have realised the imprudence of his own fury; for he dropped his hands with an impatient sigh, and blurted out:  "But you haven't told me your discovery.
10083{_}3136{_}It seems to me it is a little late to make discoveries now."
10083{_}3137{_}"This was brought about by the persistence of Sweetwater.
10083{_}3138{_}He seems to have an instinct for things.
10083{_}3139{_}He was leaning out of the window at the rear of the clubhouse--the window of that small room where your sister's coat was found--and he saw, caught in the vines beneath, a--"  "Why don't you speak out?
10083{_}3140{_}I cannot tell what he found unless you name it."
10083{_}3141{_}"A little bottle--an apothecary's phial.
10083{_}3142{_}It was labelled 'Poison,' and it came from this house."
10083{_}3143{_}Arthur Cumberland reeled; then he caught himself up and stood, staring, with a very obvious intent of getting a grip on himself before he spoke.
10083{_}3144{_}The coroner waited, a slight flush deepening on his cheek.
10083{_}3145{_}"How do you know that phial came from this house?"
10083{_}3146{_}Dr. Perry looked up, astonished.
10083{_}3147{_}He was prepared for the most frantic ebullitions of wrath, for violence even; or for dull, stupid, blank silence.
10083{_}3148{_}But this calm, quiet questioning of fact took him by surprise.
10083{_}3149{_}He dropped his anxious look, and replied:  "It has been seen on the shelves by more than one of your servants.
10083{_}3150{_}Your sister kept it with her medicines, and the druggist with whom you deal remembers selling it some time ago to a member of your family."
10083{_}3151{_}"Which member?
10083{_}3152{_}I don't believe this story; I don't believe any of your--" He was fast verging on violence now.
10083{_}3153{_}"You will have to, Arthur.
10083{_}3154{_}Facts are facts, and we cannot go against them.
10083{_}3155{_}The person who bought it was yourself.
10083{_}3156{_}Perhaps you can recall the circumstance now."
10083{_}3157{_}"I cannot."
10083{_}3158{_}He did not seem to be quite master of himself.
10083{_}3159{_}"I don't know half the things I do; at least, I didn't use to.
10083{_}3160{_}But what are you coming to?
10083{_}3161{_}What's in your mind, and what are your intentions?
10083{_}3162{_}Something to shame us further, I've no doubt.
10083{_}3163{_}You're soft on Ranelagh and don't care how I feel, or how Carmel will feel when she comes to herself--poor girl.
10083{_}3164{_}Are you going to call it suicide?
10083{_}3165{_}You can't, with those marks on her throat."
10083{_}3166{_}"We're going to carry out our investigations to the full.
10083{_}3167{_}We're going to hold the autopsy, which we didn't think necessary before.
10083{_}3168{_}That's why I am here, Arthur.
10083{_}3169{_}I thought it your due to know our intentions in regard to this matter.
10083{_}3170{_}If you wish to be present, you have only to say so; if you do not, you may trust me to remember that she was your father's daughter, as well as my own highly esteemed friend."
10083{_}3171{_}Shaken to the core, the young man sat down amid innumerable tokens of the two near, if not dear, ones just mentioned; and for a moment had nothing to say.
10083{_}3172{_}Gone was his violence, gone his self-assertion, and his insolent, captious attitude towards his visitor.
10083{_}3173{_}The net had been drawn too tightly, or the blow fallen too heavily.
10083{_}3174{_}He was no longer a man struggling with his misery, but a boy on whom had fallen a man's responsibilities, sufferings, and cares.
10083{_}3175{_}"My duty is here," he said at last.
10083{_}3176{_}"I cannot leave Carmel."
10083{_}3177{_}"The autopsy will take place to-morrow.
10083{_}3178{_}How is Carmel to-day?"
10083{_}3179{_}"No better."
10083{_}3180{_}The words came with a shudder.
10083{_}3181{_}"Doctor, I've been a brute to you.
10083{_}3182{_}I am a brute!
10083{_}3183{_}I have misused my life and have no strength with which to meet trouble.
10083{_}3184{_}What you propose to do with--with Adelaide is horrible to me.
10083{_}3185{_}I didn't love her much while she was living; I broke her heart and shamed her, from morning till night, every day of her life; but good-for-nothing as I am and good-for-nothing as I've always been, if I could save her body this last humiliation, I would willingly die right here and now, and be done with it.
10083{_}3186{_}Must this autopsy take place?"
10083{_}3187{_}"It must."
10083{_}3188{_}"Then--" He raised his arm; the blood swept up, dyeing his cheeks, his brow, his very neck a vivid scarlet.
10083{_}3189{_}"Tell them to lock up every bottle the house holds, or I cannot answer for myself.
10083{_}3190{_}I should like to drink and drink till I knew nothing, cared for nothing, was a madman or a beast."
10083{_}3191{_}"You will not drink."
10083{_}3192{_}The coroner's voice rang deep; he was greatly moved.
10083{_}3193{_}"You will not drink, and you will come to the office at five o'clock to-morrow.
10083{_}3194{_}We may have only good news to impart.
10083{_}3195{_}We may find nothing to complicate the situation."
10083{_}3196{_}Arthur Cumberland shook his head.
10083{_}3197{_}"It's not what you will find--" said he, and stopped, biting his lips and looking down.
10083{_}3198{_}The coroner uttered a few words of consolation forced from him by the painfulness of the situation.
10083{_}3199{_}The young man did not seem to hear them.
10083{_}3200{_}The only sign of life he gave was to rush away the moment the coroner had taken his leave, and regain his seat within sight and hearing of his still unconscious sister.
10083{_}3201{_}As he did so, these words came to his ears through the door which separated them:  "Flowers--I smell flowers!
10083{_}3202{_}Lila, you always loved flowers; but I never saw your hands so full of them."
10083{_}3203{_}Arthur uttered a sharp cry; then, bowing his face upon his aims, he broke into sobs which shook the table where he sat.
10083{_}3204{_}Twenty-four hours later, in the coroner's office, sat an anxious group discussing the great case and the possible revelations awaiting them.
10083{_}3205{_}The district attorney, Mr. Clifton, the chief of police, and one or two others--among them Sweetwater--made up the group, and carried on the conversation.
10083{_}3206{_}Dr. Perry only was absent.
10083{_}3207{_}He had undertaken to make the autopsy and had been absent, for this purpose, several hours.
10083{_}3208{_}Five o'clock had struck, and they were momentarily looking for his reappearance; but, when the door opened, as it did at this time, it was to admit young Cumberland, whose white face and shaking limbs betrayed his suspense and nervous anxiety.
10083{_}3209{_}He was welcomed coldly, but not impolitely, and sat down in very much the same place he had occupied during his last visit, but in a very different, and much more quiet state of mind.
10083{_}3210{_}To Sweetwater, his aspect was one of despair, but be made no remark upon it; only kept all his senses alert for the coming moment, of so much importance to them all.
10083{_}3211{_}But even he failed to guess how important, until the door opened again, and the coroner appeared, looking not so much depressed as stunned.
10083{_}3212{_}Picking out Arthur from the group, he advanced towards him with some commonplace remark; but desisted suddenly and turned upon the others instead.
10083{_}3213{_}"I have finished the autopsy," said he.
10083{_}3214{_}"I knew just what poison the phial had held, and lost no time in my tests.
10083{_}3215{_}A minute portion of this drug, which is dangerous only in large quantities, was found in the stomach of the deceased; but not enough to cause serious trouble, and she died, as we had already decided, from the effect of the murderous clutch upon her throat.
10083{_}3216{_}But," he went on sternly, as young Cumberland moved, and showed signs of breaking in with one of his violent invectives against the supposed assassin, "I made another discovery of still greater purport.
10083{_}3217{_}When we lifted the body out of its resting-place, something beside withered flowers slid from her breast and fell at our feet.
10083{_}3218{_}The ring, gentlemen--the ring which Ranelagh says was missing from her hand when he came upon her, and which certainly was not on her finger when she was laid in the casket,--rolled to the floor when we moved her.
10083{_}3219{_}Here it is; there is one person here, at least, who can identify it.
10083{_}3220{_}But I do not ask that person to speak.
10083{_}3221{_}That we may well spare him."
10083{_}3222{_}He laid the ring on the table, not too near Arthur, not within reach of his hand, but close enough for him to see it.
10083{_}3223{_}Then he sat down, and hid his face in his hands.
10083{_}3224{_}The last few days had told on him.
10083{_}3225{_}He looked older, by ten years, than he had at the beginning of the month.
10083{_}3226{_}The silence which followed these words and this action, was memorable to everybody there concerned.
10083{_}3227{_}Some had seen, and all had heard of young Cumberland's desperate interruption of the funeral, and the way his hand had invaded the flowers which the children had cast in upon her breast.
10083{_}3228{_}As the picture, real or fancied, rose before their eyes, one man rose and left his place at the table; then another, and presently another.
10083{_}3229{_}Even Charles Clifton drew back.
10083{_}3230{_}The district attorney remained where he was, and so did young Cumberland.
10083{_}3231{_}The latter had reached out his hand, but he had not touched the ring, and he sat thus, frozen.
10083{_}3232{_}What went on in his heart, no man there could guess, and he did not enlighten them.
10083{_}3233{_}When at last he looked up, it was with a dazed air and an almost humble mien:  "Providence has me this time," he muttered.
10083{_}3234{_}"I don't understand these mysteries.
10083{_}3235{_}You will have to deal with them as you think best."
10083{_}3236{_}His eyes, still glued to the jewel, dilated and filled with fierce light as he said this.
10083{_}3237{_}"Damn the ring, and damn the man who gave it to her!
10083{_}3238{_}However it came into her casket, he's at the bottom of the business, just as he was at the bottom of her death.
10083{_}3239{_}If you think anything else, you will think a lie."
10083{_}3240{_}Turning away, he made for the door.
10083{_}3241{_}There was in his manner, desperation approaching to bravado, but no man made the least effort to detain him.
10083{_}3242{_}Not till he was well out of the room did any one move, then the district attorney raised his finger, and Arthur Cumberland did not ride back to his home alone.
10083{_}3243{_}BOOK THREE  HIDDEN SURPRISES     XX  "HE OR YOU!
10083{_}3244{_}THERE IS NO THIRD"  A heavy summons lies like lead upon me, And yet I would not sleep Merciful powers!
10083{_}3245{_}Restrain in me the cursed thoughts that nature Gives way to in repose.
10083{_}3246{_}_Macbeth_.
10083{_}3247{_}For several days I had been ill.
10083{_}3248{_}They were merciful days to me since I was far too weak for thought.
10083{_}3249{_}Then there came a period of conscious rest, then renewed interest in life and my own fate and reputation.
10083{_}3250{_}What had happened during this interval?
10083{_}3251{_}I had a confused memory of having seen Clifton's face at my bedside, but I was sure that no words had passed between us.
10083{_}3252{_}When would he come again?
10083{_}3253{_}When should I hear about Carmel, and whether she were yet alive, or mercifully dead, like her sister?
10083{_}3254{_}I might read the papers, but they had been carefully kept from me.
10083{_}3255{_}Not one was in sight.
10083{_}3256{_}The nurse would undoubtedly give me the information I desired, but, kind as she had been, I dreaded to consult a stranger about matters which involved my very existence and every remaining hope.
10083{_}3257{_}Yet I must know; for I could not help thinking, now, and I dreaded to think amiss and pile up misery for myself when I needed support and consolation.
10083{_}3258{_}I would risk one question, but no more.
10083{_}3259{_}I would ask about the inquest.
10083{_}3260{_}Had it been held?
10083{_}3261{_}If she said yes--ah, if she said yes!--I should know that Carmel was dead; and the news, coming thus, would kill me.
10083{_}3262{_}So I asked nothing, and was lying in a sufficiently feverish condition when the doctor came in, saw my state, and thinking to cheer me up, remarked blandly:  "You are well enough this morning to hear good news.

10083{_}3264{_}"I'm in the hospital, am I not?"
10083{_}3265{_}"Hardly.
10083{_}3266{_}You are in one of Mr. O'Hagen's own rooms."
10083{_}3267{_}(Mr. O'Hagen was the head keeper.)

10083{_}3307{_}"Yes.
10083{_}3308{_}What you feared has happened--No, no; Carmel is not dead.
10083{_}3309{_}Did you think I meant that?
10083{_}3310{_}Forgive me.
10083{_}3311{_}I should have remembered that you had other causes for anxiety than the one weighing on our minds.
10083{_}3312{_}She is holding her own--just holding it--but that is something, in one so young and naturally healthy."
10083{_}3313{_}I could see that I baffled him.
10083{_}3314{_}It could not be helped.
10083{_}3315{_}I did not dare to utter the question with which my whole soul was full.
10083{_}3316{_}I could only look my entreaty.
10083{_}3317{_}He misunderstood it, as was natural enough.
10083{_}3318{_}"She does not know yet what is in store for her," were his words; and I could only lie still, and look at him helplessly, and try not to show the despair that was sinking me deeper and deeper into semi-unconsciousness.
10083{_}3319{_}"When she comes to herself, she will have to be told; but you will be on your feet, then, and will be allowed, no doubt, to soften the blow for her by your comfort and counsel.
10083{_}3320{_}The fact that it must have been you, if not he--"   "_He!
10083{_}3321{_}"_ Did I shout it, or was the shout simply in my own mind?
10083{_}3322{_}I trembled as I rose on my elbow.
10083{_}3323{_}I searched his face in terror of my self-betrayal; but his showed only compassion and an eager desire to clear the air between us by telling me the exact facts.
10083{_}3324{_}"Yes--Arthur.
10083{_}3325{_}His guilt has not been proven; he has not even been remanded; the sister's case is too pitiful and Coroner Perry too soft-hearted, where any of that family is involved.
10083{_}3326{_}But no one doubts his guilt, and he does not deny it himself.
10083{_}3327{_}You know--probably no one better--that he cannot very consistently do this, in face of the evidence accumulated against him, evidence stronger in many regards, than that accumulated against yourself.
10083{_}3328{_}The ungrateful boy!
10083{_}3329{_}The--the--Pardon me, I don't often indulge in invectives against unhappy men who have their punishment before them, but I was thinking of you and what you have suffered in this jail, where you have not belonged--no, not for a day."
10083{_}3330{_}"Don't think of me."
10083{_}3331{_}The words came with a gasp.
10083{_}3332{_}I was never so hard put to it--not when I first realised that I had been seen with my fingers on Adelaide's throat.
10083{_}3333{_}Arthur!
10083{_}3334{_}A booby and a boor, but certainly not the slayer of his sister, unless I had been woefully mistaken in all that had taken place in that club-house previous to my entrance into it on that fatal night.
10083{_}3335{_}As I caught Clifton's eye fixed upon me, I repeated--though with more self-control, I hope: "Don't think of me.
10083{_}3336{_}I'm not thinking of myself.
10083{_}3337{_}You speak of evidence.
10083{_}3338{_}What evidence?
10083{_}3339{_}Give me details.
10083{_}3340{_}Don't you see that I am burning with curiosity?
10083{_}3341{_}I shan't be myself till I hear."
10083{_}3342{_}This alarmed him.
10083{_}3343{_}"It's a risk," said he.
10083{_}3344{_}"The doctor told me to be careful not to excite you too much.
10083{_}3345{_}But suspense is always more intolerable than certainty, and you have heard too much to be left in ignorance of the rest."
10083{_}3346{_}"Yes, yes," I agreed feverishly, pressing his hand.
10083{_}3347{_}"It all came about through you," he blundered on.
10083{_}3348{_}"You told me of the fellow you saw riding away from The Whispering Pines at the time you entered the grounds.
10083{_}3349{_}I passed the story on to the coroner, and he to a New York detective they have put on this case.
10083{_}3350{_}He and Arthur's own surly nature did the rest."
10083{_}3351{_}I cringed where I lay.
10083{_}3352{_}This was my work.
10083{_}3353{_}The person who drove out of the club-house grounds while I stood in the club-house hall was Carmel--and the clew I had given, instead of baffling and confusing them, had led directly to Arthur!
10083{_}3354{_}Seeing nothing peculiar--or at all events, giving no evidence of having noted anything peculiar in my movement--Clifton went evenly on, pouring into my astonished ears the whole long story of this detective's investigations.
10083{_}3355{_}I heard of his visit at the mechanic's cottage and of the identification of the hat marked by Eliza Simmons's floury thumb, with an old one of Arthur's, fished out from one of the Cumberland closets; then, as I lay dumb, in my secret dismay and perturbation, of Arthur's acknowledged visit to the club-house, and his abstraction of the bottles, which to all minds save my own, perhaps, connected him directly and well-nigh unmistakably, with the crime.
10083{_}3356{_}"The finger of God!
10083{_}3357{_}Nothing else.
10083{_}3358{_}Such coincidences cannot be natural," was my thought.
10083{_}3359{_}And I braced myself to meet the further disclosures I saw awaiting me.
10083{_}3360{_}But when these disclosures were made, and Arthur's conduct at the funeral was given its natural explanation by the finding of the tell-tale ring in Adelaide's casket, I was so affected, both by the extraordinary nature of the facts and the doubtful position in which they seemed to place one whom, even now, I found it difficult to believe guilty of Adelaide's death, that Clifton, aroused, in spite of his own excitement, to a sudden realisation of my condition, bounded to his feet and impetuously cried out:  "I had to tell you.
10083{_}3361{_}It was your due and you would not have been satisfied if I had not.
10083{_}3362{_}But I fear that I rushed my narrative too suddenly upon you; that you needed more preparation, and that the greatest kindness I can show you now, is to leave before I do further mischief."
10083{_}3363{_}I believe I answered.
10083{_}3364{_}I know that his idea of leaving was insupportable to me.
10083{_}3365{_}That I wanted him to stay until I had had time to think and adjust myself to these new conditions.
10083{_}3366{_}Instinctively, I did not feel as certain of Arthur's guilt as he did.
10083{_}3367{_}My own case had taught me the insufficiency of circumstantial evidence to settle a mooted fact.
10083{_}3368{_}Besides, I knew Arthur even better than I did his sisters.
10083{_}3369{_}He was as full of faults, and as lacking in amiable and reliable traits as any fellow of my acquaintance.
10083{_}3370{_}But he had not the inherent snap which makes for crime.
