10083{_}4057{_}I was anxious to know what I had to expect from them, in case my conscience got the better of my devotion to Carmel's interests and led me into that declaration of the real facts which was forever faltering on my tongue, without having, as yet, received the final impetus which could only end in speech.
10083{_}4058{_}To give him his rightful precedence, the judge showed an impenetrable countenance but little changed from that with which he had faced us all from the start.
10083{_}4059{_}He, like most of the men involved in these proceedings, had been a close friend of the prisoner's father, and, in his capacity of judge in this momentous trial, had had to contend with his personal predilections, possibly with concealed sympathies, if not with equally well-concealed prejudices.
10083{_}4060{_}This had lent to his aspect a sternness never observable in it before; but no man, even the captious Mr. Moffat, had seriously questioned his rulings; and, whatever the cost to himself, he had, up to this time, held the scales of justice so evenly that it would have taken an audacious mind to have ventured on an interpretation of his real attitude or mental leaning in this case.
10083{_}4061{_}From this imposing presence, nobly sustained by a well-proportioned figure and a head and face indicative of intellect and every kindly attribute, I turned to gaze upon Mr. Fox and his colleagues.
10083{_}4062{_}One spirit seemed to animate them--confidence in their case, and unqualified satisfaction at its present status.
10083{_}4063{_}I was conscious of a certain ironic impulse to smile, as I noted the eager whisper and the bustle of preparation with which they settled upon their next witness and prepared to open their batteries upon him.
10083{_}4064{_}How easily I could call down that high look, and into what a turmoil I could throw them all by an ingenuous demand to be recalled to the stand!
10083{_}4065{_}But the psychological moment had not yet come, and I subdued the momentary impulse and proceeded with my scrutiny of the people about me.
10083{_}4066{_}The jury looked tired, with the exception of one especially alert little man who drank in even the most uninteresting details with avidity.
10083{_}4067{_}But they all had good faces, and none could doubt their interest, or that they were fully alive to the significance of the occasion.
10083{_}4068{_}Mr. Moffat, leading counsel for the defendant, was a spare man of unusual height, modified a little, and only a little, by the forward droop of his shoulders.
10083{_}4069{_}Nervous in manner, quick, short, sometimes rasping in speech, he had the changeful eye and mobile expression of a very sensitive nature; and from him, if from any one, I might hope to learn how much or how little Arthur had to fear from the day's proceedings.
10083{_}4070{_}But Mr. Moffat's countenance was not as readable as usual.
10083{_}4071{_}He looked preoccupied--a strange thing for him; and, instead of keeping his eye on the witness, as was his habitual practice, he allowed it to wander over the sea of heads before him, with a curious expectant interest which aroused my own curiosity, and led me to hunt about for its cause.
10083{_}4072{_}My first glance was unproductive.
10083{_}4073{_}I saw only the usual public, such as had confronted us the whole week, with curious and increasing interest.
10083{_}4074{_}But as I searched further, I discerned in an inconspicuous corner, the bowed head, veiled almost beyond recognition, of Ella Fulton.
10083{_}4075{_}It was her first appearance in court.
10083{_}4076{_}Each day I had anticipated her presence, and each day I had failed to see my anticipations realised.
10083{_}4077{_}But she was here now, and so were her father and her cold and dominating mother; and, beholding her thus accompanied, I fancied I understood Mr. Moffat's poorly concealed excitement.
10083{_}4078{_}But another glance at Mrs. Fulton assured me that I was mistaken in this hasty surmise.
10083{_}4079{_}No such serious purpose, as I feared, lay back of their presence here to-day.
10083{_}4080{_}Curiosity alone explained it; and as I realised what this meant, and how little understanding it betokened of the fierce struggle then going on in the timid breast of their distracted child, a sickening sense of my own responsibility drove Carmel's beauty, and Carmel's claims temporarily from my mind, and following the direction of Ella's thoughts, if not her glances, I sought in the face of the prisoner a recognition of her presence, if not of the promise this presence brought him.
10083{_}4081{_}His eye had just fallen on her.
10083{_}4082{_}I was assured of this by the sudden softening of his expression--the first real softening I had ever seen in it.
10083{_}4083{_}It was but a momentary flash, but it was unmistakable in its character, as was his speedy return to his former stolidity.
10083{_}4084{_}Whatever his thoughts were at sight of his little sweetheart, he meant to hide them even from his counsel--most of all from his counsel, I decided after further contemplation of them both.
10083{_}4085{_}If Mr. Moffat still showed nervousness, it was for some other reason than anxiety about this little body hiding from sight behind the proudly held figures of father and mother.
10083{_}4086{_}The opening testimony of the day, while not vital, was favourable to the prosecution in that it showed Arthur's conduct since the murder to have been inconsistent with perfect innocence.
10083{_}4087{_}His belated return at noon the next day, raging against the man who had been found in an incriminating position on the scene of crime, while at the same time failing to betray his own presence there till driven to it by accumulating circumstances and the persistent inquiries of the police; the care he took to avoid drink, though constant tippling was habitual to him and formed the great cause of quarrel between himself and the murdered Adelaide; his haunting of Carmel's door and anxious listening for any words she might let fall in her delirium; the suspicion which he constantly betrayed of the nurse when for any reason he was led to conclude that she had heard something which he had not; his behaviour at the funeral and finally his action in demanding to have the casket-lid removed that he might look again at the face he had made no effort to gaze upon when opportunity offered and time and place were seemly: these facts and many more were brought forward in grim array against the prisoner, with but little opposition from his counsel and small betrayal of feeling on the part of Arthur himself.
10083{_}4088{_}His stolid face had remained stolid even when the ring which had fallen out of his sister's casket was shown to the jury and the connection made between its presence there and the intrusion of his hand into the same, on the occasion above mentioned.
10083{_}4089{_}This once thoughtless, pleasure-loving, and hopelessly dissipated boy had not miscalculated his nerve.
10083{_}4090{_}It was sufficient for an ordeal which might have tried the courage and self-possession of the most hardened criminal.
10083{_}4091{_}Then came the great event of the day, in anticipation of which the court-room had been packed, and every heart within it awakened by slow degrees to a state of great nervous expectancy.
10083{_}4092{_}The prosecution rested and the junior counsel for the defence opened his case to the jury.
10083{_}4093{_}If I had hoped for any startling disclosure, calculated to establish his client's alleged alibi, or otherwise to free the same from the definite charge of murder, I had reason to be greatly disappointed by this maiden effort of a young and inexperienced lawyer.
10083{_}4094{_}If not exactly weak, there was an unexpected vagueness in its statements which seemed quite out of keeping with the emphatic declaration which he made of the prisoner's innocence.
10083{_}4095{_}Even Arthur was sensible of the bad effect made by this preliminary address.
10083{_}4096{_}More than once during its delivery and notably at its conclusion, he turned to Mr. Moffat, with a bitter remark, which was not without effect on that gentleman's cheek, and at once called forth a retort stinging enough to cause Arthur to sink back into his place, with the first sign of restlessness I had observed in him.
10083{_}4097{_}"Moffat is sly.
10083{_}4098{_}Moffat has something up his sleeve.
10083{_}4099{_}I will wait till he sees fit to show it," was my thought; then, as I caught a wild and pleading look from Ella, I added in positive assertion to myself, "And so must she."
10083{_}4100{_}Answering her unspoken appeal with an admonitory shake of the head, I carelessly let my fingers rest upon my mouth until I saw that she understood me and was prepared to follow my lead for a little while longer.
10083{_}4101{_}My satisfaction at this was curtailed by the calling of Arthur Cumberland to the stand to witness in his own defence.
10083{_}4102{_}I had dreaded this contingency.
10083{_}4103{_}I saw that for some reason, both his counsel and associate counsel, were not without their own misgivings as to the result of their somewhat doubtful experiment.
10083{_}4104{_}A change was observable in this degenerate son of the Cumberlands since many there had confronted him face to face.
10083{_}4105{_}Physically he was improved.
10083{_}4106{_}Enough time had elapsed since his sudden dropping of old habits, for him to have risen above its first effects and to have acquired that tone of personal dignity which follows a successful issue to any moral conflict.
10083{_}4107{_}But otherwise the difference was such as to arouse doubt as to the real man lurking behind his dogged, uncommunicative manner.
10083{_}4108{_}Even with the knowledge of his motives which I believed myself to possess, I was at a loss to understand his indifference to self and the immobility of manner he maintained under all circumstances and during every fluctuation which took place in the presentation of his case, or in the temper of the people surrounding him.
10083{_}4109{_}I felt that beyond the one fact that he could be relied upon to protect Carmel's name and Carmel's character, even to the jeopardising of his case, he was not to be counted on, and might yet startle many of us, and most notably of all, the little woman waiting to hear what he had to say in his own defence before she threw herself into the breach and made that devoted attempt to save him, in his own despite, which had been my terror from the first and was my terror now.
10083{_}4110{_}Perjury!
10083{_}4111{_}but not in his own defence--rather in opposition to it--that is what his counsel had to fear; and I wondered if they knew it.
10083{_}4112{_}My attention became absorbed in the puzzle.
10083{_}4113{_}Carmel's fate, if not Ella's--and certainly my own--hung upon the issue.
10083{_}4114{_}This I knew, and this I faced, calmly, but very surely, as, the preliminary questions having been answered, Mr. Moffat proceeded.
10083{_}4115{_}The witness's name having been demanded and given and some other preliminary formalities gone through, he was asked:  "Mr. Cumberland, did you have any quarrel with your sister during the afternoon or evening of December the second?"
10083{_}4116{_}"I did."
10083{_}4117{_}Then, as if not satisfied with this simple statement, he blurted forth: "And it wasn't the first.
10083{_}4118{_}I hated the discipline she imposed upon me, and the disapproval she showed of my ways and the manner in which I chose to spend my money."
10083{_}4119{_}A straightforward expression of feeling, but hardly a judicious one.
10083{_}4120{_}Judge Edwards glanced, in some surprise, from Mr. Moffat to the daring man who could choose thus to usher in his defence; and then, forgetting his own emotions, in his instinctive desire for order, rapped sharply with his gavel in correction of the audible expression of a like feeling on the part of the expectant audience.
10083{_}4121{_}Mr. Moffat, apparently unaffected by this result of his daring move, pursued his course, with the quiet determination of one who sees his goal and is working deliberately towards it.
10083{_}4122{_}"Do you mind particularising?
10083{_}4123{_}Of what did she especially disapprove in your conduct or way of spending money?"
10083{_}4124{_}"She disapproved of my fondness for drink.
10083{_}4125{_}She didn't like my late hours, or the condition in which I frequently came home.
10083{_}4126{_}I did not like her expressions of displeasure, or the way she frequently cut me short when I wanted to have a good time with my friends.
10083{_}4127{_}We never agreed.
10083{_}4128{_}I made her suffer often and unnecessarily.
10083{_}4129{_}I regret it now; she was a better sister to me than I could then understand."
10083{_}4130{_}This was uttered slowly and with a quiet emphasis which reawakened that excited hum the judge had been at such pains to quell a moment before.
10083{_}4131{_}But he did not quell it now; he seemed to have forgotten his duty in the strong interest called up by these admissions from the tongue of the most imperturbable prisoner he had had before him in years.
10083{_}4132{_}Mr. Moffat, with an eye on District Attorney Fox, who had shown his surprise at the trend the examination was taking by a slight indication of uneasiness, grateful enough, no doubt, to the daring counsellor, went on with his examination:  "Mr. Cumberland, will you tell us when you first felt this change of opinion in regard to your sister?"
10083{_}4133{_}Mr. Fox leaped to his feet.
10083{_}4134{_}Then he slowly reseated himself.
10083{_}4135{_}Evidently he thought it best to let the prisoner have his full say.
10083{_}4136{_}Possibly he may have regretted his leniency the next moment when, with a solemn lowering of his head, Arthur answered:  "When I saw my home desolated in one dreadful night.
10083{_}4137{_}With one sister dead in the house, the victim of violence, and another delirious from fright or some other analogous cause, I had ample time to think--and I used that time.
10083{_}4138{_}That's all."
10083{_}4139{_}Simple words, read or repeated; but in that crowded court-room, with every ear strained to catch the lie which seemed the only refuge for the man so hemmed in by circumstance, these words, uttered without the least attempt at effect, fell with a force which gave new life to such as wished to see this man acquitted.
10083{_}4140{_}His counsel, as if anxious to take advantage of this very expectation to heighten the effect of what followed, proceeded immediately to inquire:  "When did you see your sister Adelaide for the last time alive?"
10083{_}4141{_}A searching question.
10083{_}4142{_}What would be his reply?
10083{_}4143{_}A very quiet one.
10083{_}4144{_}"That night at the dinner-table.
10083{_}4145{_}When I left the room, I turned to look at her.
10083{_}4146{_}She was not looking at me; so I slammed the door and went upstairs.
10083{_}4147{_}In an hour or so, I had left the house to get a drink.
10083{_}4148{_}I got the drink, but I never saw Adelaide again till I saw her in her coffin."
10083{_}4149{_}This blunt denial of the crime for which he stood there arraigned, fell on my heart with a weight which showed me how inextinguishable is the hope we cherish deep down under all surface convictions.
10083{_}4150{_}I had been unconscious of this hope, but it was there.
10083{_}4151{_}It seemed to die a double death at these words.
10083{_}4152{_}For I believed him!
10083{_}4153{_}Courage is needed for a lie.
10083{_}4154{_}There were no signs visible in him, as yet, of his having drawn upon this last resource of the despairing.
10083{_}4155{_}I should know it when he did; he could not hide the subtle change from me.
10083{_}4156{_}To others, this declaration came with greater or less force, according as it was viewed in the light of a dramatic trick of Mr. Moffat's, or as the natural outburst of a man fighting for his life in his own way and with his own weapons.
10083{_}4157{_}I could not catch the eye of Ella cowering low in her seat, so could not judge what tender chords had been struck in her sensitive breast by these two assertions so dramatically offset against each other--the one, his antagonism to the dead; the other, his freedom from the crime in which that antagonism was supposed to have culminated.
10083{_}4158{_}Mr. Moffat, satisfied so far, put his next question with equal directness:  "Mr. Cumberland, you have mentioned seeing your sister in her coffin.
10083{_}4159{_}When was this?"
10083{_}4160{_}"At the close of her funeral, just before she was carried out."
10083{_}4161{_}"Was that the first and only time you had seen her so placed?"
10083{_}4162{_}"It was."
10083{_}4163{_}"Had you seen the casket itself prior to this moment of which you speak?"
10083{_}4164{_}"I had not."
10083{_}4165{_}"Had you been near it?
10083{_}4166{_}Had you handled it in any way?"
10083{_}4167{_}"No, sir."
10083{_}4168{_}"Mr. Cumberland, you have heard mention made of a ring worn by your sister in life, but missing from her finger after death?"
10083{_}4169{_}"I have."
10083{_}4170{_}"You remember this ring?"
10083{_}4171{_}"I do."
10083{_}4172{_}"Is this it?"
10083{_}4173{_}"It is, so far as I can judge at this distance."
10083{_}4174{_}"Hand the ring to the witness," ordered the judge.
10083{_}4175{_}The ring was so handed.
10083{_}4176{_}He glanced at it, and said bitterly: "I recognise it.
10083{_}4177{_}It was her engagement ring."
10083{_}4178{_}"Was this ring on her finger that night at the dinner-table?"
10083{_}4179{_}"I cannot say, positively, but I believe so.
10083{_}4180{_}I should have noticed its absence."
10083{_}4181{_}"Why, may I ask?"
10083{_}4182{_}For the first time the prisoner flushed and the look he darted at his counsel had the sting of a reproach in it.
10083{_}4183{_}Yet he answered: "It was the token of an engagement I didn't believe in or like.
10083{_}4184{_}I should have hailed any proof that this engagement was off."
10083{_}4185{_}Mr. Moffat smiled enigmatically.
10083{_}4186{_}"Mr. Cumberland, if you are not sure of having seen this ring then, when did you see it and where?"
10083{_}4187{_}A rustle from end to end of that crowded court-room.
10083{_}4188{_}This was an audacious move.
10083{_}4189{_}What was coming?
10083{_}4190{_}What would be the answer of the man who was believed not only to have made himself the possessor of this ring, but to have taken a most strange and uncanny method of disposing of it afterward?
10083{_}4191{_}In the breathless hush which followed this first involuntary expression of feeling, Arthur's voice rose, harsh but steady in this reply:  "I saw it when the police showed it to me, and asked me if I could identify it."
10083{_}4192{_}"Was that the only time you have seen it up to the present moment?"
10083{_}4193{_}Instinctively, the witness's right hand rose; it was as if he were mentally repeating his oath before he uttered coldly and with emphasis, though without any show of emotion:  "It is."
10083{_}4194{_}The universal silence gave way to a universal sigh of excitement and relief.
10083{_}4195{_}District Attorney Fox's lips curled with an imperceptible smile of disdain, which might have impressed the jury if they had been looking his way; but they were all looking with eager and interested eyes at the prisoner, who had just uttered this second distinct and unequivocal denial.
10083{_}4196{_}Mr. Moffat noted this, and his own lip curled, but with a very different show of feeling from that which had animated his distinguished opponent.
10083{_}4197{_}Without waiting for the present sentiment to cool, he proceeded immediately with his examination:  "You swear that you have seen this ring but once since the night of your sister's death, and that was when it was shown you in the coroner's office?"
10083{_}4198{_}"I do."
10083{_}4199{_}"Does this mean that it was not in your possession at any time during that interim?"
10083{_}4200{_}"It certainly does."
10083{_}4201{_}"Mr. Cumberland, more than one witness has testified to the fact of your having been seen to place your hand in the casket of your sister, before the eyes of the minister and of others attending her funeral.
10083{_}4202{_}Is this true?"
10083{_}4203{_}"It is."
10083{_}4204{_}"Was not this a most unusual thing to do?"
10083{_}4205{_}"Perhaps.
10083{_}4206{_}I was not thinking about that.
10083{_}4207{_}I had a duty to perform, and I performed it."
10083{_}4208{_}"A duty?
10083{_}4209{_}Will you explain to the jury what duty?"
10083{_}4210{_}The witness's head rose, then sank.
10083{_}4211{_}He, as well as every one else, seemed to be impressed by the solemnity of the moment.
10083{_}4212{_}Though the intensity of my own interest would not allow my eyes to wander from his face, I could imagine the strained look in Ella's, as she awaited his words.
10083{_}4213{_}They came in another instant, but with less steadiness than he had shown before.
10083{_}4214{_}I even thought I could detect a tremor in his muscles, as well as in his voice:  "I had rebelled against my sister's wishes; I had grieved and deceived her up to the very night of her foul and unnatural death--and all through _drink_."
10083{_}4215{_}Here his eye flashed, and for that fleeting moment he looked a man.
10083{_}4216{_}"I wished to take an oath--an oath I would remember.
10083{_}4217{_}It was for this purpose I ordered the casket opened, and thrust my fingers through the flowers I found there.
10083{_}4218{_}When my fingers touched my sister's brow, I inwardly swore never to taste liquor again.
10083{_}4219{_}I have kept that oath.
10083{_}4220{_}Difficult as it was, in my state of mind, and with all my troubles, I have kept it--and been misunderstood in doing so," he added, in lower tones, and with just a touch of bitterness.
10083{_}4221{_}It was such an unexpected explanation, and so calculated to cause a decided and favourable reaction in the minds of those who had looked upon this especial act of his as an irrefutable proof of guilt, that it was but natural that some show of public feeling should follow.
10083{_}4222{_}But this was checked almost immediately, and Mr. Moffat's voice was heard rising again in his strange but telling examination:  "When you thrust your hand in to take this oath, did you drop anything into your sister's casket?"
10083{_}4223{_}"I did not.
10083{_}4224{_}My hand was empty.
10083{_}4225{_}I held no ring, and dropped none in.
10083{_}4226{_}I simply touched her forehead."
10083{_}4227{_}This added to the feeling; and, in another instant, the excitement might have risen into hubbub, had not the emotions of one little woman found vent in a low and sobbing cry which relieved the tension and gave just the relief needed to hold in check the overstrained feelings of the crowd.
10083{_}4228{_}I knew the voice and cast one quick glance that way, in time to see Ella sinking affrightedly out of sight under the dismayed looks of father and mother; then, anxious to note whether the prisoner had recognised her, too, looked hastily back to find him standing quietly and unmoved, with his eyes on his counsel and his lips set in the stern line which was slowly changing his expression.
10083{_}4229{_}That counsel, strangely alive to the temper and feelings of his audience, waited just long enough for the few simple and solemn words uttered by the accused man to produce their full effect, then with a side glance at Mr. Fox, whose equanimity he had at last succeeded in disturbing, and whose cross-examination of the prisoner he had still to fear, continued his own examination by demanding why, when the ring was discovered in Adelaide's casket and he saw what inferences would be drawn from the fact, he had not made an immediate public explanation of his conduct and the reasons he had had for putting his hand there.
10083{_}4230{_}"I'm not a muff," shot from the prisoner's lips, in his old manner.
10083{_}4231{_}"A man who would take such an oath, in such a way, and at such a time, is not the man to talk about it until he is forced to.
10083{_}4232{_}I would not talk about it now--"  He was checked at this point; but the glimpse we thus obtained of the natural man, in this indignant and sullen outburst, following so quickly upon the solemn declarations of the moment before, did more for him in the minds of those present than the suavest and most discreet answer given under the instigation of his counsel.
10083{_}4233{_}Every face showed pleasure, and for a short space, if for no longer, all who listened were disposed to accept his assertions and accord the benefit of doubt to this wayward son of an esteemed father.
10083{_}4234{_}To me, who had hoped nothing from Moffat's efforts, the substantial nature of the defence thus openly made manifest, brought reanimation and an unexpected confidence in the future.
10083{_}4235{_}The question as to who had dropped the ring into the casket if Arthur had not--the innocent children, the grieving servants--was latent, of course, in every breast, but it had not yet reached the point demanding expression.
10083{_}4236{_}Meanwhile, the examination proceeded.
10083{_}4237{_}"Mr. Cumberland, you have stated that you did not personally drop this ring into the place where it was ultimately found.
10083{_}4238{_}Can you tell us of your own knowledge who did?"
10083{_}4239{_}"I cannot.
10083{_}4240{_}I know nothing about the ring.
10083{_}4241{_}I was much surprised, probably more surprised than any one else, to hear of its discovery in that place."
10083{_}4242{_}The slip--and it was a slip for him to introduce that _more_--was immediately taken advantage of by his counsel.
10083{_}4243{_}"You say 'more,' Why should it be more of a surprise to you than to any one else to learn where this missing engagement ring of your sister's had been found?"
10083{_}4244{_}Again that look of displeasure directed towards his questioner, and a certain additional hardness in his reply, when he finally made it.
10083{_}4245{_}"I was her brother.
10083{_}4246{_}I had a brother's antipathies and rightful suspicions.
10083{_}4247{_}I could not see how that ring came to be where it was, when the only one interested in its restoration was in prison."
10083{_}4248{_}This was a direct blow at myself, and of course called Mr. Fox to his feet, with a motion to strike out this answer.
10083{_}4249{_}An altercation followed between him and Mr. Moffat, which, deeply as it involved my life and reputation, failed to impress me, as it might otherwise have done, if my whole mind had not been engaged in reconciling the difficulty about this ring with what I knew of Carmel and the probability which existed of her having been responsible for its removal from her sister's hand.
10083{_}4250{_}But Carmel had been ill since, desperately ill and unconscious.
10083{_}4251{_}She could have had nothing to do with its disposal afterwards among the flowers at her sister's funeral.
10083{_}4252{_}Nor had she been in a condition to delegate this act of concealment to another.
10083{_}4253{_}Who, then, had been the intermediary in this business?
10083{_}4254{_}The question was no longer a latent one in my mind; it was an insistent one, compelling me either to discredit Arthur's explanation (in which case anything might be believed of him) or to accept for good and all this new theory that some person of unknown identity had played an accessory's part in this crime, whose full burden I had hitherto laid upon the shoulders of the impetuous Carmel.
10083{_}4255{_}Either hypothesis brought light.
10083{_}4256{_}I began to breathe again the air of hope, and if observed at that moment, must have presented the odd spectacle of a man rejoicing in his own shame and accepting with positive uplift, the inevitable stigma cast upon his honour by the suggestive sentence just hurled at him by an indignant witness.
10083{_}4257{_}The point raised by the district attorney having been ruled upon and sustained by the court, Mr. Moffat made no effort to carry his inquiries any further in the direction indicated; but I could see, with all my inexperience of the law and the ways of attorneys before a jury, that the episode had produced its inevitable result, and that my position, as a man released from suspicion, had received a shock, the results of which I might yet be made to feel.
10083{_}4258{_}A moment's pause followed, during which some of Mr. Moffat's nervousness returned.
10083{_}4259{_}He eyed the prisoner doubtfully, found him stoical and as self-contained as at the beginning of his examination, and plunged into a topic which most people had expected him to avoid.
10083{_}4260{_}I certainly had, and felt all the uncertainty and secret alarm which an unexpected move occasions where the issue is momentous with life or death.
10083{_}4261{_}I was filled with terror, not for the man on trial, but for my secret.
10083{_}4262{_}Was it shared by the defence?
10083{_}4263{_}Was Mr. Moffat armed with the knowledge I thought confined to myself and Arthur?
10083{_}4264{_}Had the latter betrayed the cause I had been led to believe he was ready to risk his life to defend?
10083{_}4265{_}Had I mistaken his gratitude to myself; or had I underrated Mr. Moffat's insight or powers of persuasion?
10083{_}4266{_}We had just been made witness to one triumph on the part of this able lawyer in a quarter deemed unassailable by the prosecution.
10083{_}4267{_}Were we about to be made witnesses of another?
10083{_}4268{_}I felt the sweat start on my forehead, and was only able to force myself into some show of self-possession by the evident lack of perfect assurance with which this same lawyer now addressed his client.
10083{_}4269{_}The topic which had awakened in me these doubts and consequent agitation will appear from the opening question.
10083{_}4270{_}"Mr. Cumberland, to return to the night of your sister's death.
10083{_}4271{_}Can you tell us what overcoat you put on when leaving your house?"
10083{_}4272{_}Arthur was as astonished and certainly as disconcerted, if not as seriously alarmed, as I was, by this extraordinary move.
10083{_}4273{_}Surprise, anger, then some deeper feeling rang in his voice as he replied:  "I cannot.
10083{_}4274{_}I took down the first I saw and _the first hat.
10083{_}4275{_}"_  The emphasis placed on the last three words may have been meant as a warning to his audacious counsel, but if so, it was not heeded.
10083{_}4276{_}"Took down?
10083{_}4277{_}Took down from where?"
10083{_}4278{_}"From the rack in the hall where I hang my things; the side hall leading to the door where we usually go out."
10083{_}4279{_}"Have you many coats--overcoats, I mean?"
10083{_}4280{_}"More than one."
10083{_}4281{_}"And you do not know which one you put on that cold night?"
10083{_}4282{_}"I do not."
10083{_}4283{_}"But you know what one you wore back?"
10083{_}4284{_}"No."
10083{_}4285{_}Short, sharp, and threatening was this _no_.
10083{_}4286{_}A war was on between this man and his counsel, and the wonder it occasioned was visible in every eye.
10083{_}4287{_}Perhaps Mr. Moffat realised this; this was what he had dreaded, perhaps.
10083{_}4288{_}At all events, he proceeded with his strange task, in apparent oblivion of everything but his own purpose.
10083{_}4289{_}"You do not know what one you wore back?"
10083{_}4290{_}"I do not."
10083{_}4291{_}"You have seen the hat and coat which have been shown here and sworn to as being the ones in which you appeared on your return to the house, the day following your sister's murder?"
10083{_}4292{_}"I have."
10083{_}4293{_}"Also the hat and coat found on a remote hook in the closet under the stairs, bearing the flour-mark on its under brim?"
10083{_}4294{_}"Yes, that too."
10083{_}4295{_}"Yet cannot say which of these two overcoats you put on when you left your home, an hour or so after finishing your dinner?"
10083{_}4296{_}Trapped by his own lawyer--visibly and remorselessly trapped!
10083{_}4297{_}The blood, shooting suddenly into the astounded prisoner's face, was reflected on the cheeks of the other lawyers present.
10083{_}4298{_}Even Mr. Fox betrayed his surprise; but it was a surprise not untinged by apprehension.
10083{_}4299{_}Mr. Moffat must feel very sure of himself to venture thus far.
10083{_}4300{_}I, who feared to ask myself the cause of this assurance, could only wait and search the partially visible face of little Ella for an enlightenment, which was no more to be found there than in the swollen features of the outraged Arthur.
10083{_}4301{_}The excitement which this event caused, afforded the latter some few moments in which to quell his own indignation; and when he spoke, it was passionately, yet not without some effort at restraint.
10083{_}4302{_}"I cannot.
10083{_}4303{_}I was in no condition to notice.
10083{_}4304{_}I was bent on going into town, and immediately upon coming downstairs went straight to the rack and pulled on the first things that offered."
10083{_}4305{_}It appeared to be a perfect give-a-way.
10083{_}4306{_}And it was, but it was a give-a-way which, I feared, threatened Carmel rather than her brother.
10083{_}4307{_}Mr. Moffat, still nervous, still avoiding the prisoner's eye, relentlessly pursued his course, unmindful--wilfully so, it appeared--of the harm he was doing himself, as well as the witness.
10083{_}4308{_}"Mr. Cumberland, were a coat and hat all that you took from that hall?"
10083{_}4309{_}"No, I took a key--a key from the bunch which I saw lying on the table."
10083{_}4310{_}"Did you recognise this key?"
10083{_}4311{_}"I did."
10083{_}4312{_}"What key was it?"
10083{_}4313{_}"It belonged to Mr. Ranelagh, and was the key to the club-house wine-vault."
10083{_}4314{_}"Where did you put it after taking it up?"
10083{_}4315{_}"In my trousers' pocket."
10083{_}4316{_}"What did you do then?"
10083{_}4317{_}"Went out, of course."
10083{_}4318{_}"Without seeing anybody?"
10083{_}4319{_}"Of course.
10083{_}4320{_}Whom should I see?"
10083{_}4321{_}It was angrily said, and the flush, which had begun to die away, slowly made its way back into his cheeks.
10083{_}4322{_}"Are you willing to repeat that you saw no one?"
10083{_}4323{_}"There was no one."
10083{_}4324{_}A lie!
10083{_}4325{_}All knew it, all felt it.
10083{_}4326{_}The man was perjuring himself, under his own counsel's persistent questioning on a point which that counsel had evidently been warned by him to avoid.
10083{_}4327{_}I was assured of this by the way Moffat failed to meet Arthur's eye, as he pressed on hastily, and in a way to forestall all opposition.
10083{_}4328{_}"There are two ways of leaving your house for the city.
10083{_}4329{_}Which way did you take?"
10083{_}4330{_}"The shortest.
10083{_}4331{_}I went through my neighbour's grounds to Huested Street."
10083{_}4332{_}"Immediately?"
10083{_}4333{_}"As soon as I could.
10083{_}4334{_}I don't know what you mean by immediately."
10083{_}4335{_}"Didn't you stop at the stable?"
10083{_}4336{_}A pause, during which more than one person present sat breathless.
10083{_}4337{_}These questions were what might be expected from Mr. Fox in cross-examination.
10083{_}4338{_}They seemed totally unsuited to a direct examination at the hands of his own counsel.
10083{_}4339{_}What did such an innovation mean?
10083{_}4340{_}"Yes, I stopped at the stable."
10083{_}4341{_}"What to do?"
10083{_}4342{_}"To look at the horses."
10083{_}4343{_}"Why?"
10083{_}4344{_}"One of them had gone lame.
10083{_}4345{_}I wanted to see his condition."
10083{_}4346{_}"Was it the grey mare?"
10083{_}4347{_}Had the defence changed places with the prosecution?
10083{_}4348{_}It looked like it; and Arthur looked as if he considered Mr. Moffat guilty of the unheard of, inexplainable act, of cross-examining his own witness.
10083{_}4349{_}The situation was too tempting for Mr. Fox to resist calling additional attention to it.
10083{_}4350{_}With an assumption of extreme consideration, he leaned forward and muttered under his breath to his nearest colleague, but still loud enough for those about him to hear:  "The prisoner must know that he is not bound to answer questions when such answers tend to criminate him.".
10083{_}4351{_}A lightning glance, shot in his direction, was the eloquent advocate's sole reply.
10083{_}4352{_}But Arthur, nettled into speaking, answered the question put him, in a loud, quick tone: "It was not the grey mare; but I went up to the grey mare before going out; I patted her and bade her be a good girl."
10083{_}4353{_}"Where was she then?"
10083{_}4354{_}"Where she belonged--in her stall."
10083{_}4355{_}The tones had sunk; so had the previously lifted head; he no longer commanded universal sympathy or credence.
10083{_}4356{_}The effect of his former avowals was almost gone.
10083{_}4357{_}Yet Mr. Moffat could smile.
10083{_}4358{_}As I noticed this, and recognised the satisfaction it evinced, my heart went down, in great trouble.
10083{_}4359{_}This esteemed advocate, the hero of a hundred cases, was not afraid to have it known that Arthur had harnessed that mare; he even wanted it known.
10083{_}4360{_}Why?
10083{_}4361{_}There could be but one answer to that--or, so I thought, at the moment.
10083{_}4362{_}The next, I did not know what to think; for he failed to pursue this subject, and simply asked Arthur if, upon leaving, he had locked the stable-door.
10083{_}4363{_}"Yes--no,--I don't remember," was the bungling, and greatly confused reply.
10083{_}4364{_}Mr. Moffat glanced at the jury, the smile still on his lips.
10083{_}4365{_}Did he wish to impress that body with the embarrassment of his client?
10083{_}4366{_}"Relate what followed.
10083{_}4367{_}I am sure the jury will be glad to hear your story from your own lips."
10083{_}4368{_}"It's a beastly one, but if I've got to tell it, here it is: I went straight down to Cuthbert Road and across the fields to the club-house.
10083{_}4369{_}I had not taken the key to the front door, because I knew of a window I could shake loose.
10083{_}4370{_}I did this and went immediately down to the wine-vault.
10083{_}4371{_}I used an electric torch of my own for light.
10083{_}4372{_}I pulled out several bottles, and carried them up into the kitchen, meaning to light the gas, kindle a fire, and have a good time generally.
10083{_}4373{_}But I soon found that I must do without light if I stayed there.
10083{_}4374{_}The meter had been taken out; and to drink by the flash of an electric torch was anything but a pleasing prospect.
10083{_}4375{_}Besides--" here he flashed at his counsel a glance, which for a moment took that gentleman aback--"I had heard certain vague sounds in the house which alarmed me, as well as roused my curiosity.
10083{_}4376{_}Choosing the bottle I liked best, I went to investigate these sounds."
10083{_}4377{_}Mr. Moffat started.
10083{_}4378{_}His witness was having his revenge.
10083{_}4379{_}Kept in ignorance of his counsel's plan of defence, he was evidently advancing testimony new to that counsel.
10083{_}4380{_}I had not thought the lad so subtle, and quaked in secret contemplation of the consequences.
10083{_}4381{_}So did some others; but the interest was intense.
10083{_}4382{_}He had heard sounds--he acknowledged it.
10083{_}4383{_}But what sounds?
10083{_}4384{_}Observing the excitement he had caused, and gratified, perhaps, that he had succeeded in driving that faint but unwelcome smile from Mr. Moffat's lips, Arthur hastened to add:  "But I did not complete my investigations.
10083{_}4385{_}Arrived at the top of the stairs, I heard what drove me from the house at once.
10083{_}4386{_}It was my sister's voice--Adelaide's.
10083{_}4387{_}She was in the building, and I stood almost on a level with her, with a bottle in my pocket.
10083{_}4388{_}It did not take me a minute to clamber through the window.
10083{_}4389{_}I did not stop to wonder, or ask why she was there, or to whom she was speaking.
10083{_}4390{_}I just fled and made my way as well as I could across the golf-links to a little hotel on Cuthbert Road, where I had been once before.
10083{_}4391{_}There I emptied my bottle, and was so overcome by it that I did not return home till noon the next day.
10083{_}4392{_}It was on the way to the Hill that I was told of the awful occurrence which had taken place in the club-house after I had left it.
10083{_}4393{_}That sobered me.
10083{_}4394{_}I have been sober ever since."
10083{_}4395{_}Mr. Moffat's smile came back.
10083{_}4396{_}One might have said that he had been rather pleased than otherwise by the introduction of this unexpected testimony.
10083{_}4397{_}But I doubt if any one but myself witnessed this evidence of good-humour on his part.
10083{_}4398{_}Arthur's attitude and Arthur's manner had drawn all eyes to himself.
10083{_}4399{_}As the last words I have recorded left his lips, he had raised his head and confronted the jury with a straightforward gaze.
10083{_}4400{_}The sturdiness and immobility of his aspect were impressive, in spite of his plain features and the still unmistakable signs of long cherished discontent and habitual dissipation.
10083{_}4401{_}He had struck bottom with his feet, and there he would stand,--or so I thought as I levelled my own glances at him.
10083{_}4402{_}But I had not fully sounded all of Alonzo Moffat's resources.
10083{_}4403{_}That inscrutable lawyer and not-easily-to-be-understood man seemed determined to mar every good impression his unfortunate client managed to make.
10083{_}4404{_}Ignoring the new facts just given, undoubtedly thinking that they would be amply sifted in the coming cross-examination, he drew the attention of the prisoner to himself by the following question:  "Will you tell us again how many bottles of wine you took from the club-house?"
10083{_}4405{_}"One.
10083{_}4406{_}No--I'm not sure about that--I'm not sure of anything.
10083{_}4407{_}I had only one when at the inn in Cuthbert Road."
10083{_}4408{_}"You remember but one?"
10083{_}4409{_}"I had but one.
10083{_}4410{_}One was enough.
10083{_}4411{_}I had trouble in carrying that."
10083{_}4412{_}"Was the ground slippery?"
10083{_}4413{_}"It was snowy and it was uneven.
10083{_}4414{_}I stumbled more than once in crossing the links."
10083{_}4415{_}"Mr. Cumberland, is there anything you would like to say in your own defence before I close this examination?"
10083{_}4416{_}The prisoner thus appealed to, let his eye rest for a moment on the judge, then on the jury, and finally on one little white face lifted from the crowd before him as if to meet and absorb his look.
10083{_}4417{_}Then he straightened himself, and in a quiet and perfectly natural voice, uttered these simple words:  "Nothing but this: I am innocent."
10083{_}4418{_}XXVI  THE SYLLABLE OF DOOM  I alit On a great ship lightning-split, And speeded hither on the sigh Of one who gave an enemy His plank, then plunged aside to die.
10083{_}4419{_}_Prometheus Unbound_.
10083{_}4420{_}Recess followed.
10083{_}4421{_}Clifton and I had the opportunity of exchanging a few words.
10083{_}4422{_}He was voluble; I was reticent.
10083{_}4423{_}I felt obliged to hide from him the true cause of the deep agitation under which I was labouring.
10083{_}4424{_}Attached as he was to me, keenly as he must have felt my anomalous position, he was too full of Moffat's unwarrantable introduction of testimony damaging to his client, to think or talk of anything else.
10083{_}4425{_}"He has laid him open to attack on every side.
10083{_}4426{_}Fox has but to follow his lead, and the thing is done.
10083{_}4427{_}Poor Arthur may be guilty, but he certainly should have every chance a careful lawyer could give him.
10083{_}4428{_}You can see--he makes it very evident--that he has no further use for Moffat.
10083{_}4429{_}I wonder under whose advice he chose him for his counsel.
10083{_}4430{_}I have never thought much of Moffat, myself.
10083{_}4431{_}He wins his cases but--"  "He will win this," I muttered.
10083{_}4432{_}Clifton started; looked at me very closely for a minute, paled a little--I fear that I was very pale myself--but did not ask the question rising to his lips.
10083{_}4433{_}"There is method in the madness of a man like that," I pursued with a gloom I could not entirely conceal.
10083{_}4434{_}"He has come upon some evidence which he has not even communicated to his client.
10083{_}4435{_}At least, I fear so.
10083{_}4436{_}We must be prepared for any untoward event."
10083{_}4437{_}Then, noticing Clifton's alarm and wishing to confine it within safe bounds, I added: "I feel that I am almost as much on trial as Arthur himself.
10083{_}4438{_}Naturally I am anxious at the appearance of anything I do not understand."
10083{_}4439{_}Clifton frowned.
10083{_}4440{_}We were quite alone.
10083{_}4441{_}Leaning forward, he touched my arm.
10083{_}4442{_}"Elwood," said he, "you've not been quite open with me."
10083{_}4443{_}I smiled.
10083{_}4444{_}If half the bitterness and sorrow in my heart went into that smile, it must have been a sad and bitter one indeed.
10083{_}4445{_}"You have a right to reproach me," said I, "but not wholly.
10083{_}4446{_}I did not deceive you in essentials.
10083{_}4447{_}You may still believe me as guiltless of Adelaide's violent death as a man can be who drove her and hers into misery which death alone could end."
10083{_}4448{_}"I will believe it," he muttered, "I must."
10083{_}4449{_}And he dropped the subject, as he made me see, forever.
10083{_}4450{_}I drew a deep breath of relief.
10083{_}4451{_}I had come very near to revealing my secret.
10083{_}4452{_}When we returned to the court-room, we found it already packed with a very subdued and breathless crowd.
10083{_}4453{_}It differed somewhat from the one which had faced us in the morning; but Ella and her parents were there and many others of the acknowledged friends of the accused and of his family.
10083{_}4454{_}He, himself, wore the heavy and dogged air which became him least.
10083{_}4455{_}Physically refreshed, he carried himself boldly, but it was a boldness which convinced me that any talk he may have had with his lawyer, had been no more productive of comfort than the one I had held with mine.
10083{_}4456{_}As he took the witness chair, and prepared to meet the cross-examination of the district attorney, a solemn hush settled upon the room.
10083{_}4457{_}Would the coming ordeal rob his brow of its present effrontery, or would he continue to bear himself with the same surly dignity, which, misunderstood as it was, produced its own effect, and at certain moments seemed to shake even the confidence of Mr. Fox, settled as he seemed to be in his belief in the integrity of his cause and the rights of the prosecution.
10083{_}4458{_}Shaken or not, his attack was stern, swift, and to the point.
10083{_}4459{_}"Was the visit you made to the wine-vault on the evening of the second of December, the first one you had ever paid there?"
10083{_}4460{_}"No; I had been there once before.
10083{_}4461{_}But I always paid for my depredations," he added, proudly.
10083{_}4462{_}"The categorical answer, Mr. Cumberland.
10083{_}4463{_}Anything else is superfluous."
10083{_}4464{_}Arthur's lip curled, but only for an instant; and nothing could have exceeded the impassiveness of his manner as Mr. Fox went on.
10083{_}4465{_}"Then you knew the way?"
10083{_}4466{_}"Perfectly."
10083{_}4467{_}"And the lock?"
10083{_}4468{_}"Sufficiently well to open it without difficulty."
10083{_}4469{_}"How long do you think you were in entering the house and procuring these bottles?"
10083{_}4470{_}"I cannot say.
10083{_}4471{_}I have no means of knowing; I never thought of looking at my watch."
10083{_}4472{_}"Not when you started?
10083{_}4473{_}Not when you left Cuthbert Road?"
10083{_}4474{_}"No, sir."
10083{_}4475{_}"But you know when you left the club-house to go back?"
10083{_}4476{_}"Only by this--it had not yet begun to snow.
10083{_}4477{_}I'm told that the first flakes fell that night at ten minutes to eleven.
10083{_}4478{_}I was on the golf-links when this happened.
10083{_}4479{_}You can fix the time yourself.
10083{_}4480{_}Pardon me," he added, with decided ill-grace as he met Mr. Fox's frown.
10083{_}4481{_}"I forgot your injunction."
10083{_}4482{_}Mr. Fox smiled an acrid smile, as he asked: "Whereabouts on the golf-links?
10083{_}4483{_}They extend for some distance, you remember."
10083{_}4484{_}"They are six hundred yards across from first tee to the third hole, which is the nearest one to Cuthbert Road," Arthur particularised.
10083{_}4485{_}"I was--no, I can't tell you just where I was at that moment.
10083{_}4486{_}It was a good ways from the house.
10083{_}4487{_}The snow came on very fiercely.
10083{_}4488{_}For a little while I could not see my way."
10083{_}4489{_}"How, not see your way?"
10083{_}4490{_}"The snow flew into my eyes."
10083{_}4491{_}"Crossing the links?"
10083{_}4492{_}"Yes, sir, crossing the links."
10083{_}4493{_}"But the storm came from the west.
10083{_}4494{_}It should have beaten against your back."
10083{_}4495{_}"Back or front, it bothered me.
10083{_}4496{_}I could not get on as fast as I wished."
10083{_}4497{_}Mr. Fox cast a look at the jury.
10083{_}4498{_}Did they remember the testimony of the landlord that Mr. Cumberland's coat was as thickly plastered with snow on the front as it had been on the back.
10083{_}4499{_}He seemed to gather that they did, for he went on at once to say:  "You are accustomed to the links?
10083{_}4500{_}You have crossed them often?"
10083{_}4501{_}"Yes, I play golf there all summer."
10083{_}4502{_}"I'm not alluding to the times when you play.
10083{_}4503{_}I mean to ask whether or not you had ever before crossed them directly to Cuthbert Road?"
10083{_}4504{_}"Yes, I had."
10083{_}4505{_}"In a storm?"
10083{_}4506{_}"No, not in a storm."
10083{_}4507{_}"How long did it take you that time to reach Cuthbert Road from The Whispering Pines?"
10083{_}4508{_}Mr. Moffat bounded to his feet, but the prisoner had answered before he could speak.
10083{_}4509{_}"Just fifteen minutes."
10083{_}4510{_}"How came you to know the time so exactly?"
10083{_}4511{_}"Because that day I did look at my watch.
10083{_}4512{_}I had an engagement in the lower town, and had only twenty minutes in which to keep it.
10083{_}4513{_}I was on time."
10083{_}4514{_}Honest at the core.
10083{_}4515{_}This boy was growing rapidly in my favour.
10083{_}4516{_}But this frank but unwise answer was not pleasing to his counsel, who would have advised, no doubt, a more general and less precise reply.
10083{_}4517{_}However, it had been made and Moffat was not a man to cry over spilled milk.
10083{_}4518{_}He did not even wince when the district attorney proceeded to elicit from the prisoner that he was a good walker, not afraid in the least of snow-storms and had often walked, in the teeth of the gale twice that distance in less than half an hour.
10083{_}4519{_}Now, as the storm that night had been at his back, and he was in a hurry to reach his destination, it was evidently incumbent upon him to explain how he had managed to use up the intervening time of forty minutes before entering the hotel at half-past eleven.
10083{_}4520{_}"Did you stop in the midst of the storm to take a drink?"
10083{_}4521{_}asked the district attorney.
10083{_}4522{_}As the testimony of the landlord in Cuthbert Road had been explicit as to the fact of his having himself uncorked the bottle which the prisoner had brought into the hotel, Arthur could not plead yes.
10083{_}4523{_}He must say no, and he did.
10083{_}4524{_}"I drank nothing; I was too busy thinking.
10083{_}4525{_}I was so busy thinking I wandered all over those links."
10083{_}4526{_}"In the blinding snow?"
10083{_}4527{_}"Yes, in the snow.
10083{_}4528{_}What did I care for the snow?
10083{_}4529{_}I did not understand my sister being in the club-house.
10083{_}4530{_}I did not like it; I was tempted at times to go back."
10083{_}4531{_}"And why didn't you?"
10083{_}4532{_}"Because I was more of a brute than a brother--because Cuthbert Road drew me in spite of myself--because--" He stopped with the first hint of emotion we had seen in him since the morning.
10083{_}4533{_}"I did not know what was going on there or I should have gone back," he flashed out, with a defiant look at his counsel.
10083{_}4534{_}Again sympathy was with him.
10083{_}4535{_}Mr. Fox had won but little in this first attempt.
10083{_}4536{_}He seemed to realise this, and shifted his attack to a point more vulnerable.
10083{_}4537{_}"When you heard your sister's voice in the club-house, how did you think she had got into the building?"
10083{_}4538{_}"By means of the keys Ranelagh had left at the house."
10083{_}4539{_}"When, instead of taking the whole bunch, you took the one key you wanted from the ring, did you do so with any idea she might want to make use of the rest?"
10083{_}4540{_}"No, I never thought of it.
10083{_}4541{_}I never thought of her at all."
10083{_}4542{_}"You took your one key, and let the rest lie?"
10083{_}4543{_}"You've said it."
10083{_}4544{_}"Was this before or after you put on your overcoat?"
10083{_}4545{_}"I'm not sure; after, I think.
10083{_}4546{_}Yes, it was after; for I remember that I had a deuce of a time unbuttoning my coat to get at my trousers' pocket."
10083{_}4547{_}"You dropped this key into your trousers' pocket?"
10083{_}4548{_}"I did."
10083{_}4549{_}"Mr. Cumberland, let me ask you to fix your memory on the moments you spent in the hall.
10083{_}4550{_}Did you put on your hat before you pocketed the key, or afterwards?"
10083{_}4551{_}"My hat?
10083{_}4552{_}How can I tell?
10083{_}4553{_}My mind wasn't on my hat.
10083{_}4554{_}I don't know when I put it on."
10083{_}4555{_}"You absolutely do not remember?"
10083{_}4556{_}"No."
10083{_}4557{_}"Nor where you took it from?"
10083{_}4558{_}"No."
10083{_}4559{_}"Whether you saw the keys first, and then went for your hat; or having pocketed the key, waited--"  "I did not wait."
10083{_}4560{_}"Did not stand by the table thinking?"
10083{_}4561{_}"No, I was in too much of a hurry."
10083{_}4562{_}"So that you went straight out?"
10083{_}4563{_}"Yes, as quickly as I could."
10083{_}4564{_}The district attorney paused, to be sure of the attention of the jury.
10083{_}4565{_}When he saw that every eye of that now thoroughly aroused body was on him, he proceeded to ask: "Does that mean immediately, or as soon as you could after you had made certain preparations, or held certain talk with some one you called, or who called to you?"
10083{_}4566{_}"I called to nobody.
10083{_}4567{_}I--I went out immediately."
10083{_}4568{_}It was evident that he lied; evident, too, that he had little hope from his lie.
10083{_}4569{_}Uneasiness was taking the place of confidence in his youthful, untried, undisciplined mind.
10083{_}4570{_}Carmel had spoken to him in the hall--I guessed it then, I knew it afterward--and he thought to deceive this court and blindfold a jury, whose attention had been drawn to this point by his own counsel.
10083{_}4571{_}District Attorney Fox smiled.
10083{_}4572{_}"How then did you get into the stable?"
10083{_}4573{_}"The stable!
10083{_}4574{_}Oh, I had no trouble in getting into the stable."
10083{_}4575{_}"Was it unlocked?"
10083{_}4576{_}A slow flush broke over the prisoner's whole face.
10083{_}4577{_}He saw where he had been landed and took a minute to pull himself together before he replied: "I had the key to that door, too.
10083{_}4578{_}I got it out of the kitchen."
10083{_}4579{_}"You have not spoken of going into the kitchen."
10083{_}4580{_}"I have not spoken of coming downstairs."
10083{_}4581{_}"You went into the kitchen?"
10083{_}4582{_}"Yes."
10083{_}4583{_}"When?"
10083{_}4584{_}"When I first came down."
10083{_}4585{_}"That is not in accordance with your direct testimony.
10083{_}4586{_}On the contrary, you said that on coming downstairs you went straight to the rack for your overcoat.
10083{_}4587{_}Stenographer read what the prisoner said on this topic."
10083{_}4588{_}A rustling of leaves, distinctly to be heard in the deathlike silence of the room, was followed by the reading of this reply and answer:  "_Yet you cannot say which of these two overcoats you put on when you left your home an hour or so after finishing your dinner?_"  "_I cannot.
10083{_}4589{_}I was in no condition to notice.
10083{_}4590{_}I was bent on going into town and, on coming downstairs, I went straight to the rack and pulled on the first things that offered._"  The prisoner stood immobile but with a deepening line gathering on his brow until the last word fell.
10083{_}4591{_}Then he said: "I forgot.
10083{_}4592{_}I went for the key before I put on my overcoat.
10083{_}4593{_}I wanted to see how the sick horse looked."
10083{_}4594{_}"Did you drop this key into your pocket, too?"
10083{_}4595{_}"No, I carried it into the hall."
10083{_}4596{_}"What did you do with it there?"
10083{_}4597{_}"I don't know.
10083{_}4598{_}Put it on the table, I suppose."
10083{_}4599{_}"Don't you remember?
10083{_}4600{_}There were other keys lying on this table.
10083{_}4601{_}Don't you remember what you did with the one in your hand while you took the club-house key from the midst of Mr. Ranelagh's bunch?"
10083{_}4602{_}"I laid it on the table.
10083{_}4603{_}I must have--there was no other place to put it."
10083{_}4604{_}"Laid it down by itself?"
10083{_}4605{_}"Yes."
10083{_}4606{_}"And took it up when you went out?"
10083{_}4607{_}"Of course."
10083{_}4608{_}"Carrying it straight to the stable?"
10083{_}4609{_}"Naturally."
10083{_}4610{_}"What did you do with it when you came out?"
10083{_}4611{_}"I left it in the stable-door."
10083{_}4612{_}"You did?
10083{_}4613{_}What excuse have you to give for that?"
10083{_}4614{_}"None.
10083{_}4615{_}I was reckless, and didn't care for anything--that's all."
10083{_}4616{_}"Yet you took several minutes, for all your hurry and your indifference, to get the stable key and look in at a horse that wasn't sick enough to keep your coachman home from a dance."
10083{_}4617{_}The prisoner was silent.
10083{_}4618{_}"You have no further explanation to give on this subject?"
10083{_}4619{_}"No.
10083{_}4620{_}All fellows who love horses will understand."
10083{_}4621{_}The district attorney shrugged this answer away before he went on to say: "You have listened to Zadok Brown's testimony.
10083{_}4622{_}When he returned at three, he found the stable-door locked, and the key hanging up on its usual nail in the kitchen.
10083{_}4623{_}How do you account for this?"
10083{_}4624{_}"There are two ways."
10083{_}4625{_}"Mention them, if you please."
10083{_}4626{_}"Zadok had been to a dance, and may not have been quite clear as to what he saw.
10083{_}4627{_}Or, finding the stable door open, may have blamed himself for the fact and sought to cover up his fault with a lie."
10083{_}4628{_}"Have you ever caught him in a lie?"
10083{_}4629{_}"No; but there's always a first time."
10083{_}4630{_}"You would impeach his testimony then?"
10083{_}4631{_}"No.
10083{_}4632{_}You asked me how this discrepancy could be explained, and I have tried to show you."
10083{_}4633{_}"Mr. Cumberland, the grey mare was out that night; this has been amply proved."
10083{_}4634{_}"If you believe Zadok, yes."
10083{_}4635{_}"You have heard other testimony corroborative of this fact.
10083{_}4636{_}She was seen on the club-house road that night, by a person amply qualified to identify her."
10083{_}4637{_}"So I've been told."
10083{_}4638{_}"The person driving this horse wore a hat, identified as an old one of yours, which hat was afterwards found at your house on a remote peg in a seldom-used closet.
10083{_}4639{_}If you were not this person, how can you explain the use of your horse, the use of your clothes, the locking of the stable-door--which you declare yourself to have left open--and the hanging up of the key on its own nail?"
10083{_}4640{_}It was a crucial question--how crucial no one knew but our two selves.
10083{_}4641{_}If he answered at all, he must compromise Carmel.
10083{_}4642{_}I had no fear of his doing this, but I had great fear of what Ella might do if he let this implication stand and made no effort to exonerate himself by denying his presence in the cutter, and consequent return to the Cumberland home.
10083{_}4643{_}The quick side glances I here observed cast in her direction by both father and mother, showed that she had made some impulsive demonstration visible to them, if not to others and fearful of the consequences if I did not make some effort to hold her in check, I kept my eyes in her direction, and so lost Arthur's look and the look of his counsel as he answered, with just the word I had expected--a short and dogged:  "I cannot explain."
10083{_}4644{_}It was my death warrant.
10083{_}4645{_}I realised this even while I held Ella's eye with mine and smoothed my countenance to meet the anguish in hers, in the effort to hold her back for a few minutes longer till I could quite satisfy myself that Arthur's case was really lost and that I must speak or feel myself his murderer.
10083{_}4646{_}The gloom which followed this recognition of his inability, real or fancied, to explain away the most damning feature of the case against him, taken with his own contradictions and growing despondency, could not escape my eye, accustomed as I was to the habitual expression of most every person there.
10083{_}4647{_}But it was not yet the impenetrable gloom presaging conviction; and directing Ella's gaze towards Mr. Moffat, who seemed but little disturbed either by Mr. Fox's satisfaction or the prisoner's open despair, I took heart of grace and waited for the district attorney's next move.
10083{_}4648{_}It was a fatal one.
10083{_}4649{_}I began to recognise this very soon, simple as was the subject he now introduced.
10083{_}4650{_}"When you went into the kitchen, Mr. Cumberland, to get the stable-door key, was the gas lit, or did you have to light it?"
10083{_}4651{_}"It--it was lit, I think."
10083{_}4652{_}"Don't you know?"
10083{_}4653{_}"It was lit, but turned low.
10083{_}4654{_}I could see well enough."
10083{_}4655{_}"Why, then, didn't you take both keys?"
10083{_}4656{_}"Both keys?"
10083{_}4657{_}"You have said you went down town by the short cut through your neighbour's yard.
10083{_}4658{_}That cut is guarded by a door, which was locked that night.
10083{_}4659{_}You needed the key to that door more than the one to the stable.
10083{_}4660{_}Why didn't you take it?"
10083{_}4661{_}"I--I did."
10083{_}4662{_}"You haven't said so."
10083{_}4663{_}"I--I took it when I took the other."
10083{_}4664{_}"Are you sure?"
10083{_}4665{_}"Yes; they both hung on one nail.
10083{_}4666{_}I grabbed them both at the same time."
10083{_}4667{_}"It does not appear so in your testimony.
10083{_}4668{_}You mentioned a key, not keys, in all your answers to my questions."
10083{_}4669{_}"There were two; I didn't weigh my words.
10083{_}4670{_}I needed both and I took both."
10083{_}4671{_}"Which of the two hung foremost?"
10083{_}4672{_}"I didn't notice."
10083{_}4673{_}"You took both?"
10083{_}4674{_}"Yes, I took both."
10083{_}4675{_}"And went straight out with them?"
10083{_}4676{_}"Yes, to the stable."
10083{_}4677{_}"And then where?"
10083{_}4678{_}"Through the adjoining grounds downtown."
10083{_}4679{_}"You are sure you went through Mr. Fulton's grounds at this early hour in the evening?"
10083{_}4680{_}"I am positive."
10083{_}4681{_}"Was it not at a later hour, much later, a little before eleven instead of a little before nine?"
10083{_}4682{_}"No, sir.
10083{_}4683{_}I was on the golf-links then."
10083{_}4684{_}"But some one drove into the stable."
10083{_}4685{_}"So you say."
10083{_}4686{_}"Unharnessed the horse, drew up the cutter, locked the stable-door, and, entering the house, hung up the key where it belonged."
10083{_}4687{_}No answer this time.
10083{_}4688{_}"Mr. Cumberland, you admitted in your direct examination that you took with you out of the clubhouse only one bottle of the especial brand you favoured, although you carried up two into the kitchen?"
10083{_}4689{_}"No, I said that I only had one when I got to Cuthbert Road.
10083{_}4690{_}I don't remember anything about the other."
10083{_}4691{_}"But you know where the other--or rather remnants of the other, was found?"
10083{_}4692{_}"In my own stable, taken there by my man Zadok Brown, who says he picked it out of one of our waste barrels."
10083{_}4693{_}"This is the part of bottle referred to.
10083{_}4694{_}Do you recognise the label still adhering to it as similar to the one to be found on the bottle you emptied in Cuthbert Road?"
10083{_}4695{_}"It is like that one."
10083{_}4696{_}"Had you carried that other bottle off, and had it been broken as this has been broken would it not have presented an exactly similar appearance to this?"
10083{_}4697{_}"Possibly."
10083{_}4698{_}"Only possibly?"
10083{_}4699{_}"It would have looked the same.
10083{_}4700{_}I cannot deny it.
10083{_}4701{_}What's the use fooling?"
10083{_}4702{_}"Mr. Cumberland, the only two bottles known to contain this especial brand of wine were in the clubhouse at ten o'clock that night.
10083{_}4703{_}How came one of them to get into the barrel outside your stable before your return the next day?"
10083{_}4704{_}"I cannot say."
10083{_}4705{_}"This barrel stood where?"
10083{_}4706{_}"In the passage behind the stable."
10083{_}4707{_}"The passage you pass through on your way to the door leading into your neighbour's grounds?"
10083{_}4708{_}"Yes."
10083{_}4709{_}The dreaded moment had come.
10083{_}4710{_}This "Yes" had no sooner left Arthur's lips than I saw Ella throw out her innocent arms, and leap impetuously to her feet, with a loud "No, no, I can tell--"  She did not say what, for at the hubbub roused by this outbreak in open court, she fainted dead away and was carried out in her dismayed father's arms.
10083{_}4711{_}This necessarily caused a break in the proceedings.
10083{_}4712{_}Mr. Fox suspended his cross-examination and in a few minutes more, the judge adjourned the court.
10083{_}4713{_}As the prisoner rose and turned to pass out, I cast him a hurried glance to see what effect had been made upon him by this ingenuous outburst from one he had possibly just a little depreciated.
10083{_}4714{_}A great one, evidently.
10083{_}4715{_}His features were transformed, and he seemed almost as oblivious of the countless eyes upon him as she had been when she rose to testify for him in her self-forgetful enthusiasm.
10083{_}4716{_}As I observed this and the satisfaction with which Mr. Moffat scented this new witness,--a satisfaction which promised little consideration for her if she ever came upon the stand--I surrendered to fate.
10083{_}4717{_}Inwardly committing Carmel's future to the God who made her and who knew better than we the story of her life and what her fiery temper had cost her, I drew a piece of paper from my pocket, and, while the courtroom was slowly emptying, hastily addressed the following lines to Mr. Moffat who had lingered to have a few words with his colleague:  "There is a witness in this building who can testify more clearly and definitely than Miss Fulton, that Arthur Cumberland, for all we have heard in seeming contradiction to the same, might have been on the golf-links at the time he swears to.
10083{_}4718{_}That witness is myself.
10083{_}4719{_}"ELWOOD RANELAGH."
10083{_}4720{_}The time which elapsed between my passing over this note and his receiving and reading it, was to me like the last few moments of a condemned criminal.
10083{_}4721{_}How gladly would I have changed places with Arthur, and with what sensations of despair I saw flitting before me in my mind's eye, the various visions of Carmel's loveliness which had charmed me out of myself.
10083{_}4722{_}But the die had been cast, and I was ready to meet the surprised lawyer's look when his eve rose from the words I had written and settled steadily on my face.
10083{_}4723{_}Next minute he was writing busily and in a second later I was reading these words:  "Do you absolutely wish to be recalled as a witness, and by the defence?
10083{_}4724{_}M."  My answer was brief:  "I do.
10083{_}4725{_}Not to make a confession of crime.
10083{_}4726{_}I have no such confession to make.
10083{_}4727{_}But I know who drove that horse.
10083{_}4728{_}R."  I had sacrificed Carmel to my sense of right.
10083{_}4729{_}Never had I loved her as I did at that moment.
10083{_}4730{_}XXVII  EXPECTANCY  I see your end, 'T is my undoing.
10083{_}4731{_}_King Henry VIII_.
10083{_}4732{_}A turning-point had been reached in the defence.
10083{_}4733{_}That every one knew after the first glance at Mr. Moffat, on the opening of the next morning's session.
10083{_}4734{_}As I noted the excitement which this occasioned even in quarters where self-control is usually most marked and such emotions suppressed, I marvelled at the subtle influence of one man's expectancy, and the powerful effect which can be produced on a feverish crowd by a well-ordered silence suggestive of coming action.
10083{_}4735{_}I, who knew the basis of this expectancy and the nature of the action with which Mr. Moffat anticipated startling the court, was the quietest person present.
10083{_}4736{_}Since it was my hand and none other which must give this fresh turn to the wheel of justice, it were well for me to do it calmly and without any of the old maddening throb of heart.
10083{_}4737{_}But the time seemed long before Arthur was released from further cross-examination, and the opportunity given Mr. Moffat to call his next witness.
10083{_}4738{_}Something in the attitude he now took, something in the way he bent over his client and whispered a few admonitory words, and still more the emotion with which these words were received and answered by some extraordinary protest, aroused expectation to a still greater pitch, and made my course seem even more painful to myself than I had foreseen when dreaming over and weighing the possibilities of this hour.
10083{_}4739{_}With something like terror, I awaited the calling of my name; and, when it was delayed, it was with emotions inexplicable to myself that I looked up and saw Mr. Moffat holding open a door at the left of the judge, with that attitude of respect, which a man only assumes in the presence and under the dominating influence of woman.
10083{_}4740{_}"Ella!"
10083{_}4741{_}thought I.
10083{_}4742{_}"Instead of saving her by my contemplated sacrifice of Carmel, I have only added one sacrifice to another."
10083{_}4743{_}But when the timid faltering step we could faintly hear crossing the room beyond, had brought its possessor within sight, and I perceived the tall, black-robed, heavily veiled woman who reached for Mr. Moffat's sustaining arm, I did not need the startling picture of the prisoner, standing upright, with outheld and repellant hands, to realise that the impossible had happened, and that all which he, as well as I, had done and left undone, suffered and suppressed, had been in vain.
10083{_}4744{_}Mr. Moffat, with no eye for him or for me, conducted his witness to a chair; then, as she loosened her veil and let it drop in her lap, he cried in tones which rang from end to end of the court-room: "I summon Carmel Cumberland to the stand, to witness in her brother's defence."
10083{_}4745{_}The surprise was complete.
10083{_}4746{_}It was a great moment for Mr. Moffat; but for me all was confusion, dread, a veil of misty darkness, through which shone her face, marred by its ineffaceable scar, but calm as I had never expected to see it again in this life, and beautiful with a smile under which her deeply shaken and hardly conscious brother sank slowly back into his seat, amid a silence as profound as the hold she had immediately taken upon all hearts.
10083{_}4747{_}XXVIII  "WHERE IS MY BROTHER?"
10083{_}4748{_}Let me see the writing.
10083{_}4749{_}My lord, 't is nothing.
10083{_}4750{_}No matter, then, who sees it; I will be satisfied, let me see the writing.
10083{_}4751{_}_Richard II_.
10083{_}4752{_}What is the explanation of Carmel's reappearance in town and of this sensational introduction of her into the court-room, in a restored state of health of which no one, so far as known, had had any intimation save the man who was responsible for her appearance?
10083{_}4753{_}The particulars are due you.
10083{_}4754{_}She had passed some weeks at Lakewood, under the eye of the nurse who was detailed to watch, as well as tend her.
10083{_}4755{_}During these weeks she gave no sign of improvement mentally, though she constantly gained strength otherwise, and impressed everybody with the clear light in her eye and the absence of everything suggestive of gloom in her expression and language.
10083{_}4756{_}There was the same complete loss of memory up to the time of the tragic occurrence which had desolated her home; the same harping at odd moments on Adelaide's happiness and her own prospect of seeing this dear sister very soon which had marked the opening days of her convalescence.
10083{_}4757{_}But beyond and back of all this was some secret joy, unintelligible to the nurse, which helped rather than retarded the sick girl's recovery, and made Carmel appear at times as if she walked on air and breathed the very breath of Paradise--an anomaly which not only roused Miss Unwin's curiosity, but led her to regard with something like apprehension, any change in her patient's state of mind which would rob her of the strange and unseen delights which fed her secret soul and made her oblivious of the awful facts awaiting a restored memory.
10083{_}4758{_}Meanwhile Carmel was allowed such liberty as her condition required; but was never left alone for a moment after a certain day when her eye suddenly took on a strange look of confused inquiry, totally dissociated with anything she saw or heard.
10083{_}4759{_}A stir had taken place in her brain, and her nurse wanted to take her back home.
10083{_}4760{_}But this awakening--if such it could be called, was so short in its duration and was followed so immediately by a string of innocent questions about Adelaide, that Nurse Unwin concluded to remain a few days longer before risking this delicately balanced mind amid old scenes and the curious glances of her townspeople.
10083{_}4761{_}Alas!
10083{_}4762{_}the awakening was to take place in Lakewood and under circumstances of the most ordinary nature.
10083{_}4763{_}Carmel had been out and was just crossing the hall of her hotel to the elevator, when she stopped with a violent start and clutching the air, was caught by her nurse who had hurried up at the first intimation of anything unusual in the condition of her patient.
10083{_}4764{_}The cause of this agitation was immediately apparent.
10083{_}4765{_}Near them sat two ladies, each with a small wine-glass in her hand.
10083{_}4766{_}One was drinking, the other waiting and watching, but with every apparent intention of drinking when the other had ceased.
10083{_}4767{_}A common sight enough, but it worked a revolution in Carmel's darkened mind.
10083{_}4768{_}The light of youthful joyousness fled from her face; and the cheek, just pulsing softly with new life, blanched to the death-like hue of mortal suffering.
10083{_}4769{_}Dropping her eyes from the women, who saw nothing and continued to sip their wine in happy ignorance of the soul-tragedy going on within ten feet of them, she looked down at her dress, then up at the walls about her; and then slowly, anxiously, and with unmistakable terror, at the woman in whose arms she felt herself supported.
10083{_}4770{_}"Explain," she murmured.
10083{_}4771{_}"Where am I?"
10083{_}4772{_}"At Lakewood, in a hotel.
10083{_}4773{_}You have been ill, and are only just recovering."
10083{_}4774{_}Her hand went up to her cheek, the one that had been burned, and still showed the deep traces of that accident.
10083{_}4775{_}"I remember," said she.
10083{_}4776{_}Then with another glance at her dress, which had studiously been kept cheerful, she remarked, with deep reproach: "My sister is dead; why am I not in black?"
10083{_}4777{_}The nurse, realising her responsibility (she said afterwards that it was the most serious moment of her life), subdued her own astonishment at this proof of her young patient's knowledge of a crime of which she was universally supposed to be entirely ignorant, and, bestowing a reassuring smile on the agitated girl, observed softly:  "You wore too ill to be burdened with black.
10083{_}4778{_}You are better now and may assume it if you will.
10083{_}4779{_}I will help you buy your mourning."
10083{_}4780{_}"Yes, you look like a kind woman.
10083{_}4781{_}What is your name, please, and are we here alone in this great hotel?"
10083{_}4782{_}Now, as a matter of expediency--to save Carmel from the unendurable curiosity of the crowd, and herself from the importunities of the New York reporters, Miss Unwin had registered herself and her charge under assumed names.
10083{_}4783{_}She was, therefore, forced to reply:  "My name is Huckins, and we are here alone.
10083{_}4784{_}But that need not worry you.
10083{_}4785{_}I have watched over you night and day for many weeks."
10083{_}4786{_}"You have?
10083{_}4787{_}Because of this slight burn?"
10083{_}4788{_}Again Carmel's hand went to her cheek.
10083{_}4789{_}"Not on account of that only.
10083{_}4790{_}You have had a serious illness quite apart from that injury.
10083{_}4791{_}But you are better; you are almost well--well enough to go home, if you will."
10083{_}4792{_}"I cannot go home--not just yet.
10083{_}4793{_}I'm--I'm not strong enough.
10083{_}4794{_}But we shouldn't be here alone without some man to look after us.
10083{_}4795{_}Miss Huckins, _where is my brother_?"
10083{_}4796{_}At this question, uttered with emphasis, with anxiety--with indignation even--Miss Unwin felt the emotion she had so successfully subdued up to this moment, betray itself in her voice as she answered, with a quiet motion towards the elevator: "Let us go up to our room.
10083{_}4797{_}There I will answer all your questions."
10083{_}4798{_}But Carmel, with the waywardness of her years--or perhaps, with deeper reasoning powers than the other would be apt to attribute to her--broke softly away from Miss Unwin's detaining hand, and walking directly into the office, looked about for the newspaper stand.
10083{_}4799{_}Miss Unwin, over-anxious not to make a scene, followed, but did not seek to deter her, until they were once again by themselves in the centre of the room.
10083{_}4800{_}Then she ventured to speak again:  "We have all the papers in our room.
10083{_}4801{_}Come up, and let me read them to you."
10083{_}4802{_}But Fate was making ready its great stroke.
10083{_}4803{_}Just as Carmel seemed about to yield to this persuasion, some lingering doubt drew her eyes again to the stand, just at the very moment a boy stepped into view with the evening bulletin, on which had just been written these words:  The Last Juror Obtained in the Trial of Arthur Cumberland for the Murder of His Sister, Adelaide.
10083{_}4804{_}Carmel saw, and stood--a breathless image of horror.
10083{_}4805{_}A couple of gentlemen came running; but the nurse waved them back, and herself caught Carmel and upheld her, in momentary dread of another mental, if not physical, collapse.
10083{_}4806{_}But Carmel had come back into the world of consciousness to stay.
