10083{_}4807{_}Accepting her nurse's support, but giving no sign of waning faculties or imperfect understanding of what she had seen, she spoke quite clearly and with her eyes fixed upon Miss Unwin:  "So that is why I am here, away from all my friends.
10083{_}4808{_}Was I too ill to be told?
10083{_}4809{_}Couldn't you make me know what was happening?
10083{_}4810{_}You or the doctors or--or anybody?"
10083{_}4811{_}"You were much too ill," protested the nurse, leading her towards the elevator and so by degrees to her room.
10083{_}4812{_}"I tried to arouse you after the crisis of your illness had passed; but you seemed to have forgotten everything which took place that night and the doctors warned me not to press you."
10083{_}4813{_}"And Arthur--poor Arthur, has been the sufferer!
10083{_}4814{_}Tell me the whole story.
10083{_}4815{_}I can bear it," she pleaded.
10083{_}4816{_}"I can bear anything but not knowing.
10083{_}4817{_}Why should he have fallen under suspicion?
10083{_}4818{_}He was not even there.
10083{_}4819{_}I must go to him!
10083{_}4820{_}Pack up our clothing, Miss Huckins.
10083{_}4821{_}I must go to him at once."
10083{_}4822{_}They were in their own room now, and Carmel was standing quite by herself in the full light of the setting sun.
10083{_}4823{_}With the utterance of this determination, she had turned upon her companion; and that astute and experienced woman had every opportunity for observing her face.
10083{_}4824{_}There was a woman's resolution in it.
10083{_}4825{_}With the sudden rending of the clouds which had obscured her intellect, strange powers had awakened in this young girl, giving her a force of expression which, in connection with her inextinguishable beauty, formed a spectacle before which this older woman, in spite of her long experience, hesitated in doubt.
10083{_}4826{_}"You shall go--" began the nurse, and stopped.
10083{_}4827{_}Carmel was not listening.
10083{_}4828{_}Another change of thought had come, and her features, as keenly alive now to every passing emotion as they had formerly been set in a dull placidity, mirrored doubts of her own, which had a deeper source than any which had disturbed the nurse, even in these moments of serious perplexity.
10083{_}4829{_}"How can I?"
10083{_}4830{_}fell in unconscious betrayal from her lips.
10083{_}4831{_}"How can I!"
10083{_}4832{_}Then she stood silent, ghastly with lack of colour one minute, and rosy red with its excess the next, until it was hard to tell in which extreme her feeling spoke most truly.
10083{_}4833{_}What was the feeling?
10083{_}4834{_}Nurse Unwin felt it imperative to know.
10083{_}4835{_}Relying on the confidence shown her by this unfortunate girl, in her lonely position and unbearable distress, she approached Carmel, with renewed offers of help and such expressions of sympathy as she thought might lure her into open speech.
10083{_}4836{_}But discretion had come with fear, and Carmel, while not disdaining the other's kindness, instantly made it apparent that, whatever her burden, and however unsuited it was to her present weak condition, it was not one she felt willing to share.
10083{_}4837{_}"I must think," she murmured, as she finally followed the nurse's lead and seated herself on a lounge.
10083{_}4838{_}"Arthur on trial for his life!
10083{_}4839{_}_Arthur on trial for his life!_ And Adelaide was not even murdered!"
10083{_}4840{_}"No?"
10083{_}4841{_}gasped the nurse, intent on every word this long-silenced witness let fall.
10083{_}4842{_}"Had he no friend?
10083{_}4843{_}Was there not some one to understand?
10083{_}4844{_}Adelaide--" here her head fell till her face was lost to sight--"had--a--lover--"  "Yes.
10083{_}4845{_}Mr. Elwood Ranelagh.
10083{_}4846{_}He was the first to be arrested for the crime."
10083{_}4847{_}The soul in Carmel seemed to vanish at this word.
10083{_}4848{_}The eyes, which had been so far-seeing the moment before, grew blank, and the lithe young body stiff with that death in life which is almost worse to look upon than death itself.
10083{_}4849{_}She did not speak; but presently she arose, as an automaton might arise at the touch of some invisible spring, and so stood, staring, until the nurse, frightened at the result of her words and the complete overthrow which might follow them, sprang for a newspaper and thrust it into her patient's unwilling hand.
10083{_}4850{_}Was it too late?
10083{_}4851{_}For a minute it seemed to be so; then the stony eyes softened and fell, the rigidity of her frame relaxed, and Carmel sank back again on the sofa and tried to read the headlines on the open sheet before her.
10083{_}4852{_}But her eyes were unequal to the task.
10083{_}4853{_}With a sob she dropped the paper and entreated the nurse to relate to her from her own knowledge, all that had passed, sparing her nothing that would make the situation perfectly clear to one who had been asleep during the worst crisis of her life.
10083{_}4854{_}Miss Unwin complied, but with reservations.
10083{_}4855{_}She told of Adelaide having been found dead at The Whispering Pines by the police, whom she had evidently summoned during a moment of struggle or fear; of Ranelagh's presence there, and of the suspicions to which it gave rise; of his denial of the crime; of his strange reticence on certain points, which served to keep him incarcerated till a New York detective got to work and found so much evidence against her brother that Mr. Ranelagh was subsequently released and Arthur Cumberland indicted.
10083{_}4856{_}But she said nothing about the marks on Adelaide's throat, or of the special reason which the police had for arresting Mr. Ranelagh.
10083{_}4857{_}She did not dare.
10083{_}4858{_}Strangulation was a horrible death to contemplate; and if this factor in the crime--she was not deceived by Carmel's exclamation that there had been no murder--was unknown as yet to her patient, as it must be from what she had said, and the absolute impossibility, as she thought, of her having known what went on in The Whispering Pines, then it had better remain unknown to her until circumstances forced it on her knowledge, or she had gotten sufficient strength to bear it.
10083{_}4859{_}Carmel received the account well.
10083{_}4860{_}She started when she heard of the discovery of Ranelagh in the club-house on the entrance of the police, and seemed disposed to ask some questions.
10083{_}4861{_}But though the nurse gave her an opportunity to do so, she appeared to hunt in vain for the necessary words, and the narrative proceeded without further interruption.
10083{_}4862{_}When all was done, she sat quite still; then carefully, and with a show of more judgment than might be expected from one of her years, she propounded certain inquiries which brought out the main causes for her brother's arraignment.
10083{_}4863{_}When she had these fully in mind, she looked up into the nurse's face again and repeated, quite calmly, but with immovable decision, the order of an hour before:  "We must return at once.
10083{_}4864{_}You will pack up immediately."
10083{_}4865{_}Miss Unwin nodded, and began to open the trunks.
10083{_}4866{_}This, however, was a ruse.
10083{_}4867{_}She did not intend to take her patient back that night.
10083{_}4868{_}She was afraid to risk it.
10083{_}4869{_}The next day would be soon enough.
10083{_}4870{_}But she would calm her by making ready, and when the proper moment came, would find some complication of trains which would interfere with their immediate departure.
10083{_}4871{_}Meanwhile, she would communicate at the earliest moment with Mr. Fox.
10083{_}4872{_}She had been in the habit of sending him frequent telegrams as to her patient's condition.
10083{_}4873{_}They had been invariable so far: "No difference; mind still a blank," or some code word significant of the same.
10083{_}4874{_}But a new word was necessary now.
10083{_}4875{_}She must look it up, and formulate her telegram before she did anything else.
10083{_}4876{_}The code-book was in her top tray.
10083{_}4877{_}She hunted and hunted for it, without being able to lay her hands on it.
10083{_}4878{_}She grew very nervous.
10083{_}4879{_}She was only human; she was in a very trying position, and she realised it.
10083{_}4880{_}Where could that book be?
10083{_}4881{_}Suddenly she espied it and, falling on her knees before the trunk, with her back still to Carmel, studied out the words she wanted.
10083{_}4882{_}She was leaning over the tray to write these words in her note-book, when--no one ever knew how it happened--the lid of the heavy trunk fell forward and its iron edge struck her on the nape of the neck, with a keen blow which laid her senseless.
10083{_}4883{_}When Carmel reached her side, she found herself the strong one and her stalwart nurse the patient.
10083{_}4884{_}When help had been summoned, the accident explained, and everything done for the unconscious woman which medical skill could suggest, Carmel, finding a moment to herself, stole to the trunk, and, lifting up the lid, looked in.
10083{_}4885{_}She had been watchful of her nurse from the first, and was suspicious of the actions which had led to this untoward accident.
10083{_}4886{_}Seeing the two little books, she took them out.
10083{_}4887{_}The note-book lay open and on the page thus disclosed, she beheld written:  Ap Lox Fidestum Truhum  Ridiculous nonsense--until she consulted the code.
10083{_}4888{_}Then these detached and meaningless words took on a significance which she could not afford to ignore:  Ap         A change.
10083{_}4889{_}Lox        Makes remarkable statements.
10083{_}4890{_}Fidestum   Shall we return?
10083{_}4891{_}Trubum     Not tractable.
10083{_}4892{_}Carmel endeavoured to find out for whom this telegram was intended.
10083{_}4893{_}There was nothing to inform her.
10083{_}4894{_}A moment of indecision was followed by quick action.
10083{_}4895{_}She had noticed that she had been invariably addressed as Miss Campbell by every one who had come into the room.
10083{_}4896{_}Whether this was a proof of the care with which she had been guarded from the curiosity of strangers, or whether it was part of a system of deception springing from quite different causes, she felt that in the present emergency it was a fact to be thankful for and to be utilised.
10083{_}4897{_}Regaining her own room, which was on the other side of their common sitting-room, she collected a few necessary articles, and placed them in a bag which she thrust under her bed.
10083{_}4898{_}Hunting for money, she found quite an adequate amount in her own purse, which was attached to her person.
10083{_}4899{_}Satisfied thus far, she chose her most inconspicuous hat and coat, and putting them on, went out by her own door into the corridor.
10083{_}4900{_}The time--it was the dinner-hour--favoured her attempt.
10083{_}4901{_}She found her way to the office unobserved, and, going frankly up to the clerk, informed him that she had some telegrams to send and that she would be out for some little time.
10083{_}4902{_}Would he see that Miss Huckins was not neglected in her absence?
10083{_}4903{_}The clerk, startled at these evidences of sense and self-reliance in one he had been accustomed to see under the special protection of the very woman she was now confiding to his care, surveyed her eloquent features beaming with quiet resolve, and for a moment seemed at a loss how to take this change and control the strange situation.
10083{_}4904{_}Perhaps she understood him, perhaps she only followed the impulses natural to her sex.
10083{_}4905{_}She never knew; she only remembers that she smiled, and that his hesitation vanished at that smile.
10083{_}4906{_}"I will see to it," said he.
10083{_}4907{_}Then, as she turned to go, he ventured to add, "It is quite dark now.
10083{_}4908{_}If you would like one of the boys to go with you--".
10083{_}4909{_}But he received no encouragement, and allowed his suggestion to remain unfinished.
10083{_}4910{_}She looked grateful for this, and was pulling down her veil when she perceived two or three men on the other side of the room, watching her in evident wonder.
10083{_}4911{_}Stepping back to the desk, she addressed the clerk again, this time with a marked distinctness:  "I have been very ill, I know, and not always quite myself.
10083{_}4912{_}But the shock of this accident to my nurse has cleared my brain and made me capable again of attending to my own affairs.
10083{_}4913{_}You can trust me; I can do my errands all right; but perhaps I had better have one of the boys go with me."
10083{_}4914{_}The clerk, greatly relieved, rang his bell, and the gentlemen at the other end of the room sauntered elsewhere to exchange their impressions of an incident which was remarkable enough in itself, without the accentuation put upon it by the extreme beauty of the girl and the one conspicuous blemish to that beauty--her unfortunate scar.
10083{_}4915{_}With what additional wonder would they have regarded the occurrence, had they known that the object of their interest was not an unknown Miss Campbell, but the much pitied, much talked-of Carmel Cumberland, sister of the man then on trial for his life in a New York town.
10083{_}4916{_}With her first step into the street, Carmel's freshly freed mind began its work.
10083{_}4917{_}She knew she was in a place called Lakewood, but she knew little of its location, save that it was somewhere in New Jersey.
10083{_}4918{_}Another strange thing!
10083{_}4919{_}she did not recognise the streets.
10083{_}4920{_}They were new to her.
10083{_}4921{_}She did not remember ever having been in them before.
10083{_}4922{_}"Where is the railroad station?"
10083{_}4923{_}she inquired of the boy who was trotting along at her side.
10083{_}4924{_}"Over there," he answered, vaguely.
10083{_}4925{_}"Take me to it."
10083{_}4926{_}He obeyed, and they threaded several streets whose lighted shops pleased her, notwithstanding her cares; such a joy it was to be alive to things once more, and capable of remembrance, even though remembrance brought visions at which she shuddered, and turned away, appalled.
10083{_}4927{_}The sight of the station, from which a train was just leaving, frightened her for a moment with its bustle and many lights; but she rallied under the stress of her purpose, and, entering, found the telegraph office, from which she sent this message, directed to her physician, at home, Dr. Carpenter:  "Look for me on early train.
10083{_}4928{_}All is clear to me now, and I must return.
10083{_}4929{_}Preserve silence till we meet."
10083{_}4930{_}This she signed with a pet name, known only to themselves, and dating back to her childish days.
10083{_}4931{_}Then she bought a ticket, and studied the time-table.
10083{_}4932{_}When quite satisfied, she returned to the hotel.
10083{_}4933{_}She was met in the doorway by the physician who was attending the so-called Miss Huckins.
10083{_}4934{_}He paused when he saw her, and asked a few questions which she was penetrating enough to perceive were more for the purpose of testing her own condition than to express interest in his patient.
10083{_}4935{_}She answered quietly, and was met by a surprise and curiosity which evinced that he was greatly drawn towards her case.
10083{_}4936{_}This alarmed her.
10083{_}4937{_}She did not wish to be the object of any one's notice.
10083{_}4938{_}On the contrary, she desired to obliterate herself; to be counted out so far as all these people were concerned.
10083{_}4939{_}But above all, she was anxious not to rouse suspicion.
10083{_}4940{_}So she stopped and talked as naturally as she could about Miss Huckins's accident and what the prospects were for the night.
10083{_}4941{_}These were favourable, or so the doctor declared, but the injured woman's condition called for great care and he would send over a capable nurse at-once.
10083{_}4942{_}Meanwhile, the maid who was with her would do very well.
10083{_}4943{_}She, herself, need have no worry.
10083{_}4944{_}He would advise against worry, and suggested that she should have a good and nourishing dinner sent to her room, after which she should immediately retire and get what sleep she could by means of an anodyne he would send her.
10083{_}4945{_}Carmel exerted herself.
10083{_}4946{_}"You are very good," said she, "I need no anodyne.
10083{_}4947{_}I _am_ tired and when I once get to bed shall certainly sleep.
10083{_}4948{_}I shall give orders not to be disturbed.
10083{_}4949{_}Isn't that right?"
10083{_}4950{_}"Quite right.
10083{_}4951{_}I will myself tell the nurse."
10083{_}4952{_}He was going, but turned to look at her again.
10083{_}4953{_}"Shall I accompany you to the door of your room?"
10083{_}4954{_}he asked.
10083{_}4955{_}She shook her head, with a smile.
10083{_}4956{_}This delay was a torment to her, but it must be endured.
10083{_}4957{_}"I am quite capable of finding my room.
10083{_}4958{_}I hope Miss Huckins will be as well in a week from now as I am at this moment.
10083{_}4959{_}But, doctor--" she had been struck by a strange possibility--"I should like to settle one little matter before we part.
10083{_}4960{_}The money I have may not be quite safe in my hands.
10083{_}4961{_}My memory might leave me again, and then Miss Huckins might suffer.
10083{_}4962{_}If you will take charge of some of it on her account, I shall feel relieved."
10083{_}4963{_}"It would be a wise precaution," he admitted.
10083{_}4964{_}"But you could just as well leave it at the desk."
10083{_}4965{_}"So I can," she smiled.
10083{_}4966{_}Then, as his eye remained fixed on her: "You are wondering if I have friends.
10083{_}4967{_}We both have and I have just come from telegraphing to one of them.
10083{_}4968{_}You can leave us, with an easy mind.
10083{_}4969{_}All that I dread is that Miss Huckins will worry about me if her consciousness should return during the night."
10083{_}4970{_}"It will not return so soon.
10083{_}4971{_}Next week we may look for it.
10083{_}4972{_}Then you can be by to reassure her if she asks for you."
10083{_}4973{_}Carmers eyes fell.
10083{_}4974{_}"I would not be a cause of distress to her for the world.
10083{_}4975{_}She has been very good to me."
10083{_}4976{_}Bowing, she turned in the direction of the office.
10083{_}4977{_}The doctor, lifting his hat, took his departure.
10083{_}4978{_}The interview might have lasted five minutes.
10083{_}4979{_}She felt as though it had lasted an hour.
10083{_}4980{_}She followed the doctor's advice and left half the money she had, in charge of the clerk.
10083{_}4981{_}Then she went upstairs.
10083{_}4982{_}She was not seen to come down again; but when the eight-forty-five train started out of the station that night, it had for a passenger, a young, heavily veiled girl, who went straight to her section.
10083{_}4983{_}A balcony running by her window had favoured her escape.
10083{_}4984{_}It led to a hall window at the head of a side staircase.
10083{_}4985{_}She met no one on the staircase, and, once out of the door at its foot, her difficulties were over, and her escape effected.
10083{_}4986{_}She was missed the next morning, and an account of her erratic flight reached the papers, and was published far and wide.
10083{_}4987{_}But the name of Miss Caroline Campbell conveyed nothing to the public, and the great trial went on without a soul suspecting the significance of this midnight flitting of an unknown and partially demented girl.
10083{_}4988{_}At the house of Dr. Carpenter she met Mr. Moffat.
10083{_}4989{_}What she told him heartened him greatly for the struggle he saw before him.
10083{_}4990{_}Indeed, it altered the whole tone of the defence.
10083{_}4991{_}Perceiving from her story, and from what the doctor could tell him of their meeting at the station that her return to town was as yet a secret to every one but themselves, he begged that the secret should continue to be kept, in order that the _coup d'etat_ which he meditated might lose none of its force by anticipation.
10083{_}4992{_}Carmel, whose mind was full of her coming ordeal, was willing enough to hide her head until it came; while Dr. Carpenter, alarmed at all this excitement, would have insisted on it in any event.
10083{_}4993{_}Carmel wished her brother informed of her return, but the wily lawyer persuaded her to excuse him from taking Arthur into his confidence until the last moment.
10083{_}4994{_}He knew that he would receive only opposition from his young and stubborn client; that Carmel's presence and Carmel's determination would have to be sprung upon Arthur even more than upon the prosecution; that the prisoner at the bar would struggle to the very last against Carmel's appearance in court, and make an infinite lot of trouble, if he did not actually endanger his own cause.
10083{_}4995{_}One of the stipulations which he had made in securing Mr. Moffat for his counsel was that Carmel's name was to be kept as much as possible out of the proceedings; and to this Mr. Moffat had subscribed, notwithstanding his conviction that the crime laid to the defendant's charge was a result of Ranelagh's passion for Carmel, and, consequently, distinctly the work of Ranelagh's own hand.
10083{_}4996{_}He had thought that he could win his case by the powers of oratory and a somewhat free use of innuendo; but his view changed under the fresh enlightenment which he received in his conversation with Carmel.
10083{_}4997{_}He saw unfolding before him a defence of unparalleled interest.
10083{_}4998{_}True, it involved this interesting witness in a way that would be unpleasant to the brother; but he was not the man to sacrifice a client to any sentimental scruple--certainly not this client, whose worth he was just beginning to realise.
10083{_}4999{_}Professional pride, as well as an inherent love of justice, led him to this conclusion.
10083{_}5000{_}Nothing in God's world appealed to him, or ever had appealed to him, like a prisoner in the dock facing a fate from which only legal address, added to an orator's eloquence, could save him.
10083{_}5001{_}His sympathies went out to a man so placed, even when he was a brute and his guilt far from doubtful.
10083{_}5002{_}How much more, then, must he feel the claims of this surly but chivalrous-hearted boy, son of a good father and pious mother, who had been made the butt of circumstances, and of whose innocence he was hourly becoming more and more convinced.
10083{_}5003{_}Could he have probed the whole matter, examined and re-examined this new witness until every detail was his and the whole story of that night stood bare before him, he might have hesitated a little longer and asked himself some very serious questions.
10083{_}5004{_}But Carmel was not strong enough for much talk.
10083{_}5005{_}Dr. Carpenter would not allow it, and the continued clearness of her mind was too invaluable to his case for this far-seeing advocate to take any risk.
10083{_}5006{_}She had told him enough to assure him that circumstances and not guilt had put Arthur where he was, and had added to the assurance, details of an unexpected nature--so unexpected, indeed, that the lawyer was led away by the prospect they offered of confounding the prosecution by a line of defence to which no clew had been given by anything that had appeared.
10083{_}5007{_}He planned then and there a dramatic climax which should take the breath away from his opponent, and change the whole feeling of the court towards the prisoner.
10083{_}5008{_}It was a glorious prospect, and if the girl remained well--the bare possibility of her not doing so, drove him prematurely from her presence; and so it happened that, for the second time, the subject of Adelaide's death was discussed in her hearing without any mention being made of strangulation as its immediate cause.
10083{_}5009{_}Would her action have been different had she known that this was a conceded fact?
10083{_}5010{_}Mr. Moffat did not repeat this visit.
10083{_}5011{_}He was not willing to risk his secret by being seen too often at the doctor's house; but telephonic communication was kept up between him and her present guardian, and he was able to bear himself quietly and with confidence until the time drew near for the introduction of her testimony.
10083{_}5012{_}Then he grew nervous, fearing that Nurse Unwin would come to herself and telegraph Carmel's escape, and so prepare the prosecution for his great stroke.
10083{_}5013{_}But nothing of the kind happened; and, when the great day came, he had only to consider how he should prepare Arthur for the surprise awaiting him, and finally decided not to prepare him at all, but simply to state at the proper moment, and in the face of the whole court-room, that his sister had recovered and would soon take her place upon the stand.
10083{_}5014{_}The restraint of the place would thus act as a guard between them, and Carmel's immediate entrance put an end to the reproaches of whose bitterness he could well judge from his former experience of them.
10083{_}5015{_}With all these anxieties and his deeply planned _coup d'etat_ awaiting the moment of action, Ella's simple outburst and even Ranelagh's unexpected and somewhat startling suggestion lost much of their significance.
10083{_}5016{_}All his mind and heart were on his next move.
10083{_}5017{_}It was to be made with the queen, and must threaten checkmate.
10083{_}5018{_}Yet he did not forget the two pawns, silent in their places--but guarding certain squares which the queen, for all her royal prerogatives, might not be able to reach.
10083{_}5019{_}BOOK FOUR  WHAT THE PINES WHISPERED     XXIX  "I REMEMBERED THE ROOM"  MERCURY.--If thou mightst dwell among the Gods the while           Lapped in voluptuous joy?
10083{_}5020{_}PROMETHEUS.--I would not quit              This bleak ravine, these unrepentant pains.
10083{_}5021{_}_Prometheus Unbound_.
10083{_}5022{_}Great moments, whether of pain, surprise, or terror, awaken in the startled breast very different emotions from those we are led to anticipate from the agitation caused by lesser experiences.
10083{_}5023{_}As Carmel disclosed her features to the court, my one absorbing thought was: Would she look at me?
10083{_}5024{_}Could I hope for a glance of her eye?
10083{_}5025{_}Did I wish it?
10083{_}5026{_}My question was answered before Mr. Moffat had regained his place and turned to address the court.
10083{_}5027{_}As her gaze passed from her brother's face, it travelled slowly and with growing hesitation over the countenances of those near her, on and on past the judge, past the jury, until they reached the spot where I sat.
10083{_}5028{_}There they seemed to falter, and the beating of my heart became so loud that I instinctively shrank away from my neighbour.
10083{_}5029{_}By so doing, I drew her eye, which fell full upon mine for one overwhelming minute; then she shrank and looked away, but not before the colour had risen in a flood to her cheek.
10083{_}5030{_}The hope which had sprung to life under her first beautiful aspect, vanished in despair at sight of this flush.
10083{_}5031{_}For it was not one of joy, or surprise, or even of unconscious sympathy.
10083{_}5032{_}It was the banner of a deep, unendurable shame.
10083{_}5033{_}Versed in her every expression, I could not mistake the language of her dismayed soul, at this, the most critical instant of her life.
10083{_}5034{_}She had hoped to find me absent; she was overwhelmed to find me there.
10083{_}5035{_}Could she, with a look, have transported me a thousand miles from this scene of personal humiliation and unknown, unimaginable outcome, she would have bestowed that look and ignored the consequences.
10083{_}5036{_}Nor was I behind her in the reckless passion of the moment.
10083{_}5037{_}Could I, by means of a wish, have been transported those thousand miles, I should even now have been far from a spot where, in the face of a curious crowd, busy in associating us together, I must submit to the terror of hearing her speak and betray herself to these watchful lawyers, and to the just and impartial mind of the presiding judge.
10083{_}5038{_}But the days of magic had passed.
10083{_}5039{_}I could not escape the spot; I could not escape her eye.
10083{_}5040{_}The ordeal to which she was thus committed, I must share.
10083{_}5041{_}As she advanced step by step upon her uncertain road, it would be my unhappy fate to advance with her, in terror of the same pitfalls, with our faces set towards the same precipice--slipping, fainting, experiencing agonies together.
10083{_}5042{_}She knew my secret, and I, alas!
10083{_}5043{_}knew hers.
10083{_}5044{_}So I interpreted this intolerable, overwhelming blush.
10083{_}5045{_}Recoiling from the prospect, I buried my face in my hands, and so missed the surprising sight of this young girl, still in her teens, conquering a dismay which might well unnerve one of established years and untold experiences.
10083{_}5046{_}In a few minutes, as I was afterward told by my friends, her features had settled into a strange placidity, undisturbed by the levelled gaze of a hundred eyes.
10083{_}5047{_}Her whole attention was concentrated on her brother, and wavered only, when the duties of the occasion demanded a recognition of the various gentlemen concerned in the trial.
10083{_}5048{_}Mr. Moffat prefaced his examination by the following words:  "May it please your Honour, I wish to ask the indulgence of the court in my examination of this witness.
10083{_}5049{_}She is just recovering from a long and dangerous illness; and while I shall endeavour to keep within the rules of examination, I shall be grateful for any consideration which may be shown her by your Honour and by the counsel on the other side."
10083{_}5050{_}Mr. Fox at once rose.
10083{_}5051{_}He had by this time recovered from his astonishment at seeing before him, and in a fair state of health, the young girl whom he had every reason to believe to be still in a condition of partial forgetfulness at Lakewood, and under the care of a woman entirely in his confidence and under his express orders.
10083{_}5052{_}He had also mastered his chagrin at the triumph which her presence here, and under these dramatic circumstances, had given his adversary.
10083{_}5053{_}Moved, perhaps, by Miss Cumberland's beauty, which he saw for the first time--or, perhaps, by the spectacle of this beauty devoting its first hours of health to an attempt to save a brother, of whose precarious position before the law she had been ignorant up to this time--or more possibly yet, by a fear that it might be bad tactics to show harshness to so interesting a personality before she had uttered a word of testimony, he expressed in warmer tones than usual, his deep desire to extend every possible indulgence.
10083{_}5054{_}Mr. Moffat bowed his acknowledgments, and waited for his witness to take the oath, which she did with a simple grace which touched all hearts, even that of her constrained and unreconciled brother.
10083{_}5055{_}Compelled by the silence and my own bounding pulses to look at her in my own despite, I caught the sweet and elevated look with which she laid her hand on the Book, and asked myself if her presence here was not a self-accusation, which would bring satisfaction to nobody--which would sink her and hers into an ignominy worse than the conviction of the brother whom she was supposedly there to save.
10083{_}5056{_}Tortured by this fear, I awaited events in indescribable agitation.
10083{_}5057{_}The cool voice of Mr. Moffat broke in upon my gloom.
10083{_}5058{_}Carmel had reseated herself, after taking the oath, and the customary question could be heard:  "Your name, if you please."
10083{_}5059{_}"Carmel Cumberland."
10083{_}5060{_}"Do you recognise the prisoner, Miss Cumberland?"
10083{_}5061{_}"Yes; he is my brother."
10083{_}5062{_}A thrill ran through the room.
10083{_}5063{_}The lingering tone, the tender accent, told.
10083{_}5064{_}Some of the feeling she thus expressed seemed to pass into every heart which contemplated the two.
10083{_}5065{_}From this moment on, he was looked upon with less harshness; people showed a disposition to discern innocence, where, perhaps, they had secretly desired, until now, to discover guilt.
10083{_}5066{_}"Miss Cumberland, will you be good enough to tell us where you were, at or near the hour of ten, on the evening of your sister's death?"
10083{_}5067{_}"I was in the club-house--in the house you call The Whispering Pines."
10083{_}5068{_}At this astounding reply, unexpected by every one present save myself and the unhappy prisoner, incredulity, seasoned with amazement, marked every countenance.
10083{_}5069{_}Carmel Cumberland in the club-house that night--she who had been found at a late hour, in her own home, injured and unconscious!
10083{_}5070{_}It was not to be believed--or it would not have been, if Arthur with less self-control than he had hitherto maintained, had not shown by his morose air and the silent drooping of his head that he accepted this statement, wild and improbable as it seemed.
10083{_}5071{_}Mr. Fox, whose mind without doubt had been engaged in a debate from the first, as to the desirability of challenging the testimony of this young girl, whose faculties had so lately recovered from a condition of great shock and avowed forgetfulness that no word as yet had come to him of her restored health, started to arise at her words; but noting the prisoner's attitude, he hastily reseated himself, realising, perhaps, that evidence of which he had never dreamed lay at the bottom of the client's manner and the counsel's complacency.
10083{_}5072{_}If so, then his own air of mingled disbelief and compassionate forbearance might strike the jury unfavourably; while, on the contrary, if his doubts were sound, and the witness were confounding the fancies of her late delirium with the actual incidents of this fatal night, then would he gain rather than lose by allowing her to proceed until her testimony fell of its own weight, or succumbed before the fire of his cross-examination.
10083{_}5073{_}Modifying his manner, he steadied himself for either exigency, and, in steadying himself, steadied his colleagues also.
10083{_}5074{_}Mr. Moffat, who saw everything, smiled slightly as he spoke encouragingly to his witness, and propounded his next question:  "Miss Cumberland, was your sister with you when you went to the club-house?"
10083{_}5075{_}"No; we went separately"  "How?
10083{_}5076{_}Will you explain?"
10083{_}5077{_}"I drove there.
10083{_}5078{_}I don't know how Adelaide went."
10083{_}5079{_}"You drove there?"
10083{_}5080{_}"Yes.
10083{_}5081{_}I had Arthur harness up his horse for me and I drove there."
10083{_}5082{_}A moment of silence; then a slow awakening--on the part of judge, jury, and prosecution--to the fact that the case was taking a turn for which they were ill-prepared.
10083{_}5083{_}To Mr. Moffat, it was a moment of intense self-congratulation, and something of the gratification he felt crept into his voice as he said:  "Miss Cumberland, will you describe this horse?"
10083{_}5084{_}"It was a grey horse.
10083{_}5085{_}It has a large black spot on its left shoulder."

10083{_}5091{_}Entrancement had now seized upon every mind.
10083{_}5092{_}Even if her testimony were not true, but merely the wanderings of a mind not fully restored, the interest of it was intense.
10083{_}5093{_}Mr. Fox, glancing at the jury, saw there would be small use in questioning at this time the mental capacity of the witness.
10083{_}5094{_}This was a story which all wished to hear.
10083{_}5095{_}Perhaps he wished to hear it, too.
10083{_}5096{_}Mr. Moffat rose to more than his accustomed height.

10083{_}5100{_}I drove back in my brother's cutter and being all alone just as before, I put the horse away myself, and went into my empty home and up to Adelaide's room, where I lost consciousness."
10083{_}5101{_}The excitement, which had been seething, broke out as she ceased; but the judge did not need to use his gavel, or the officers of the court exert their authority.
10083{_}5102{_}At Mr. Moffat's lifted hand, the turmoil ceased as if by magic.
10083{_}5103{_}"Miss Cumberland, do you often ride out alone on nights like that?"
10083{_}5104{_}"I never did before.
10083{_}5105{_}I would not have dared to do it then, if I had not taken a certain precaution."
10083{_}5106{_}"And what was this precaution?"
10083{_}5107{_}"I wore an old coat of my brother's over my dress, and one of his hats on my head."
10083{_}5108{_}It was out--the fact for the suppression of which I had suffered arrest without a word; because of which Arthur had gone even further, and submitted to trial with the same constancy.
10083{_}5109{_}Instinctively, his eyes and mine met, and, at that moment, there was established between us an understanding that was in strong contrast to the surrounding turmoil, which now exceeded all limits, as the highly wrought up spectators realised that these statements, if corroborated, destroyed one of the strongest points which had been made by the prosecution.
10083{_}5110{_}This caused a stay in the proceedings until order was partially restored, and the judge's voice could be heard in a warning that the court-room would be cleared of all spectators if this break of decorum was repeated.
10083{_}5111{_}Meanwhile, my own mind had been busy.
10083{_}5112{_}I had watched Arthur; I had watched Mr. Moffat.

10083{_}5226{_}"I answered the note."

10083{_}5228{_}"I refused Mr. Ranelagh's request.
10083{_}5229{_}I said that I could not do what he asked, and told him to wait till the next day, and he would see how I felt towards him and towards Adelaide.

10083{_}5231{_}I could not write much.

10083{_}5234{_}"Suffering in my mind.

10083{_}5243{_}He was a guest next door, and I carried the note in to him."

10083{_}5275{_}During all this Mr. Fox had sat by, understanding his right to object to the witness's mixed statements of fact and of feelings, and quite confident that his objections would be sustained.
10083{_}5276{_}But he had determined long since that he would not interrupt the witness in her relation.
10083{_}5277{_}The air of patience he assumed was sufficiently indicative of his displeasure, and he confined himself to this.
10083{_}5278{_}Mr. Moffat understood, and testified his appreciation by a slight bow.

10083{_}5280{_}"Arthur's room is near, and Adelaide's far off; but I went to Adelaide's first.
10083{_}5281{_}Her door was shut and when I went to open it I found it locked.

10083{_}5366{_}I was going out, when I remembered there would be no light in the club-house.
10083{_}5367{_}I had put a box of matches in my bag while I was upstairs, but I needed a candle.
10083{_}5368{_}Slipping back, I took a candlestick and candle from the dining-room mantel, and finding that the bag would not hold them, thrust them into the pocket of the coat I wore, and quickly left the house.
10083{_}5369{_}Jenny was in the stable, all harnessed; and hesitating no longer, I got in among the bear-skins and drove swiftly away."
10083{_}5370{_}There was a moment's silence.
10083{_}5371{_}Carmel had paused, and was sitting with her hand on her heart, looking past judge, past jury, upon the lonely and desolate scene in which she at this moment moved and suffered.
10083{_}5372{_}An inexpressible fatality had entered into her tones, always rich and resonant with feeling.
10083{_}5373{_}No one who listened could fail to share the dread by which she was moved.
10083{_}5374{_}District Attorney Fox fumbled with his papers, and endeavoured to maintain his equanimity and show an indifference which his stern but fascinated glances at the youthful witness amply belied.
10083{_}5375{_}He was biding his time, but biding it in decided perturbation of mind.
10083{_}5376{_}Neither he nor any one else, unless it were Moffat, could tell whither this tale tended.
10083{_}5377{_}While she held the straight course which had probably been laid out for her, he failed to object; but he could not prevent the subtle influence of her voice, her manner, and her supreme beauty on the entranced jury.
10083{_}5378{_}Nevertheless, his pencil was busy; he was still sufficiently master of himself for that.
10083{_}5379{_}Mr. Moffat, quite aware of the effect which was being produced on every side, but equally careful to make no show of it, put in a commonplace question at this point, possibly to rouse the witness from her own abstraction, possibly to restore the judicial tone of the inquiry.
10083{_}5380{_}"How did you leave the stable-door?"
10083{_}5381{_}"Open."
10083{_}5382{_}"Can you tell us what time it was when you started?"
10083{_}5383{_}"No.
10083{_}5384{_}I did not look.
10083{_}5385{_}Time meant nothing to me.
10083{_}5386{_}I drove as fast as I could, straight down the hill, and out towards The Whispering Pines.
10083{_}5387{_}I had seen Adelaide in her window as I went flying by the house, but not a soul on the road, nor a sign of life, near or far.
10083{_}5388{_}The whistle of a train blew as I stopped in the thicket near the club-house door.
10083{_}5389{_}If it was the express train, you can tell--"  "Never mind the _if_" said Mr. Moffat.

10083{_}5391{_}Go on with what you did."
10083{_}5392{_}"I tied up my horse; then I went into the house.
10083{_}5393{_}I had used Mr. Ranelagh's key to open the door and for some reason I took it out of the lock when I got in, and put the whole bunch back into my satchel.
10083{_}5394{_}But I did not lock the door.
10083{_}5395{_}Then I lit my candle and then--I went upstairs."
10083{_}5396{_}Fainter and fainter the words fell, and slower and slower heaved the youthful breast under her heavily pressing palm.
10083{_}5397{_}Mr. Moffat made a sign across the court-room, and I saw Dr. Carpenter get up and move nearer to the witness stand.
10083{_}5398{_}But she stood in no need of his help.
10083{_}5399{_}In an instant her cheek flushed; the eye I watched with such intensity of wonder that apprehension unconsciously left me, rose, glowed, and fixed itself at last--not on the judge, not on the prisoner, not even on that prisoner's counsel--but on _me_; and as the soft light filled my soul and awoke awe, where it had hitherto awakened passion, she quietly said:  "There is a room upstairs, in the club-house, where I have often been with Adelaide.
10083{_}5400{_}It has a fireplace in it, and I had seen a box there, half filled with wood the day before.
10083{_}5401{_}This is the room I went to, and here I built a fire.
10083{_}5402{_}When it was quite bright, I took out something I had brought in my satchel, and thrust it into the flame.
10083{_}5403{_}Then I got up and walked away.
10083{_}5404{_}I--I did not feel very strong, and sank on my knees when I got to the couch, and buried my face in my arms.
10083{_}5405{_}But I felt better when I came back to the fire again, and very brave till I caught a glimpse of my face in the mirror over the mantelpiece.
10083{_}5406{_}That--that unnerved me, and I think I screamed.
10083{_}5407{_}Some one screamed, and I think it was I. I know my hands went out--I saw them in the glass; then they fell straight down at my side, and I looked and looked at myself till I saw all the terror go out of my face, and when it was quite calm again, I stooped down and pulled out the little tongs I had been heating in the fire, and laid them quick--quick, before I could be sorry again--right across my cheek, and then--"  Uproar in the court.
10083{_}5408{_}If she had screamed when she said she did, so some one cried out loudly now.
10083{_}5409{_}I think that pitiful person was myself.
10083{_}5410{_}They say I had been standing straight up in my place for the last two minutes.
10083{_}5411{_}XXX  "CHOOSE"  Let me have A dram of poison; such soon speeding geer As will disperse itself through all the veins, That the life-weary taker may fall dead.
10083{_}5412{_}Come, bitter conduct, come unsavoury guide!
10083{_}5413{_}Thou desperate pilot, now at once run on The dashing rocks thy sea-sick weary bark.
10083{_}5414{_}_Romeo and Juliet_   "I have not finished," were the first words we heard, when order was restored, and we were all in a condition to listen again.
10083{_}5415{_}"I had to relate what you have just heard, that you might understand what happened next.
10083{_}5416{_}I was not used to pain, and I could never have kept on pressing those irons to my cheek if I had not had the strength given me by my own reflection in the glass.
10083{_}5417{_}When I thought the burn was quite deep enough, I tore the tongs away, and was lifting them to the other cheek when I saw the door behind me open, inch by inch, as thought pushed by hesitating touches.
10083{_}5418{_}"Instantly, I forgot my pain, almost my purpose, watching that door.
10083{_}5419{_}I saw it slowly swing to its full width, and disclose my sister standing in the gap, with a look and in an attitude which terrified me more than the fire had done.
10083{_}5420{_}Dropping the tongs, I turned and faced her, covering my cheek instinctively with my hand.
10083{_}5421{_}"I saw her eyes run over my elaborate dinner dress--my little hand-bag, and the candle burning in a room made warm with a fire on the hearth.
10083{_}5422{_}This, before she spoke a single word.
10083{_}5423{_}Then, with a deep labouring breath, she looked me in the eye again, with the simple question:  "'And where is he?'"
10083{_}5424{_}Carmel's head had drooped at this, but she raised it almost instantly.
10083{_}5425{_}Mine did not rise so readily.

10083{_}5441{_}She glanced down at the words; and I felt like falling at her feet, she looked so miserable.

10083{_}5449{_}You are a child, a warm-hearted and passionate child; but you do not know a woman's heart.

10083{_}5451{_}I doubt if any one does--even he.
10083{_}5452{_}Cares have warped my life.
10083{_}5453{_}I do not quarrel with these cares; I only say that they have robbed me of what makes girlhood lovely.
10083{_}5454{_}Duty is a stern task-master; and sternness, coming early into one's life, hardens its edges, but does not sap passion from the soul or devotion from the heart.
10083{_}5455{_}I was ready for joy when it came, but I was no longer capable of bestowing it.

10083{_}5464{_}My very heart seemed frozen, and the silence was dreadful.
10083{_}5465{_}But I could not speak, I could not answer her.
10083{_}5466{_}"'You have everything,' she now went on.
10083{_}5467{_}'Why did you rob me of my one happiness?
10083{_}5468{_}And you have robbed me.
10083{_}5469{_}I have seen your smile when his head turned your way.
10083{_}5470{_}It was the smile which runs before a promise.
10083{_}5471{_}I know it; I have had that smile in my heart a long, long time--but it never reached my lips.

10083{_}5481{_}"I tell you this--I bare my sister's broken heart to you, giving you her very words, sacred as they are to me and--and to others, who are present, and must listen to all I say--because it is right that you should understand her frenzy, and know all that passed between us in that awful hour."
10083{_}5482{_}This was irregular, highly irregular--but District Attorney Fox sat on, unmoved.
10083{_}5483{_}Possibly he feared to prejudice the jury; possibly he recognised the danger of an interruption now, not only to the continuity of her testimony, but to the witness herself; or--what is just as likely--possibly he cherished a hope that, in giving her a free rein and allowing her to tell her story thus artlessly, she would herself supply the clew he needed to reconstruct his case on the new lines upon which it was being slowly forced by these unexpected revelations.
10083{_}5484{_}Whatever the cause, he let these expressions of feeling pass.
10083{_}5485{_}At a gesture from Mr. Moffat, Carmel proceeded:  "I tottered at this threat; and she, a mother to me from my cradle, started instinctively to catch me; but the feeling left her before she had taken two steps, and she stopped still.
10083{_}5486{_}'Drop your hand,' she cried.
10083{_}5487{_}'I want to see your whole face while I ask you one last question.
10083{_}5488{_}I could not read the note.
10083{_}5489{_}Why did you come _here?_ I dropped my hand, and she stood staring; then she uttered a cry and ran quickly towards me.
10083{_}5490{_}'What is it?'
10083{_}5491{_}she cried.
10083{_}5492{_}'What has happened to you?
10083{_}5493{_}Is it the shadow or--'  "I caught her by the hand.
10083{_}5494{_}I could speak now.
