10083{_}5498{_}'You say that to-morrow I shall be free to receive notes.
10083{_}5499{_}He will not wish to write them, tomorrow.
10083{_}5500{_}The beauty he liked is gone.
10083{_}5501{_}If it weighed overmuch with him, then you and I are on a plane again--or I am on an inferior one.
10083{_}5502{_}Your joy will be sweeter for this break!'
10083{_}5503{_}"She started, raised my head from her shoulder, looked at me and shuddered--but no longer with hate.
10083{_}5504{_}'Carmel!'
10083{_}5505{_}she whispered, 'the story--the story I read you of Francis the First and--'  "'Yes,' I agreed, 'that made me think,' Her knees bent under her; she sank at my feet, but her eyes never left my face.
10083{_}5506{_}'And--and Elwood?'
10083{_}5507{_}'He knows nothing.
10083{_}5508{_}I did not make up my mind till to-night.
10083{_}5509{_}Adelaide, it had to be.
10083{_}5510{_}I hadn't the strength to--to leave you all, or--or to say no, if he ever asked me to my face what he asked me in that note,'  "And then I tried to lift her; but she was kissing my feet, kissing my dress, sobbing out her life on my hands.
10083{_}5511{_}Oh, I was happy!
10083{_}5512{_}My future looked very simple to me.
10083{_}5513{_}But my cheek began to burn, and instinctively I put up my hand.
10083{_}5514{_}This brought her to her feet.
10083{_}5515{_}'You are suffering,' she cried.
10083{_}5516{_}'You must go home, at once, at once, while I telephone to Dr. Carpenter,' 'We will go together,' I said.
10083{_}5517{_}'We can telephone from there.'
10083{_}5518{_}But at this, the awful look came back into her face, and seeing her forget my hurt, I forgot it, too, in dread of what she would say when she found strength to speak.
10083{_}5519{_}"It was worse than anything I had imagined; she refused absolutely to go back home.
10083{_}5520{_}'Carmel,' said she, 'I have done injustice to your youth.
10083{_}5521{_}You love him, too--not like a child but a woman.
10083{_}5522{_}The tangle is worse than I thought; your heart is caught in it, as well as mine, and you shall have your chance.
10083{_}5523{_}My death will give it to you.'
10083{_}5524{_}I shook my head, pointing to my cheek.
10083{_}5525{_}She shook hers, and quietly, calmly said, 'You have never looked so beautiful.
10083{_}5526{_}Should we go back together and take up the old life, the struggle which has undermined my conscience and my whole existence would only begin again.
10083{_}5527{_}I cannot face that ordeal, Carmel.
10083{_}5528{_}The morning light would bring me daily torture, the evening dusk a night of blasting dreams.
10083{_}5529{_}We three cannot live in this world together.
10083{_}5530{_}I am the least loved and so I should be the one to die.
10083{_}5531{_}I am determined, Carmel.
10083{_}5532{_}Life, with me, has come to this.'
10083{_}5533{_}"I tried to dissuade her.
10083{_}5534{_}I urged every plea, even that of my own sacrifice.
10083{_}5535{_}But she was no more her natural self.
10083{_}5536{_}She had taken up the note and read it during my entreaties, and my words fell on deaf ears.
10083{_}5537{_}'Why, these words have killed me,' she cried crumpling the note in her hand.
10083{_}5538{_}'What will a little poison do?
10083{_}5539{_}It can only finish what he has begun.'
10083{_}5540{_}"Poison!
10083{_}5541{_}I remembered how I had heard her pushing about bottles in the medicine cabinet, and felt my legs grow weak and my head swim.
10083{_}5542{_}'You will not!'
10083{_}5543{_}I cried, watching her hand, in terror of seeing it rise to her breast.
10083{_}5544{_}'You are crazed to-night; to-morrow you will feel differently.'
10083{_}5545{_}"But the fixed set look of her bleak face gave me no hope.
10083{_}5546{_}'I shall never feel differently.
10083{_}5547{_}If I do not end it to-night, I shall do so soon.
10083{_}5548{_}When a heart like mine goes down, it goes down forever,' I could only shudder.
10083{_}5549{_}I did not know what to do, or which way to turn.
10083{_}5550{_}She stood between me and the door, and her presence was terrible.
10083{_}5551{_}'When I came here,' she said, 'I brought a bottle of cordial with me and three glasses.
10083{_}5552{_}I brought a little phial of poison too, once ordered for sickness.
10083{_}5553{_}I expected to find Elwood here.
10083{_}5554{_}If I had, I meant to drop the poison into one glass, and then fill them all up with the cordial.
10083{_}5555{_}We should have drunk, each one of us his glass, and one of us would have fallen.
10083{_}5556{_}I did not care which, you or Elwood or myself.
10083{_}5557{_}But he is not here, and the cast of the die is between us two, unless you wish a certainty, Carmel,--in which case I will pour out but one glass and drink that myself.'
10083{_}5558{_}"She was in a fever, now, and desperate.
10083{_}5559{_}Death was in the room; I felt it in my lifted hair, and in her strangely drawn face.
10083{_}5560{_}If I screamed, who would hear me?
10083{_}5561{_}I never thought of the telephone, and I doubt if she would have let me use it then.
10083{_}5562{_}The power she had always exerted over me was very strong in her at this moment; and not till afterwards did it cross my mind that I had never asked her how she got to the house, or whether we were as much alone in the building as I believed.
10083{_}5563{_}"'Shall I drink alone?'
10083{_}5564{_}she repeated, and I cried out 'No'; at which her hand went to her breast, as I had so long expected, and I saw the glitter of a little phial as she drew it forth.
10083{_}5565{_}"'Oh, Adelaide!'
10083{_}5566{_}I began; but she heeded me no more than the dead.
10083{_}5567{_}"On leaving home, she had put on a long coat with pockets and this coat was still on her, and the pockets gaping.
10083{_}5568{_}Thrusting her other hand into one of these, she drew out a little flask covered with wicker, and set it on a stand beside her.
10083{_}5569{_}Then she pulled out two small glasses, and set them down also, and then she turned her back.
10083{_}5570{_}I could hear the drop, drop of the liquor; and, dark as the room was, it seemed to turn darker, till I put out my hands like one groping in a sudden night.
10083{_}5571{_}But everything cleared before me when she turned around again.
10083{_}5572{_}Features set like hers force themselves to be seen.
10083{_}5573{_}"She advanced, a glass in either hand.
10083{_}5574{_}As she came, the floor swayed, and the walls seemed to bow together; but they did not sway her.
10083{_}5575{_}Step by step, she drew near, and when she reached my side she smiled in my face once.
10083{_}5576{_}Then she said: 'Choose aright, dear heart.
10083{_}5577{_}Leave the poisoned one for me.'
10083{_}5578{_}"Fascinated, I stared at one glass, then at the other.
10083{_}5579{_}Had either of her hands trembled, I should have grasped at the glass it held; but not a tremor shook those icy fingers, nor did her eyes wander to the right hand or to the left.
10083{_}5580{_}'Adelaide!'
10083{_}5581{_}I shrieked out.
10083{_}5582{_}'Toss them behind you.
10083{_}5583{_}Let us live--live!'
10083{_}5584{_}But she only reiterated that awful word: 'Choose!'
10083{_}5585{_}and I dare not hesitate longer, lest I lose my chance to save her.
10083{_}5586{_}Groping, I touched a glass--I never knew which one--and drawing it from her fingers, I lifted it to my mouth.
10083{_}5587{_}Instantly her other hand rose.
10083{_}5588{_}'I don't know which is which, myself,' she said, and drank.
10083{_}5589{_}That made me drink, also.
10083{_}5590{_}"The two glasses sent out a clicking sound as we set them back on the stand.
10083{_}5591{_}Then we waited, looking at each other.
10083{_}5592{_}'Which?'
10083{_}5593{_}her lips seemed to say.
10083{_}5594{_}'Which?'
10083{_}5595{_}In another moment we knew.
10083{_}5596{_}'Your choice was the right one,' said she, and she sank back into a chair.
10083{_}5597{_}'Don't leave me!'
10083{_}5598{_}she called out, for I was about to run shrieking out into the night.
10083{_}5599{_}'I--I am happy now that it is all settled; but I do not want to die alone.
10083{_}5600{_}Oh, how hot I am!'
10083{_}5601{_}And leaping up, she flung off her coat, and went gasping about the room for air.
10083{_}5602{_}When she sank down again, it was on the lounge; and again I tried to fly for help, and again she would not let me.
10083{_}5603{_}Suddenly she started up, and I saw a great change in her.
10083{_}5604{_}The heavy, leaden look was gone; tenderness had come back to her eyes, and a human anxious expression to her whole face.
10083{_}5605{_}'I have been mad!'
10083{_}5606{_}she cried.
10083{_}5607{_}'Carmel, Carmel, what have I done to you, my more than sister--my child, my child!'
10083{_}5608{_}"I tried to soothe her--to keep down my awful fear and soothe her.
10083{_}5609{_}But the nearness of death had calmed her poor heart into its old love and habitual thoughtfulness.
10083{_}5610{_}She was terrified at my position.
10083{_}5611{_}She recalled our mother, and the oath she had taken at that mother's death-bed to protect me and care for me and my brother.
10083{_}5612{_}'And I have failed to do either,' she cried.
10083{_}5613{_}'Arthur, I have alienated, and you I am leaving to unknown trouble and danger,'  "She was not to be comforted.
10083{_}5614{_}I saw her life ebbing and could do nothing.
10083{_}5615{_}She clung to me while she called up all her powers, and made plans for me and showed me a way of escape.
10083{_}5616{_}I was to burn the note, fling two of the glasses from the window and leave the other and the deadly phial near her hand.
10083{_}5617{_}This, before I left the room.
10083{_}5618{_}Then I was to call up the police and say there was something wrong at the club-house, but I was not to give my name or ever acknowledge I was there.
10083{_}5619{_}'Nothing can save trouble,' she said, 'but that trouble must not come near you.
10083{_}5620{_}Swear that you will heed my words--swear that you will do what I say,'  "I swore.
10083{_}5621{_}All that she asked I promised.
10083{_}5622{_}I was almost dying, too; and had the light gone out and the rafters of the house fallen in and buried us both, it would have been better.
10083{_}5623{_}But the light burned on, and the life in her eyes faded out, and the hands grasping mine relaxed.
10083{_}5624{_}I heard one little gasp; then a low prayer: 'Tell Arthur never--never--again to--' Then--silence!"
10083{_}5625{_}Sobs--cries--veiled faces--then silence in the courtroom, too.
10083{_}5626{_}It was broken but by one sound, a heartrending sigh from the prisoner.
10083{_}5627{_}But nobody looked at him, and thank God!--nobody looked at me.
10083{_}5628{_}Every eye was on the face of this young girl, whose story bore such an impress of truth, and yet was so contradictory of all former evidence.
10083{_}5629{_}What revelations were yet to follow.
10083{_}5630{_}It would seem that she was speaking of her sister's death.
10083{_}5631{_}But her sister had not died that way; her sister had been strangled.
10083{_}5632{_}Could this dainty creature, with beauty scarred and yet powerfully triumphant, be the victim of an hallucination as to the cause of that scar and the awesome circumstances which attended its infliction?
10083{_}5633{_}Or, harder still to believe, were these soul-compelling tones, these evidences of grief, this pathetic yielding to the rights of the law in face of the heart's natural shrinking from disclosures sacred as they were tragic--were these the medium by which she sought to mislead justice and to conceal truth?
10083{_}5634{_}Even I, with my memory of her looks as she faltered down the staircase on that memorable night--pale, staring, her left hand to her cheek and rocking from side to side in pain or terror--could not but ask if this heart-rending story did not involve a still more terrible sequel.
10083{_}5635{_}I searched her face, and racked my very soul, in my effort to discern what lay beneath this angelic surface--beneath this recital which if it were true and the whole truth, would call not only for the devotion of a lifetime, but a respect transcending love and elevating it to worship.
10083{_}5636{_}But, in her cold and quiet features, I could detect nothing beyond the melancholy of grief; and the suspense from which all suffered, kept me also on the rack, until at a question from Mr. Moffat she spoke again, and we heard her say:  "Yes, she died that way, with her hands in mine.
10083{_}5637{_}There was no one else by; we were quite alone."
10083{_}5638{_}That settled it, and for a moment the revulsion of feeling threatened to throw the court into tumult.
10083{_}5639{_}But one thing restrained them.
10083{_}5640{_}Not the look of astonishment on her face, not the startled uplift of Arthur's head, not the quiet complacency which in an instant replaced the defeated aspect of the district attorney; but the gesture and attitude of Mr. Moffat, the man who had put her on the stand, and who now from the very force of his personality, kept the storm in abeyance, and by his own composure, forced back attention to his witness and to his own confidence in his case.
10083{_}5641{_}This result reached, he turned again towards Carmel, with renewed respect in his manner and a marked softening in his aspect and voice.
10083{_}5642{_}"Can you fix the hour of this occurrence?"
10083{_}5643{_}he asked.
10083{_}5644{_}"In any way can you locate the time?"
10083{_}5645{_}"No; for I did not move at once.
10083{_}5646{_}I felt tied to that couch; I am very young, and I had never seen death before.
10083{_}5647{_}When I did get up, I hobbled like an old woman and almost went distracted; but came to myself as I saw the note on the floor--the note I was told to burn.
10083{_}5648{_}Lifting it, I moved towards the fireplace, but got a fright on the way, and stopped in the middle of the floor and looked back.
10083{_}5649{_}I thought I had heard my sister speak!
10083{_}5650{_}"But the fancy passed as I saw how still she lay, and I went on, after a while, and threw the note into the one small flame which was all that was left of the fire.
10083{_}5651{_}I saw it caught by a draught from the door behind me, and go flaming up the chimney.
10083{_}5652{_}"Some of my trouble seemed to go with it, but a great one yet remained.
10083{_}5653{_}I didn't know how I could ever turn around again and see my sister lying there behind me, with her face fixed in death, for which I was, in a way, responsible.
10083{_}5654{_}I was abjectly frightened, and knelt there a long time, praying and shuddering, before I could rise again to my feet and move about as I had to, since God had not stricken me and I must live my life and do what my sister had bidden me.
10083{_}5655{_}Courage--such courage as I had had--was all gone from me now; and while I knew there was something else for me to do before I left the room, I could not remember what it was, and stood hesitating, dreading to lift my eyes and yet feeling that I ought to, if only to aid my memory by a look at my sister's face.
10083{_}5656{_}"Suddenly I did look up, but it did not aid my memory; and, realising that I could never think with that lifeless figure before me, I lifted a pillow from the window-seat near by and covered her face.
10083{_}5657{_}I must have done more; I must have covered the whole lounge with pillows and cushions; for, presently my mind cleared again, and I recollected that it was something about the poison.
10083{_}5658{_}I was to put the phial in her hand--or was I to throw it from the window?
10083{_}5659{_}Something was to be thrown from the window--it must be the phial.
10083{_}5660{_}But I couldn't lift the window, so having found the phial standing on the table beside the little flask, I carried it into the closet where there was a window opening inward, and I dropped it out of that, and thought I had done all.
10083{_}5661{_}But when I came back and saw Adelaide's coat lying in a heap where she had thrown it, I recalled that she had said something about this but what, I didn't know.
10083{_}5662{_}So I lifted it and put it in the closet--why, I cannot say.
10083{_}5663{_}Then I set my mind on going home.
10083{_}5664{_}"But there was something to do first--something not in that room.
10083{_}5665{_}It was a long time before it came to me; then the sight of the empty hall recalled it.
10083{_}5666{_}The door by which Adelaide had come in had never been closed, and as I went towards it I remembered the telephone, and that I was to call up the police.
10083{_}5667{_}Lifting the candle, I went creeping towards the front hall.
10083{_}5668{_}Adelaide had commanded me, or I could never have accomplished this task.
10083{_}5669{_}I had to open a door; and when it swung to behind me and latched, I turned around and looked at it, as if I never expected it to open again.
10083{_}5670{_}I almost think I fainted, if one can faint standing, for when I knew anything, after the appalling latching of that door, I was in quite another part of the room and the candle which I still held, looked to my dazed eyes shorter than when I started with it from the place where my sister lay.
10083{_}5671{_}"I was wasting time.
10083{_}5672{_}The thought drove me to the table.
10083{_}5673{_}I caught up the receiver and when central answered, I said something about The Whispering Pines and wanting help.
10083{_}5674{_}This is all I remember about that.
10083{_}5675{_}"Some time afterward--I don't know when--I was stumbling down the stairs on my way out.
10083{_}5676{_}I had gone to--to the room again for my little bag; for the keys were in it, and I dared not leave them.
10083{_}5677{_}But I didn't stay a minute, and I cast but one glance at the lounge.
10083{_}5678{_}What happened afterward is like a dream to me.
10083{_}5679{_}I found the horse; the horse found the road; and some time later I reached home.
10083{_}5680{_}As I came within sight of the house I grew suddenly strong again.
10083{_}5681{_}The open stable door reminded me of my duty, and driving in, I quickly unharnessed Jenny and put her away.
10083{_}5682{_}Then I dragged the cutter into place, and hung up the harness.
10083{_}5683{_}Lastly, I locked the door and carried the key with me into the house and hung it up on its usual nail in the kitchen.
10083{_}5684{_}I had obeyed Adelaide, and now I would go to my room.
10083{_}5685{_}That is what she would wish; but I don't know whether I did this or not.
10083{_}5686{_}My mind was full of Adelaide till confusion came--then darkness--and then a perfect blank."
10083{_}5687{_}She had finished; she had done as she had been asked; she had told the story of that evening as she knew it, from the family dinner till her return home after midnight--and the mystery of Adelaide's death was as great as ever.
10083{_}5688{_}Did she realise this?
10083{_}5689{_}Had I wronged this lovely, tempestuous nature by suspicions which this story put to blush?
10083{_}5690{_}I was happy to think so--madly, unreasonably happy.
10083{_}5691{_}Whatever happened, whatever the future threatening Arthur or myself, it was rapture to be restored to right thinking as regards this captivating and youthful spirit, who had suffered and must suffer always--and all through me, who thought it a pleasant pastime to play with hearts, and awoke to find I was playing with souls, and those of the two noblest women I had ever known!
10083{_}5692{_}The cutting in of some half dozen questions from Mr. Moffat, which I scarcely heard and which did not at all affect the status of the case as it now stood, served to cool down the emotional element, which had almost superseded the judicial, in more minds than those of the jury; and having thus prepared his witness for an examination at other and less careful hands, he testified his satisfaction at her replies, and turned her over to the prosecution, with the time-worn phrase:  "Mr. District Attorney, the witness is yours."
10083{_}5693{_}Mr. Fox at once arose; the moment was ripe for conquest.
10083{_}5694{_}He put his most vital question first:  "In all this interview with your sister, did you remark any discoloration on her throat?"
10083{_}5695{_}The witness's lips opened; surprise spoke from her every feature.
10083{_}5696{_}"Discoloration?"
10083{_}5697{_}she repeated.
10083{_}5698{_}"I do not know what you mean."
10083{_}5699{_}"Any marks darker than the rest of her skin on her throat or neck?"
10083{_}5700{_}"No.
10083{_}5701{_}Adelaide had a spotless skin.
10083{_}5702{_}It looked like marble as she lay there.
10083{_}5703{_}No, I saw no marks."
10083{_}5704{_}"Miss Cumberland, have you heard or read a full account of this trial?"
10083{_}5705{_}She was trembling, now.
10083{_}5706{_}Was it from fear of the truth, or under that terror of the unknown embodied in this question.
10083{_}5707{_}"I do not know," said she.
10083{_}5708{_}"What I heard was from my nurse and Mr. Moffat.
10083{_}5709{_}I read very little, and that was only about the first days of the trial and the swearing in of jurors.
10083{_}5710{_}This is the first time I have heard any mention made of marks, and I do not understand yet what you allude to."
10083{_}5711{_}District Attorney Fox cast at Mr. Moffat an eloquent glance, which that gentleman bore unmoved; then turning back to the witness, he addressed her in milder and more considerate tones than were usually heard from him in cross-examination, and asked: "Did you hold your sister's hands all the time she lay dying, as you thought, on the lounge?"
10083{_}5712{_}"Yes, yes."
10083{_}5713{_}"And did not see her raise them once?"
10083{_}5714{_}"No, no."
10083{_}5715{_}"How was it when you let go of them?
10083{_}5716{_}Where did they fall then?"
10083{_}5717{_}"On her breast.
10083{_}5718{_}I laid them down softly and crossed them.
10083{_}5719{_}I did not leave her till I had done this and closed her eyes."
10083{_}5720{_}"And what did you do then?"
10083{_}5721{_}"I went for the note, to burn it."
10083{_}5722{_}"Miss Cumberland, in your direct examination, you said that you stopped still as you crossed the floor at the time, thinking that your sister called, and that you looked back at her to see."
10083{_}5723{_}"Yes, sir."
10083{_}5724{_}"Were her hands crossed then?"
10083{_}5725{_}"Yes, sir, just the same."
10083{_}5726{_}"And afterward, when you came from the fire after waiting some little time for courage?"
10083{_}5727{_}"Yes, yes.
10083{_}5728{_}There were no signs of movement.
10083{_}5729{_}Oh, she was dead--quite dead."
10083{_}5730{_}"No statements, Miss Cumberland.
10083{_}5731{_}She looked the same, and you saw no change in the position of her hands?"
10083{_}5732{_}"None; they were just as I left them."
10083{_}5733{_}"Miss Cumberland, you have told us how, immediately after taking the poison, she staggered about the room, and sank first on a chair and then on the lounge.
10083{_}5734{_}Were you watching her then?"
10083{_}5735{_}"Oh, yes--every moment."
10083{_}5736{_}"Her hands as well as her face?"
10083{_}5737{_}"I don't know about her hands.
10083{_}5738{_}I should have observed it if she had done anything strange with them."
10083{_}5739{_}"Can you say she did not clutch or grip her throat during any of this time?"
10083{_}5740{_}"Yes, yes.
10083{_}5741{_}I couldn't have forgotten it, if she had done that.
10083{_}5742{_}I remember every move she made so well.
10083{_}5743{_}She didn't do that."
10083{_}5744{_}Mr. Fox's eye stole towards the jury.
10083{_}5745{_}To a man, they were alert, anxious for the next question, and serious, as the arbitrators of a man's life ought to be.
10083{_}5746{_}Satisfied, he put the question: "When, after telephoning, you returned to the room where your sister lay, you glanced at the lounge?"
10083{_}5747{_}"Yes, I could not help it."
10083{_}5748{_}"Was it in the same condition as when you left--the pillows, I mean?"
10083{_}5749{_}"I--I think so.
10083{_}5750{_}I cannot say; I only half looked; I was terrified by it."
10083{_}5751{_}"Can you say they had not been disturbed?"
10083{_}5752{_}"No.
10083{_}5753{_}I can say nothing.
10083{_}5754{_}But what does--"  "Only the answer, Miss Cumberland.
10083{_}5755{_}Can you tell us how those pillows were arranged?"
10083{_}5756{_}"I'm afraid not.
10083{_}5757{_}I threw them down quickly, madly, just as I collected them.
10083{_}5758{_}I only know that I put the window cushion down first.
10083{_}5759{_}The rest fell anyhow; but they quite covered her--quite."
10083{_}5760{_}"Hands and face?"
10083{_}5761{_}"Her whole body."
10083{_}5762{_}"And did they cover her quite when you came back?"
10083{_}5763{_}"They must have--Wait--wait!
10083{_}5764{_}I know I have no right to say that, but I cannot swear that I saw any change."
10083{_}5765{_}"Can you swear that there was no change--that the pillows and the window cushion lay just as they did when you left the room?"
10083{_}5766{_}She did not answer.
10083{_}5767{_}Horror seemed to have seized hold of her.
10083{_}5768{_}Her eyes, fixed on the attorney's face, wavered and, had they followed their natural impulse, would have turned towards her brother, but her fear--possibly her love--was her counsellor and she brought them back to Mr. Fox.
10083{_}5769{_}Resolutely, but with a shuddering insight of the importance of her reply, she answered with that one weighty monosyllable which can crush so many hopes, and even wreck a life:  "No."
10083{_}5770{_}At the next moment she was in Dr. Carpenter's arms.
10083{_}5771{_}Her strength had given way for the time, and the court was hastily adjourned, to give her opportunity for rest and recuperation.
10083{_}5772{_}XXXI  "WERE HER HANDS CROSSED THEN?"
10083{_}5773{_}Threescore and ten I can remember well: Within the volume of which time, I have seen Hours dreadful, and things strange; but this sore night Hath trifled former knowledge.
10083{_}5774{_}_Macbeth_.
10083{_}5775{_}I shall say nothing about myself at this juncture.
10083{_}5776{_}That will come later.
10083{_}5777{_}I have something of quite different purport to relate.
10083{_}5778{_}When I left the court-room with the other witnesses, I noticed a man standing near the district attorney.
10083{_}5779{_}He was a very plain man--with no especial claims to attention, that I could see, yet I looked at him longer than I did at any one else, and turned and looked at him again as I passed through the doorway.
10083{_}5780{_}Afterward I heard that he was Sweetwater, the detective from New York who had had so much to do in unearthing the testimony against Arthur,--testimony which in the light of this morning's revelations, had taken on quite a new aspect, as he was doubtless the first to acknowledge.
10083{_}5781{_}It was the curious blending of professional disappointment and a personal and characteristic appreciation of the surprising situation, which made me observe him, I suppose.
10083{_}5782{_}Certainly my heart and mind were full enough not to waste looks on a commonplace stranger unless there had been some such overpowering reason.
10083{_}5783{_}I left him still talking to Mr. Fox, and later received this account of the interview which followed between them and Dr. Perry.
10083{_}5784{_}"Is this girl telling the truth?"
10083{_}5785{_}asked District Attorney Fox, as soon as the three were closeted and each could speak his own mind.
10083{_}5786{_}"Doctor, what do you think?"
10083{_}5787{_}"I do not question her veracity in the least.
10083{_}5788{_}A woman who for purely moral reasons could defy pain and risk the loss of a beauty universally acknowledged as transcendent, would never stoop to falsehood even in her desire to save a brother's life.
10083{_}5789{_}I have every confidence in her.
10083{_}5790{_}Fox, and I think you may safely have the same."
10083{_}5791{_}"You believe that she burnt herself--intentionally?"
10083{_}5792{_}"I wouldn't disbelieve it--you may think me sentimental; I knew and loved her father--for any fortune you might name."
10083{_}5793{_}"Say that you never knew her father; say that you had no more interest in the girl or the case, than the jurors have?
10083{_}5794{_}What then---?
10083{_}5795{_}"I should believe her for humanity's sake; for the sake of the happiness it gives one to find something true and strong in this sordid work-a-day world--a jewel in a dust-heap.
10083{_}5796{_}Oh, I'm a sentimentalist, I acknowledge."
10083{_}5797{_}Mr. Fox turned to Sweetwater.
10083{_}5798{_}"And you?"
10083{_}5799{_}"Mr. Fox, have you those tongs?"
10083{_}5800{_}"Yes, I forgot; they were brought to my office, with the other exhibits.
10083{_}5801{_}I attached no importance to them, and you will probably find them just where I thrust them into the box marked 'Cumb.'"
10083{_}5802{_}They were in the district attorney's office, and Sweetwater at once rose and brought forward the tongs.
10083{_}5803{_}"There is my answer," he said pointing significantly at one of the legs.
10083{_}5804{_}The district attorney turned pale, and motioned Sweetwater to carry them back.
10083{_}5805{_}He sat silent for a moment, and then showed that he was a man.
10083{_}5806{_}"Miss Cumberland has my respect," said he.
10083{_}5807{_}Sweetwater came back to his place.
10083{_}5808{_}Dr. Perry waited.
10083{_}5809{_}Finally Mr. Fox turned to him and put the anticipated question:  "You are satisfied with your autopsy?
10083{_}5810{_}Miss Cumberland's death was due to strangulation and not to the poison she took?"
10083{_}5811{_}"That was what I swore to, and what I should have to swear to again if you placed me back on the stand.
10083{_}5812{_}The poison, taken with her great excitement, robbed her of consciousness, but there was too little of it, or it was too old and weakened to cause death.
10083{_}5813{_}She would probably have revived, in time; possibly did revive.
10083{_}5814{_}But the clutch of those fingers was fatal; she could not survive it.
10083{_}5815{_}It costs me more than you can ever understand to say this, but questions like yours must be answered.
10083{_}5816{_}I should not be an honest man otherwise."
10083{_}5817{_}Sweetwater made a movement.
10083{_}5818{_}Mr. Fox turned and looked at him critically.
10083{_}5819{_}"Speak out," said he.
10083{_}5820{_}But Sweetwater had nothing to say.
10083{_}5821{_}Neither had Dr. Perry.
10083{_}5822{_}The oppression of an unsolved problem, involving lives of whose value each formed a different estimate, was upon them all; possibly heaviest upon the district attorney, the most serious portion of whose work lay still before him.
10083{_}5823{_}To the relief of all, Carmel was physically stronger than we expected when she came to retake the stand in the afternoon.
10083{_}5824{_}But she had lost a little of her courage.
10083{_}5825{_}Her expectation of clearing her brother at a word had left her, and with it the excitation of hope.
10083{_}5826{_}Yet she made a noble picture as she sat there, meeting, without a blush, but with an air of sweet humility impossible to describe, the curious, all-devouring glances of the multitude, some of them anxious to repeat the experience of the morning; some of them new to the court, to her, and the cause for which she stood.
10083{_}5827{_}Mr. Fox kept nobody waiting.
10083{_}5828{_}With a gentleness such as he seldom showed to any witness for the defence, he resumed his cross-examination by propounding the following question:  "Miss Cumberland, in your account of the final interview you had with your sister, you alluded to a story you had once read together.
10083{_}5829{_}Will you tell us the name of this story?"
10083{_}5830{_}"It was called 'A Legend of Francis the First.'
10083{_}5831{_}It was not a novel, but a little tale she found in some old magazine.
10083{_}5832{_}It had a great effect upon us; I have never forgotten it."
10083{_}5833{_}"Can you relate this tale to us in a few words?"
10083{_}5834{_}"I will try.
10083{_}5835{_}It was very simple; it merely told how a young girl marred her beauty to escape the attentions of the great king, and what respect he always showed her after that, even calling her sister."
10083{_}5836{_}Was the thrill in her voice or in my own heart, or in the story--emphasised as it was by her undeniable attempt upon her own beauty?
10083{_}5837{_}As that last word fell so softly, yet with such tender suggestion, a sensation of sympathy passed between us for the first time; and I knew, from the purity of her look and the fearlessness of this covert appeal to one she could not address openly, that the doubts I had cherished of her up to this very moment were an outrage and that were it possible or seemly, I should be bowed down in the dust at her feet--in reality, as I was in spirit.
10083{_}5838{_}Others may have shared my feeling; for the glances which flew from her face to mine were laden with an appreciation of the situation, which for the moment drove the prisoner from the minds of all, and centred attention on this tragedy of souls, bared in so cruel a way to the curiosity of the crowd.
10083{_}5839{_}I could not bear it.
10083{_}5840{_}The triumph of my heart battled with the shame of my fault, and I might have been tempted into some act of manifest imprudence, if Mr. Fox had not cut my misery short by recalling attention to the witness, with a question of the most vital importance.
10083{_}5841{_}"While you were holding your sister's hands in what you supposed to be her final moments, did you observe whether or not she still wore on her finger the curious ring given her by Mr. Ranelagh, and known as her engagement ring?"
10083{_}5842{_}"Yes--I not only saw it, but felt it.
10083{_}5843{_}It was the only one she wore on her left hand."
10083{_}5844{_}The district attorney paused.
10083{_}5845{_}This was an admission unexpected, perhaps, by himself, which it was desirable to have sink into the minds of the jury.
10083{_}5846{_}The ring had not been removed by Adelaide herself; it was still on her finger as the last hour drew nigh.
10083{_}5847{_}An awful fact, if established--telling seriously against Arthur.
10083{_}5848{_}Involuntarily I glanced his way.
10083{_}5849{_}He was looking at me.
10083{_}5850{_}The mutual glance struck fire.
10083{_}5851{_}What I thought, he thought--but possibly with a difference.
10083{_}5852{_}The moment was surcharged with emotion for all but the witness herself.
10083{_}5853{_}She was calm; perhaps she did not understand the significance of the occasion.
10083{_}5854{_}Mr. Fox pressed his advantage.
10083{_}5855{_}"And when you rose from the lounge and crossed your sister's hands?"
10083{_}5856{_}"It was still there; I put that hand uppermost."
10083{_}5857{_}"And left the ring on?"
10083{_}5858{_}"Oh, yes--oh, yes."
10083{_}5859{_}Her whole attitude and face were full of protest.
10083{_}5860{_}"So that, to the best of your belief, it was still on your sister's finger when you left the room?"
10083{_}5861{_}"Certainly, sir, certainly."
10083{_}5862{_}There was alarm in her tone now, she was beginning to see that her testimony was not as entirely helpful to Arthur as she had been led to expect.
10083{_}5863{_}In her helplessness, she cast a glance of entreaty at her brother's counsel.
10083{_}5864{_}But he was busily occupied with pencil and paper, and she received no encouragement unless it was from his studiously composed manner and general air of unconcern.
10083{_}5865{_}She did not know--nor did I know then--what uneasiness such an air may cover.
10083{_}5866{_}Mr. Fox had followed her glances, and perhaps understood his adversary better than she did; for he drew himself up with an appearance of satisfaction as he asked very quietly:  "What material did you use in lighting the fire on the club-house hearth?"
10083{_}5867{_}"Wood from the box, and a little kindling I found there."
10083{_}5868{_}"How large was this kindling?"
10083{_}5869{_}"Not very large; some few stray pieces of finer wood I picked out from she rest."
10083{_}5870{_}"And how did you light these?"
10083{_}5871{_}"With some scraps of paper I brought in my bag?"
10083{_}5872{_}"Oh--you brought scraps?"
10083{_}5873{_}"Yes.
10083{_}5874{_}I had seen the box, seen the wood, but knew the wood would not kindle without paper.
10083{_}5875{_}So I brought some."
10083{_}5876{_}"Did the fire light quickly?"
10083{_}5877{_}"Not very quickly."
10083{_}5878{_}"You had trouble with it?"
10083{_}5879{_}"Yes, sir.
10083{_}5880{_}But I made it burn at last."
10083{_}5881{_}"Are you in the habit of kindling fires in your own home?"
10083{_}5882{_}"Yes, on the hearth."
10083{_}5883{_}"You understand them?"
10083{_}5884{_}"I have always found it a very simple matter, if you have paper and enough kindling."
10083{_}5885{_}"And the draught is good."
10083{_}5886{_}"Yes, sir."
10083{_}5887{_}"Wasn't the draught good at the club-house?"
10083{_}5888{_}"Not at first."
10083{_}5889{_}"Oh--not at first.
10083{_}5890{_}When did you see a change?"
10083{_}5891{_}"When the note I was trying to burn flew up the chimney."
10083{_}5892{_}"I see.
10083{_}5893{_}Was that after or before the door opened?"
10083{_}5894{_}"After."
10083{_}5895{_}"Did the opening of this door alter the temperature of the room?"
10083{_}5896{_}"I cannot say; I felt neither heat nor cold at any time."
10083{_}5897{_}"Didn't you feel the icy cold when you opened the dressing-closet window to throw out the phial?"
10083{_}5898{_}"I don't remember."
10083{_}5899{_}"Wouldn't you remember if you had?"
10083{_}5900{_}"I cannot say."
10083{_}5901{_}Can you say whether you noticed any especial chill in the hall when you went out to telephone?"
10083{_}5902{_}"My teeth were chattering but--"  "Had they chattered before?"
10083{_}5903{_}"They may have.
10083{_}5904{_}I only noticed it then; but--"  "The facts, Miss Cumberland.
10083{_}5905{_}Your teeth chattered while you were passing through the hall.
10083{_}5906{_}Did this keep up after you entered the room where you found the telephone?"
10083{_}5907{_}"I don't remember; I was almost insensible."
10083{_}5908{_}"You don't remember that they did?"
10083{_}5909{_}"No, sir."
10083{_}5910{_}"But you do remember having shut the door behind you?"
10083{_}5911{_}"Yes."
10083{_}5912{_}An open window in the hall!
10083{_}5913{_}That was what he was trying to prove--open at this time.
10083{_}5914{_}From the expression of such faces of the jury as I could see, I think he had proved it.
10083{_}5915{_}The next point he made was in the same line.
10083{_}5916{_}Had she, in all the time she was in the building, heard any noises she could not account for?
10083{_}5917{_}"Yes, many times."
10083{_}5918{_}"Can you describe these noises?"
10083{_}5919{_}"No; they were of all kinds.
10083{_}5920{_}The pines sighed continually; I knew it was the pines, but I had to listen.
10083{_}5921{_}Once I heard a rushing sound--it was when the pines stopped swaying for an instant--but I don't know what it was.

10083{_}5925{_}I didn't think of it at the time, but it might have been."

10083{_}5952{_}"Yes, sir."
10083{_}5953{_}Oh, the sinister memories!

10083{_}5955{_}And some one had been there before me!

10083{_}5958{_}There was nothing to be learned from him now; the hour for self-betrayal was past.
10083{_}5959{_}I began to have a hideous doubt.
10083{_}5960{_}Carmel being innocent, who could be guilty but he.

10083{_}5962{_}The misery under which I had suffered was only lightened, not removed.
10083{_}5963{_}We were still to see evil days.

10083{_}5965{_}I must not reckon without Moffat.
10083{_}5966{_}He had sprung one surprise.

10083{_}5969{_}What was Mr. Fox asking her now?

10083{_}6088{_}"Yes."
10083{_}6089{_}"And then locked them out?"
10083{_}6090{_}"I didn't care--I didn't care."
10083{_}6091{_}An infinite number of questions followed.
10083{_}6092{_}The poor child was near fainting, but bore up wonderfully notwithstanding, contradicting herself but seldom; and then only from lack of understanding the question, or from sheer fatigue.
10083{_}6093{_}Mr. Fox was considerate, and Mr. Moffat interrupted but seldom.
10083{_}6094{_}All could see that this noble-hearted girl, this heroine of all hearts was trying to tell the truth, and sympathy was with her, even that of the prosecution.
10083{_}6095{_}But certain facts had to be brought out, among them the blowing off of her hat on that hurried drive home through the ever thickening snow-storm--a fact easily accounted for, when one considered the thick coils of hair over which it had been drawn.
10083{_}6096{_}The circumstances connected with her arrival at the house were all carefully sifted, but nothing new came up, nor was her credibility as a witness shaken.
10083{_}6097{_}The prosecution had lost much by this witness, but it had also gained.
10083{_}6098{_}No doubt now remained that the ring was still on the victim's hand when she succumbed to the effects of the poison; and the possibility of another presence in the house during the fateful interview just recorded, had been strengthened, rather than lessened, by Carmel' s hesitating admissions.
10083{_}6099{_}And so the question hung poised, and I was expecting to see her dismissed from the stand, when the district attorney settled himself again into his accustomed attitude of inquiry, and launched this new question:  "When you went into the stable to unharness your horse, what did you do with the little bag you carried?"
10083{_}6100{_}"I took it out of the cutter."
10083{_}6101{_}"What, then?"
10083{_}6102{_}"Set it down somewhere."
10083{_}6103{_}"Was there anything in the bag?"
10083{_}6104{_}"Not now.
10083{_}6105{_}I had left the tongs at the club-house, and the paper I had burned.
10083{_}6106{_}I took nothing else."
10083{_}6107{_}"How about the candlestick?"
10083{_}6108{_}"That I carried in one of the pockets of my coat.
10083{_}6109{_}That I left, too."
10083{_}6110{_}"Was that all you carried in your pockets?"
10083{_}6111{_}"Yes--the candlestick and the candle.
10083{_}6112{_}The candlestick on one side and the candle on the other."
10083{_}6113{_}"And these you did not have on your return?"
10083{_}6114{_}"No, I left both."
10083{_}6115{_}"So that your pockets were empty--entirely empty--when you drove into your own gate?"
10083{_}6116{_}"Yes, sir, so far as I know.
10083{_}6117{_}I never looked into them."
10083{_}6118{_}"And felt nothing there?"
10083{_}6119{_}"No, sir."
10083{_}6120{_}"Took nothing out?"
10083{_}6121{_}"No, sir."
10083{_}6122{_}"Then or when you unharnessed your horse, or afterward, as you passed back to the house?"
10083{_}6123{_}"No, sir."
10083{_}6124{_}"What path did you take in returning to the house?"
10083{_}6125{_}"There is only one."
10083{_}6126{_}"Did you walk straight through it?"
10083{_}6127{_}"As straight as I could.
10083{_}6128{_}It was snowing heavily, and I was dizzy and felt strange, I may have zigzagged a little."
10083{_}6129{_}"Did you zigzag enough to go back of the stable?"
10083{_}6130{_}"Oh, no."
10083{_}6131{_}"You are sure that you did not wander in back of the stable?"
10083{_}6132{_}"As sure as I can be of anything."
10083{_}6133{_}"Miss Cumberland, I have but a few more questions to ask.
10083{_}6134{_}Will you look at this portion of a broken bottle?"
10083{_}6135{_}"I see it, sir."
10083{_}6136{_}"Will you take it in your hand and examine it carefully?"
10083{_}6137{_}She reached out her hand; it was trembling visibly and her face expressed a deep distress, but she took the piece of broken bottle and looked at it before passing it back.
10083{_}6138{_}"Miss Cumberland, did you ever see that bit of broken glass before?"
10083{_}6139{_}She shook her head.
10083{_}6140{_}Then she cast a quick look at her brother, and seemed to gain an instantaneous courage.
10083{_}6141{_}"No," said she.
10083{_}6142{_}"I may have seen a whole bottle like that, at some time in the club-house, but I have no memory of this broken end--none at all."
10083{_}6143{_}"I am obliged to you, Miss Cumberland.
10083{_}6144{_}I will trouble you no more to-day."
10083{_}6145{_}Then he threw up his head and smiled a slow, sarcastic smile at Mr. Moffat.
10083{_}6146{_}XXXII  AND I HAD SAID NOTHING!
10083{_}6147{_}O my soul's joy!
10083{_}6148{_}If after every tempest come such calms May the winds blow till they have wakened death!
10083{_}6149{_}_Othello_.
10083{_}6150{_}I had always loved her; that I knew even in the hour of my darkest suspicion--but now I felt free to worship her.
10083{_}6151{_}As the thought penetrated my whole being, it made the night gladsome.
10083{_}6152{_}Whatever awaited her, whatever awaited Arthur, whatever awaited me, she had regenerated me.
10083{_}6153{_}A change took place that night in my whole nature, in my aspect of life and my view of women.
10083{_}6154{_}One fact rode triumphant above all other considerations and possible distresses.
10083{_}6155{_}Fate--I was more inclined now to call it Providence--had shown me the heart of a great and true woman; and I was free to expend all my best impulses in honouring her and loving her, whether she ever looked my way again, received or even acknowledged a homage growing out of such wrong as I had done her and her unfortunate sister.
10083{_}6156{_}It set a star in my firmament.
10083{_}6157{_}It turned down all the ill-written and besmirched leaves in my book of life and opened up a new page on which her name, written in letters of gold, demanded clean work in the future and a record which should not shame the aura surrounding that pure name.
10083{_}6158{_}Sorrow for the past, dread of the future--both were lost in the glad rebound of my distracted soul.
10083{_}6159{_}The night was dedicated to joy, and to joy alone.
10083{_}6160{_}The next day being Sunday, I had ample time for the reaction bound to follow hours of such exaltation.
10083{_}6161{_}I had no wish for company.
10083{_}6162{_}I even denied myself to Clifton.
10083{_}6163{_}The sight of a human face was more than I could bear unless it were the one face; and that I could not hope for.
10083{_}6164{_}But the desire to see her, to hear from her--if only to learn how she had endured the bitter ordeal of the day before--soon became unbearable.
10083{_}6165{_}I must know this much at any cost to her feelings or to mine.
10083{_}6166{_}After many a struggle with myself, I called up Dr. Carpenter on the telephone.
10083{_}6167{_}From him I learned that she was physically prostrated, but still clear in mind and satisfied of her brother's innocence.
10083{_}6168{_}This latter statement might mean anything; but imparted by him to me, it seemed to be capable of but one interpretation.
10083{_}6169{_}I must be prepared for whatever distrust of myself this confidence carried with it.
10083{_}6170{_}This was intolerable.
10083{_}6171{_}I had to speak; I had to inquire if she had yet heard the real reason why I was the first to be arrested.
10083{_}6172{_}A decided "No," cut short that agony.
10083{_}6173{_}I could breathe again and proffer a humble request.
10083{_}6174{_}"Doctor, I cannot approach her; I cannot even write,--it would seem too presumptuous.
10083{_}6175{_}But tell her, as you find the opportunity, how I honour her.
10083{_}6176{_}Do not let her remain under the impression that I am not capable of truly feeling what she has borne and must still bear."
10083{_}6177{_}"I will do what I can," was his reply, and he mercifully cut short the conversation.
10083{_}6178{_}This was the event of the morning.
10083{_}6179{_}In the afternoon I sat in my window thinking.
10083{_}6180{_}My powers of reasoning had returned, and the insoluble problem of Adelaide's murder occupied my whole mind.
10083{_}6181{_}With Carmel innocent, who was there left to suspect?
10083{_}6182{_}Not Arthur.
10083{_}6183{_}His fingers were as guiltless as my own of those marks on her throat.
10083{_}6184{_}Of this I was convinced, difficult as it made my future.
10083{_}6185{_}My mind refused to see guilt in a man who could meet my eye with just the look he gave me on leaving the courtroom, at the conclusion of his sister's triumphant examination.
10083{_}6186{_}It was a momentary glance, but I read it, I am sure, quite truthfully.
10083{_}6187{_}"You are the man," it said; but not in the old, bitter, and revengeful way voiced by his tongue before we came together in the one effort to save Carmel from what, in our short-sightedness and misunderstanding of her character, we had looked upon as the worst of humiliations and the most desperate of perils.
10083{_}6188{_}There was sadness in his conviction and an honest man's regret--which, if noted by those about us--was far more dangerous to my good name than the loudest of denunciations or the most acrimonious of assaults.
10083{_}6189{_}It put me in the worst of positions.
10083{_}6190{_}But one chance remained for me now.
10083{_}6191{_}The secret man of guilt might yet come to light; but how or through whose agency, I found myself unable to conceive.
10083{_}6192{_}I had neither the wit nor the experience to untangle this confused web.
10083{_}6193{_}Should I find the law in shape to deal with it?
10083{_}6194{_}A few days would show.
10083{_}6195{_}With the termination of Arthur's trial, the story of my future would begin.
10083{_}6196{_}Meanwhile, I must have patience and such strength as could be got from the present.
10083{_}6197{_}And so the afternoon passed.
10083{_}6198{_}With the coming on of night, my mood changed.
10083{_}6199{_}I wanted air, movement.
10083{_}6200{_}The closeness of my rooms had become unbearable.
10083{_}6201{_}As soon as the lamps were lit in the street, I started out and I went--toward the cemetery.
10083{_}6202{_}I had no motive in choosing this direction for my walk.
10083{_}6203{_}The road was an open one, and I should neither avoid people nor escape the chilly blast blowing directly in my face from the northeast.
10083{_}6204{_}Whim, or shall I not say, true feeling, carried me there though I was quite conscious, all the time, of a strong desire to see Ella Fulton and learn from her the condition of affairs--whether she was at peace, or in utter disgrace, with her parents.
10083{_}6205{_}It was a cold night, as I have said, and there were but few people in the streets.
10083{_}6206{_}On the boulevard I met nobody.
10083{_}6207{_}As I neared the cemetery, I passed one man; otherwise I was, to all appearance, alone on this remote avenue.
10083{_}6208{_}The effect was sinister, or my mood made it so; yet I did not hasten my steps; the hours till midnight had to be lived through in some way, and why not in this?
10083{_}6209{_}No companion would have been welcome, and had the solitude been less perfect, I should have murmured at the prospect of intrusion.
10083{_}6210{_}The cemetery gates were shut.
10083{_}6211{_}This I had expected, but I did not need to enter the grounds to have a view of Adelaide's grave.
10083{_}6212{_}The Cumberland lot occupied a knoll in close proximity to the fence, and my only intention had been to pass this spot and cast one look within, in memory of Adelaide.
10083{_}6213{_}To reach the place, however, I had to turn a corner, and on doing so I saw good reason, as I thought, for not carrying out my intention at this especial time.
10083{_}6214{_}Some man--I could not recognise him from where I stood--had forestalled me.
10083{_}6215{_}Though the night was a dark one, sufficient light shone from the scattered lamps on the opposite side of the way for me to discern his intent figure, crouching against the iron bars and gazing, with an intentness which made him entirely oblivious of my presence, at the very plot--and on the very grave--which had been the end of my own pilgrimage.
10083{_}6216{_}So motionless he stood, and so motionless I myself became at this unexpected and significant sight, that I presently imagined I could hear his sighs in the dread quiet into which the whole scene had sunk.
10083{_}6217{_}Grief, deeper than mine, spoke in those labouring breaths.
10083{_}6218{_}Adelaide was mourned by some one as I, for all my remorse, could never mourn her.
10083{_}6219{_}_And I did not know the man_.
10083{_}6220{_}Was not this strange enough to rouse my wonder?
10083{_}6221{_}I thought so, and was on the point of satisfying this wonder by a quick advance upon this stranger, when there happened an uncanny thing, which held me in check from sheer astonishment.
10083{_}6222{_}I was so placed, in reference to one of the street lamps I have already mentioned, that my shadow fell before me plainly along the snow.
10083{_}6223{_}This had not attracted my attention until, at the point of moving, I cast my eyes down and saw two shadows where only one should be.
10083{_}6224{_}As I had heard no one behind me, and had supposed myself entirely alone with the man absorbed in contemplation of Adelaide's grave, I experienced a curious sensation which, without being fear, held me still for a moment, with my eyes on this second shadow.
10083{_}6225{_}It did not move, any more than mine did.
10083{_}6226{_}This was significant, and I turned.
10083{_}6227{_}A man stood at my back--not looking at me but at the fellow in front of us.
10083{_}6228{_}A quiet "hush!"
10083{_}6229{_}sounded in my ear, and again I stood still.
10083{_}6230{_}But only for an instant.
10083{_}6231{_}The man at the fence--aroused by my movement, perhaps--had turned, and, seeing our two figures, started to fly in the opposite direction.
10083{_}6232{_}Instinctively I darted forward in pursuit, but was soon passed by the man behind me.
10083{_}6233{_}This caused me to slacken; for I had recognised this latter, as he flew by, as Sweetwater, the detective, and knew that he would do this work better than myself.
10083{_}6234{_}But I reckoned without my host.
10083{_}6235{_}He went only as far as the spot where the man had been standing.
10083{_}6236{_}When, in my astonishment, I advanced upon him there, he wheeled about quite naturally in my direction and, accosting me by name, remarked, in his genial off-hand manner:  "There is no need for us to tire our legs in a chase after that man.
10083{_}6237{_}I know him well enough."
10083{_}6238{_}"And who--" I began.
10083{_}6239{_}A quizzical smile answered me.
10083{_}6240{_}The light was now in our faces, and I had a perfect view of his.
10083{_}6241{_}Its expression quite disarmed me; but I knew, as well as if he had spoken, that I should receive no other reply to my half-formed question.
10083{_}6242{_}"Are you going back into town?"
10083{_}6243{_}he asked, as I paused and looked down at the umbrella swinging in his hand.
10083{_}6244{_}I was sure that he had not held this umbrella when he started by me on the run.
10083{_}6245{_}"If so, will you allow me to walk beside you for a little way?"
10083{_}6246{_}I could not refuse him; besides, I was not sure that I wanted to.
10083{_}6247{_}Homely as any man I had ever seen, there was a magnetic quality in his voice and manner that affected even one so fastidious as myself.
10083{_}6248{_}I felt that I had rather talk to him, at that moment, than to any other person I knew.
10083{_}6249{_}Of course, curiosity had something to do with it, and that community of interest which is the strongest bond that can link two people together.
10083{_}6250{_}"You are quite welcome," said I; and again cast my eye at the umbrella.
10083{_}6251{_}"You are wondering where I got this," he remarked, looking down at it in his turn.
10083{_}6252{_}"I found it leaning against the fence.
10083{_}6253{_}It gives me all the clue I need to our fleet-footed friend.
10083{_}6254{_}Mr. Ranelagh, will you credit me with good intentions if I ask a question or two which you may or may not be willing to answer?"
10083{_}6255{_}"You may ask what you will," said I.
10083{_}6256{_}"I have nothing to conceal, since hearing Miss Cumberland's explanation of her presence at The Whispering Pines."
10083{_}6257{_}"Ah!"
10083{_}6258{_}The ejaculation was eloquent.
10083{_}6259{_}So was the silence which followed it.
10083{_}6260{_}Without good reason, perhaps, I felt the strain upon my heart loosen a little.
10083{_}6261{_}Was it possible that I should find a friend in this man?
10083{_}6262{_}"The question I am going to ask," he continued presently, "is one which you may consider unpardonable.
10083{_}6263{_}Let me first express an opinion.
10083{_}6264{_}You have not told all that you know of that evening's doings."
10083{_}6265{_}This called for no reply and I made none.
10083{_}6266{_}"I can understand your reticence, if your knowledge included the fact of Miss Cumberland's heroic act and her sister's manner of death at the club-house."
10083{_}6267{_}"But it did not," I asserted, with deliberate emphasis.
10083{_}6268{_}"I knew nothing of either.
10083{_}6269{_}My arrival happened later.
10083{_}6270{_}Miss Cumberland's testimony gave me my first enlightenment on these points.
10083{_}6271{_}But I did know that the two sisters were there together, for I had a glimpse of the younger as she was leaving the house."
10083{_}6272{_}"You had.
10083{_}6273{_}And are willing to state it now?"
10083{_}6274{_}"Assuredly.
10083{_}6275{_}But any testimony of that kind is for the defence, and your interests are all with the prosecution.
10083{_}6276{_}Mr. Moffat is the man who should talk to me."
10083{_}6277{_}"Does he know it?"
10083{_}6278{_}"Yes."
10083{_}6279{_}"Who told him?"
10083{_}6280{_}"I did."
10083{_}6281{_}"You?"
10083{_}6282{_}"Yes, it was my duty."
10083{_}6283{_}"You are interested then in seeing young Cumberland freed?"
10083{_}6284{_}"I must be; he is innocent."
10083{_}6285{_}The man at my side turned, shot at me one glance which I met quite calmly, then, regulating his step by mine, moved on silently for a moment--thinking, as it appeared to me, some very serious thoughts.
10083{_}6286{_}It was not until we had traversed a whole block in this way that he finally put his question.
10083{_}6287{_}Whether it was the one he had first had in mind, I cannot say.
10083{_}6288{_}"Mr. Ranelagh, will you tell me why, when you found yourself in such a dire extremity as to be arrested for this crime, on evidence as startling as to call for all and every possible testimony to your innocence, you preserved silence in regard to a fact which you must have then felt would have secured you a most invaluable witness?
10083{_}6289{_}I can understand why Mr. Cumberland has been loth to speak of his younger sister's presence in the club-house on that night; but his reason was not your reason.
10083{_}6290{_}Yet you have been as hard to move on this point as he."
10083{_}6291{_}Then it was I regretted my thoughtless promise to be candid with this man.
10083{_}6292{_}To answer were impossible, yet silence has its confidences, too.
10083{_}6293{_}In my dilemma, I turned towards him and just then we stepped within the glare of an electric light pouring from some open doorway.
10083{_}6294{_}I caught his eye, and was astonished at the change which took place in him.
10083{_}6295{_}"Don't answer," he muttered, volubly.
10083{_}6296{_}"It isn't necessary.
10083{_}6297{_}I understand the situation, now, and you shall never regret that you met Caleb Sweetwater on your walk this evening.
10083{_}6298{_}Will you trust me, sir?
10083{_}6299{_}A detective who loves his profession is no gabbler.
10083{_}6300{_}Your secret is as safe with me as if you had buried it in the grave."
10083{_}6301{_}And I had said nothing!
10083{_}6302{_}He started to go, then he stopped suddenly and observed, with one of his wise smiles:  "I once spent several minutes in Miss Carmel Cumberland's room, and I saw a cabinet there which I found it very hard to understand.
10083{_}6303{_}But its meaning came to me later.
10083{_}6304{_}I could not rest till it did."
10083{_}6305{_}At the next moment he was half way around a corner, and in another, out of sight.
10083{_}6306{_}This was the evening's event.
10083{_}6307{_}XXXIII  THE ARROW OF DEATH  O if you rear this house against this house, It will the wofulest division prove That ever fell upon this cursed earth.
10083{_}6308{_}_Prometheus Unbound_.
10083{_}6309{_}In my first glance around the court-room the next morning, I sought first for Carmel and then for the detective Sweetwater.
10083{_}6310{_}Neither was visible.
10083{_}6311{_}But this was not true of Ella.
10083{_}6312{_}She had come in on her father's arm, closely followed by the erect figure of her domineering mother.
10083{_}6313{_}As I scrutinised the latter's bearing, I seemed to penetrate the mystery of her nature.
10083{_}6314{_}Whatever humiliation she may have felt at the public revelation of her daughter's weakness, it had been absorbed by her love for that daughter, or had been forced, through the agency of her indomitable will, to become a ministrant to her pride which was unassailable.
10083{_}6315{_}She had accepted the position exacted from her by the situation, and she looked for no loss of prestige, either on her daughter's or her own account.
10083{_}6316{_}Such was the language of her eyes; and it was a language which should have assured Ella that she had a better friend in her mother than she had ever dreamed of.
10083{_}6317{_}The entrance of the defendant cut short my contemplation of any mere spectator.
10083{_}6318{_}The change in him was so marked that I was conscious of it before I really saw him.
10083{_}6319{_}Every eye had reflected it, and it was no surprise to me when I noted the relieved, almost cheerful aspect of his countenance as he took his place and met his counsel's greeting with a smile--the first, I believe, which had been seen on his face since his sister's death.
10083{_}6320{_}That counsel I had already noted.
10083{_}6321{_}He was cheerful also, but with a restrained cheerfulness.
10083{_}6322{_}His task was not yet over, and the grimness of Mr. Fox, and the non-committal aspect of the jurymen, proved that it was not to be made too easy for him.
10083{_}6323{_}The crier announced the opening of the court, and the defence proceeded by the calling of Ella Fulton to the witness stand.
10083{_}6324{_}I need not linger over her testimony.
10083{_}6325{_}It was very short and contained but one surprise.
10083{_}6326{_}She had stated under direct examination that she had waited and watched for Arthur's return that whole night, and was positive that he had not passed through their grounds again after that first time in the early evening.
10083{_}6327{_}This was just what I had expected from her.
10083{_}6328{_}But the prosecution remembered the snowfall, and in her cross-examination on this point, she acknowledged that it was very thick, much too thick for her to see her own gate distinctly; but added, that this only made her surer of the fact she had stated; for finding that she could not see, she had dressed herself for the storm and gone out into the driveway to watch there, and had so watched until the town clock struck three.
10083{_}6329{_}This did not help the prosecution.
10083{_}6330{_}Sympathy could not fail to be with this young and tremulous girl, heroic in her love, if weak in other respects, and when on her departure from the stand, she cast one deprecatory glance at the man for whom she had thus sacrificed her pride, and, meeting his eye fixed upon her with anything but ingratitude, flushed and faltered till she with difficulty found her way, the sentiments of the onlookers became so apparent that the judge's gavel was called into requisition before order could be restored and the next witness summoned to testify.
10083{_}6331{_}This witness was no less a person than Arthur himself.
10083{_}6332{_}Recalled by his counsel, he was reminded of his former statement that he had left the club-house in a hurry because he heard his sister Adelaide's voice, and was now asked if hers was the only voice he had heard.
10083{_}6333{_}His answer revealed much of his mind.
10083{_}6334{_}"No, I heard Carmel's answering her."
10083{_}6335{_}This satisfying Mr. Moffat, he was passed over to Mr. Fox, and a short cross-examination ensued on this point.
10083{_}6336{_}"You heard both your sisters speaking?"
10083{_}6337{_}"Yes, sir."
10083{_}6338{_}"Any of their words, or only their voices?"
10083{_}6339{_}"I heard one word."
10083{_}6340{_}"What word?"
10083{_}6341{_}"The word, 'Elwood.'"
10083{_}6342{_}"In which voice?"
10083{_}6343{_}"In that of my sister Adelaide."
10083{_}6344{_}"And you fled?"
10083{_}6345{_}"Immediately."
10083{_}6346{_}"Leaving your two sisters alone in this cold and out-of-the-way house?"
10083{_}6347{_}"I did not think they were alone."
10083{_}6348{_}"Who did you think was with them?"
10083{_}6349{_}"I have already mentioned the name."
10083{_}6350{_}"Yet you left them?"
10083{_}6351{_}"Yes, I've already explained that.
10083{_}6352{_}I was engaged in a mean act.
10083{_}6353{_}I was ashamed to be caught at it by Adelaide.
10083{_}6354{_}I preferred flight.
10083{_}6355{_}I had no premonition of tragedy--any such tragedy as afterwards occurred.
10083{_}6356{_}I understood neither of my sisters and my thoughts were only for myself."
10083{_}6357{_}"Didn't you so much as try to account for their both being there?"
10083{_}6358{_}"Not then."
10083{_}6359{_}"Had you expected Adelaide to accompany your younger sister when you harnessed the horse for her?"
10083{_}6360{_}"No, sir."
10083{_}6361{_}"Had not this younger sister even enjoined secrecy upon you in asking you to harness the horse?"
10083{_}6362{_}"Yes, sir."
10083{_}6363{_}"Yet you heard the two together in this remote building without surprise?"
10083{_}6364{_}"No, I must have felt surprise, but I didn't stop to analyse my feelings.
10083{_}6365{_}Afterward, I turned it over in my mind and tried to make something out of the whole thing.
10083{_}6366{_}But that was when I was far out on the links."
10083{_}6367{_}A losing game thus far.
10083{_}6368{_}This the district attorney seemed to feel; but he was not an ungenerous man though cursed (perhaps, I should say blessed, considering the position he held) by a tenacity which never let him lose his hold until the jury gave their verdict.
10083{_}6369{_}"You have a right to explain yourself fully," said he, after a momentary struggle in which his generosity triumphed over his pride.
10083{_}6370{_}"When you did think of your sisters, what explanation did you give yourself of the facts we have just been considering?"
10083{_}6371{_}"I could not imagine the truth, so I just satisfied myself that Adelaide had discovered Carmel's intentions to ride into town and had insisted on accompanying her.
10083{_}6372{_}They were having it out, I thought, in the presence of the man who had made all this trouble between them."
10083{_}6373{_}"And you left them to the task?"
10083{_}6374{_}"Yes, sir, but not without a struggle.
10083{_}6375{_}I was minded several times to return.
10083{_}6376{_}This I have testified to before."
10083{_}6377{_}"Did this struggle consume forty minutes?"
10083{_}6378{_}"It must have and more, if I entered the hold in Cuthbert Road at the hour they state."
10083{_}6379{_}Mr. Fox gave up the game, and I looked to be the next person called.
10083{_}6380{_}But it was not a part of Mr. Moffat's plan to weaken the effect of Carmel's testimony by offering any weak corroboration of facts which nobody showed the least inclination to dispute.
10083{_}6381{_}Satisfied with having given the jury an opportunity to contrast his client's present cheerfulness and manly aspect with the sullenness he had maintained while in doubt of Carmel's real connection with this crime, Mr. Moffat rested his case.
10083{_}6382{_}There was no testimony offered in rebuttal and the court took a recess.
10083{_}6383{_}When it reassembled I cast another anxious glance around.
10083{_}6384{_}Still no Carmel, nor any signs of Sweetwater.
10083{_}6385{_}I could understand her absence, but not his, and it was in a confusion of feeling which was fast getting the upper hand of me, that I turned my attention to Mr. Moffat and the plea he was about to make for his youthful client.
10083{_}6386{_}I do not wish to obtrude myself too much into this trial of another man for the murder of my betrothed.
10083{_}6387{_}But when, after a wait during which the prisoner had a chance to show his mettle under the concentrated gaze of an expectant crowd, the senior counsel for the defence slowly rose, and, lifting his ungainly length till his shoulders lost their stoop and his whole presence acquired a dignity which had been entirely absent from it up to this decisive moment, I felt a sudden slow and creeping chill seize and shake me, as I have heard people say they experienced when uttering the common expression, "Some one is walking over my grave."
10083{_}6388{_}It was not that he glanced my way, for this he did not do; yet I received a subtle message from him, by some telepathic means I could neither understand nor respond to--a message of warning, or, possibly of simple preparation for what his coming speech might convey.
10083{_}6389{_}It laid my spirits low for a moment; then they rose as those of a better man might rise at the scent of danger.
10083{_}6390{_}If he could warn, he could also withhold.
10083{_}6391{_}I would trust him, or I would, at least, trust my fate.
10083{_}6392{_}And so, good-bye to self.
10083{_}6393{_}Arthur's life and Carmel's future peace were trembling in the balance.
10083{_}6394{_}Surely these were worth the full attention of the man who loved the woman, who pitied the man.
10083{_}6395{_}At the next moment I heard these words, delivered in the slow and but slightly raised tones with which Mr. Moffat invariably began his address:  "May it please the court and gentlemen of the jury, my learned friend of the prosecution has shown great discretion in that, so far as appears from the trend of his examinations, he is planning no attempt to explain the many silences and the often forbidding attitude of my young client by any theory save the obvious one--the natural desire of a brother to hide his only remaining sister's connection with a tragedy of whose details he was ignorant, and concerning which he had formed a theory derogatory to her position as a young and well-bred woman.
10083{_}6396{_}"I am, therefore, spared the task of pressing upon your consideration these very natural and, I may add, laudable grounds for my client's many hesitations and suppressions--which, under other circumstances, would militate so deeply against him in the eyes of an upright and impartial jury.
10083{_}6397{_}Any man with a heart in his breast, and a sense of honour in his soul, can understand why this man--whatever his record, and however impervious he may have seemed in the days of his prosperity and the wilfulness of his youth--should recoil from revelations which would attack the honour, if not the life, of a young and beautiful sister, sole remnant of a family eminent in station, and in all those moral and civic attributes which make for the honour of a town and lend distinction to its history.
10083{_}6398{_}"Fear for a loved one, even in one whom you will probably hear described as a dissipated man, of selfish tendencies and hitherto unbrotherly qualities, is a great miracle-worker.
10083{_}6399{_}No sacrifice seems impossible which serves as a guard for one so situated and so threatened.
10083{_}6400{_}"Let us review his history.
10083{_}6401{_}Let us disentangle, if we can, our knowledge of what occurred in the clubhouse, from his knowledge of it at the time he showed these unexpected traits of self-control and brotherly anxiety, which you will yet hear so severely scored by my able opponent.
10083{_}6402{_}His was a nature in which honourable instincts had forever battled with the secret predilections of youth for independence and free living.
10083{_}6403{_}He rebelled at all monition; but this did not make him altogether insensible to the secret ties of kinship, or the claims upon his protection of two highly gifted sisters.
10083{_}6404{_}Consciously or unconsciously, he kept watch upon the two; and when he saw that an extraneous influence was undermining their mutual confidence, he rebelled in his heart, whatever restraint he may have put upon his tongue and actions.
10083{_}6405{_}Then came an evening, when, with heart already rasped by a personal humiliation, he saw a letter passed.
10083{_}6406{_}You have heard the letter and listened to its answer; but he knew nothing beyond the fact--a fact which soon received a terrible significance from the events which so speedily followed."
10083{_}6407{_}Here Mr. Moffat recapitulated those events, but always from the standpoint of the defendant--a standpoint which necessarily brought before the jury the many excellent reasons which his client had for supposing this crime to have resulted solely from the conflicting interests represented by that furtively passed note, and the visit of two girls instead of one to The Whispering Pines.
10083{_}6408{_}It was very convincing, especially his picture of Arthur's impulsive flight from the club-house at the first sound of his sisters' voices.
10083{_}6409{_}"The learned counsel for the people may call this unnatural," he cried.
10083{_}6410{_}"He may say that no brother would leave the place under such circumstances, whether sober or not sober, alive to duty or dead to it--that curiosity would hold him there, if nothing else.
10083{_}6411{_}But he forgets, if thus he thinks and thus would have you think, that the man who now confronts you from the bar is separated by an immense experience from the boy he was at that hour of surprise and selfish preoccupation.
10083{_}6412{_}"You who have heard the defendant tell how he could not remember if he carried up one or two bottles from the kitchen, can imagine the blank condition of this untutored mind at the moment when those voices fell upon his ear, calling him to responsibilities he had never before shouldered, and which he saw no way of shouldering now.
10083{_}6413{_}In that first instant of inconsiderate escape, he was alarmed for himself,--afraid of the discovery of the sneaking act of which he had just been guilty--not fearful for his sisters.
10083{_}6414{_}_You_ would have done differently; but you are all men disciplined to forget yourselves and think first of others, taught, in the school of life to face responsibility rather than shirk it.
10083{_}6415{_}But discipline had not yet reached this unhappy boy--the slave, so far, of his unfortunate habits.
10083{_}6416{_}It began its work later; yet not much later.
10083{_}6417{_}Before he had half crossed the golf-links, the sense of what he had done stopped him in middle course, and, reckless of the oncoming storm, he turned his back upon the place he was making for, only to switch around again, as craving got the better of his curiosity, or of that deeper feeling to which my experienced opponent will, no doubt, touchingly allude when he comes to survey this situation with you.
10083{_}6418{_}"The storm, continuing, obliterated his steps as fast as the ever whitening spaces beneath received them; but if it had stopped then and there, leaving those wandering imprints to tell their story, what a tale we might have read of the first secret conflict in this awakening soul!
10083{_}6419{_}I leave you to imagine this history, and pass to the bitter hour when, racked by a night of dissipation, he was aroused, indeed, to the magnitude of his fault and the awful consequences of his self-indulgence, by the news of his elder sister's violent death and the hardly less pitiful condition of the younger.
10083{_}6420{_}"The younger!"
10083{_}6421{_}The pause he here made was more eloquent than any words.
10083{_}6422{_}"Is it for me to laud her virtues, or to seek to impress upon you in this connection, the overwhelming nature of the events which in reality had laid her mind and body low?
10083{_}6423{_}You have seen her; you have heard her; and the memory of the tale she has here told will never leave you, or lose its hold upon your sympathies or your admiration.
10083{_}6424{_}If everything else connected with this case is forgotten, the recollection of that will remain.
10083{_}6425{_}You, and I, and all who wait upon your verdict, will in due time pass from among the living, and leave small print behind us on the sands of time.
10083{_}6426{_}But her act will not die, and to it I now offer the homage of silence, since that would best please her heroic soul, which broke the bonds of womanly reserve only to save from an unmerited charge a falsely arraigned brother."
10083{_}6427{_}The restraint and yet the fire with which Mr. Moffat uttered these simple words, lifted all hearts and surcharged the atmosphere with an emotion rarely awakened in a court of law.
10083{_}6428{_}Not in my pulses alone was started the electric current of renewed life.
10083{_}6429{_}The jury, to a man, glowed with enthusiasm, and from the audience rose one long and suppressed sigh of answering feeling, which was all the tribute he needed for his eloquence--or Carmel for her uncalculating, self-sacrificing deed.
10083{_}6430{_}I could have called upon the mountains to cover _me_; but--God be praised--no one thought of me in that hour.
10083{_}6431{_}Every throb, every thought was for her.
10083{_}6432{_}At the proper moment of subsiding feeling, Mr. Moffat again raised his voice:  "Gentlemen of the jury, you have seen point after point of the prosecution's case demolished before your eyes by testimony which no one has had the temerity to attempt to controvert.
10083{_}6433{_}What is left?
10083{_}6434{_}Mr. Fox will tell you--three strong and unassailable facts.
10083{_}6435{_}The ring found in the murdered woman's casket, the remnants of the tell-tale bottle discovered in the Cumberland stable, and the opportunity for crime given by the acknowledged presence of the defendant on or near the scene of death.
10083{_}6436{_}He will harp on these facts; he will make much of them; and he will be justified in doing so, for they are the only links remaining of the strong chain forged so carefully against my client.
10083{_}6437{_}"But are these points so vital as they seem?
10083{_}6438{_}Let us consider them, and see.
10083{_}6439{_}My client has denied that he dropped anything into his sister's casket, much less the ring missing from that sister's finger.
10083{_}6440{_}Dare you, then, convict on this point when, according to count, ten other persons were seen to drop flowers into this very place--any one of which might have carried this object with it?
10083{_}6441{_}"And the bit of broken bottle found in or near the defendant's own stable!
10083{_}6442{_}Is he to be convicted on the similarity it offers to the one known to have come from the club-house wine-vault, while a reasonable doubt remains of his having been the hand which carried it there?
10083{_}6443{_}No!
10083{_}6444{_}Where there is a reasonable doubt, no high-minded jury will convict; and I claim that my client has made it plain that there is such a reasonable doubt."
10083{_}6445{_}All this and more did Mr. Moffat dilate upon.
10083{_}6446{_}But I could no longer fix my mind on details, and much of this portion of his address escaped me.
10083{_}6447{_}But I do remember the startling picture with which he closed.
10083{_}6448{_}His argument so far, had been based on the assumption of Arthur's ignorance of Carmers purpose in visiting the club-house, or of Adelaide's attempt at suicide.
10083{_}6449{_}His client had left the building when he said he did, and knew no more of what happened there afterward than circumstances showed, or his own imagination conceived.
